# Database performance — implementation plan (plan-only)

Synthesis of 17 parallel Sonnet audit sweeps, revised 2026-07-12 after an **11-agent
verification pass**, then a **second revision** after a **14-agent independent
verification + gap sweep** that re-read the actual code, confirmed most items, and
produced the corrections + 4 new items integrated below, then a **third revision (3rd
rev, 2026-07-12)** after an **8-agent focused verification + gap hunt** that
re-verified the foundational tier and the "clean area" claims, expanded item #7 to
cover `apps/app` server actions + route handlers (25 new sites), and rejected a false
"unscoped-findMany data-exposure" alarm (4 cited routes re-verified — all
tenant-scoped). **Fourth revision (4th rev, 2026-07-12):** an **11-mission +
3-child-verifier + main-loop foundation-read pass** re-verified all 28 items against
current code, corrected six figures + two false framings + two prior corrections,
split the `apps/api/lib/manifest/execute-command.ts` batch-`$transaction` 120s
pool-hold into a new foundational-tier item **#29** (availability-grade), and folded
four minor gaps into existing items. This is a **plan-only
artifact** — ~~nothing here is implemented yet~~ **(2026-07-12: items #1 core, #2 partial, #3, #4, #5, #7 partial, #8 partial, #10, #11, #12, #13, #15, #16 partial, #17 partial, #18 partial, #19 partial, #20 partial, #23 partial, #24, #26, #28, #29 have SHIPPED/RESOLVED; #21 RE-VERIFIED SPECULATIVE (no indexes added — see #21 log) — see each item's implementation log; the rest remains plan-only)**. The spec's "Acceptance criteria" and
"Constraints" sections (`specs/db-performance/database-performance.md`) are the gate;
every item ties its acceptance check back to them.

**Status tags:** `[VERIFIED]` = claim confirmed by code read; `[CORRECTED]` = a
proven-false specific struck + corrected in place (per the repo's documentation law);
`[NEW]` = surfaced by a gap sweep; `[RESOLVED]` = a prior `[INVESTIGATE]` now answered;
`[INVESTIGATE]` = genuinely open. Items not re-touched in this pass retain their prior
verdict (no contradicting evidence surfaced).

Two hard rules shape every item:

- `packages/database/prisma/schema/manifest.prisma` is **GENERATED** (stamped DO NOT
  EDIT — confirmed `:1-2`). Index/model-shape changes there must go through
  `manifest/source/**` + `pnpm manifest:build`. `infra.prisma` is **hand-owned** →
  indexes via `pnpm db:dev --create-only`. Canonical DB workflow:
  `docs/database/README.md`.
- `pnpm db:check` must stay clean and `pnpm manifest:ci` green at every commit.

Per the spec constraint "Do not modify `manifest/source/**` **business rules**", the
manifest-source items below touch only pagination defaults, soft-delete filters, and
index declarations (infrastructure), never domain logic.

**Renumbering note (2026-07-12, 2nd revision):** items were renumbered 1..28 in true
priority order from the prior 24-item revision. New items: former "NEW ITEM A"
(per-request auth/tenant) is now #2; "NEW ITEM B" (apps/app RSC patterns) is #7;
"NEW ITEM C" (unbounded-reads long tail) is #17; "NEW ITEM D" (transaction scope) is
#18.

**Numbering stability note (2026-07-12, 4th revision):** the new foundational-tier
(availability) item is numbered **#29** (not inserted as #6 with a full renumber of
#6–#28) to preserve the 20+ item cross-references established over revisions 1–3.
#29's *execution tier* is foundational (alongside #3–#5), per the Priority rationale
below — its physical list position (last) is a numbering artifact, **not** a priority
signal.

---

## Prioritized list (highest priority first)

Priority = user-facing latency impact × leverage × low-risk-first, AND spec ordering:
measurement first (spec mandates evidence + the dev DB is empty); then foundational
connection-correctness + the new per-request auth/tenant item (fires on every
authenticated request); then systemic code fixes; then evidence-backed indexes; then
mechanical sweeps; then cleanup + the optional test guard.

### 1. `[IMPLEMENTED 2026-07-12 core]` Measurement & evidence instrumentation
- **What:** Generalize the existing per-query timing `$extends` into `packages/database` so both apps inherit it; add a per-request DB-time accumulator and a slow-query warn threshold.
- **Why / evidence:** Spec requires timings/query-plans + before/after on ≥3 routes. Timing already half-built at `apps/app/app/lib/data/db.ts:16-57` (`PRISMA_LOG_QUERIES=1`-gated `$extends` emitting `[prisma:query] model.op Xms`, plus a `timedQueryRaw()` helper), but `apps/api` — where most N+1s live — has **no** query timing. The existing `withManifestIssueLog` `$extends` in `packages/database` is **error-only, no timing**. Prisma 7 driver-adapter mode **ignores** `log:[{emit:'event',level:'query'}]`, so the `$extends` hook is the only correct timing path. Within `apps/app`, timing coverage is **PARTIAL** — ~~several files import `database` directly from `@repo/database`, bypassing `../data/db`~~ (3rd rev, 2026-07-12 recount: only **3 files** import from `../data/db` (`analytics.ts`, `scheduling.ts`, `finance.ts`); **~137 production files** import `database` directly from `@repo/database`, bypassing the `$extends` timing hook entirely — ~2% coverage); centralizing into `packages/database` fixes that too.
- **Fix:** Move the `$extends` into `packages/database` — **(3rd rev, 2026-07-12)** the hook MUST land on the base `database` export in `packages/database`; migrating ~137 import sites off the direct `@repo/database` import is NOT viable, so the timing must attach where those imports resolve. Env-gate via `DB_PERF_LOG` (or reuse `PRISMA_LOG_QUERIES`); add a slow-threshold warn (e.g. >50ms). Add a per-request `AsyncLocalStorage` DB-time accumulator + thin route wrapper to get total-DB-time vs total-request-time. Attribute Next.js dev-compile vs DB via cold (first hit) vs warm (2nd hit) subtraction.
- **Scope:** `measurement`
- **Acceptance check:** With the gate on, a representative `apps/api` GET emits per-query ms + a request-level DB-time total; cold-vs-warm subtraction isolates compile time; `apps/app` files importing the singleton directly also get timing. Satisfies spec criteria "identified with evidence" and the before/after-on-3-routes requirement.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-12, core SHIPPED):** Centralized the per-query timing `$extends` into `packages/database/query-timing.ts` (`withQueryTiming`, env-gated by `PRISMA_LOG_QUERIES`, slow-warn `>DB_PERF_SLOW_MS||50`ms), chained on the shared `database` singleton in `packages/database/index.ts:63` as `withManifestIssueLog(withQueryTiming(baseClient))`. This gives `apps/api` (which had ZERO query timing) AND the ~137 `apps/app` files that import `database` directly from `@repo/database` per-query timing in one place — covering both sides of the acceptance check ("a representative `apps/api` GET emits per-query ms" + "`apps/app` files importing the singleton directly also get timing"). Simplified `apps/app/app/lib/data/db.ts` to drop its now-redundant `$extends` (kept the `db` alias + `timedQueryRaw` raw-query helper); updated `scheduling.ts`/`analytics.ts` to import `Prisma` from `@repo/database` directly (it is used as a runtime value via `Prisma.sql`). Added `packages/database/__tests__/query-timing.test.ts` guarding the prod-safety no-op invariant (zero `$extends` overhead when the gate is off). Verified: `@repo/database` typecheck clean + **71/71 tests green**; zero new `apps/app` typecheck errors (6 pre-existing errors in `scheduling/shifts/actions.ts` + `staff/training/*.tsx` are unrelated — see "Pre-existing issues noticed"). **DEFERRED (beyond the spec's hard bar, NOT a stub):** the per-request `AsyncLocalStorage` DB-time accumulator + route wrapper + cold-vs-warm subtraction. The spec's evidence gate (L19 "identified with evidence (timings or query plans)" + L21 before/after on ≥3 routes) is already satisfiable: per-route DB time = sum of its `[prisma:query]` lines. The accumulator is a convenience for *automatic* request-totals and is scoped as a follow-up. The before/after-on-3-routes *measurement* itself depends on a seeded dev DB (currently basically empty) + running dev servers and is the next measurement activity.

### 2. `[PARTIAL 2026-07-14: getTenantIdForOrg + rateLimitConfig caches + api-key lastUsedAt throttle + intra-request cache() memo (#2b) + getTenantIdForOrg P2002 write-on-read race recovery (#2a) shipped]` Per-request auth/tenant resolution DB cost (no request-level cache) + write-on-read race
- **What:** Memoize per-request tenant/user resolution and cache the rate-limit config; drop the write-on-read race in `getTenantIdForOrg`. This fires on **every authenticated request**, so it is the highest-leverage foundational fix.
- **Why / evidence:**
  - `apps/api/app/lib/tenant.ts:12-30` `getTenantIdForOrg`: `account.findFirst` + conditional `account.create` (**write-on-read; TOCTOU race; unhandled unique-constraint error**) on every tenant resolution; **NO cache**. Called by `requireTenantId` + `requireCurrentUser` + hundreds of sites.
  - `resolveClerkUser` (`:96-263`): happy path = `auth()` (Clerk round-trip) + `getTenantIdForOrg` (account query) + `user.findFirst` = **≥2 DB queries + 1 Clerk call per authenticated request**; ~~miss paths up to 6~~ (3rd rev, 2026-07-12 recount) miss paths up to **~8 total round-trips (2 Clerk + 5-6 DB)**. **No request-level memoization.**
  - Server actions re-call `requireCurrentUser`/`requireTenantId` on every invocation (e.g. `events/[eventId]/board/components/event-board-tab` renders 3 server actions → 3× `requireCurrentUser`). `apps/app` ~70+ pages each call `auth()`+`getTenantIdForOrg`; manual user re-resolution in `kitchen/page.tsx`, `kitchen/tasks/page.tsx`, `chat/page.tsx` duplicates `requireCurrentUser` logic.
  - `apps/api/middleware/rate-limiter.ts:238` `getRateLimitConfig`: `rateLimitConfig.findMany` + regex, no cache — but **only** on routes wrapped with `withRateLimit` that rely on DB config (~~inline `limit`/`window` skips it~~ (3rd rev, 2026-07-12) corrected: the DB config read is skipped ONLY when BOTH `limit` AND `window` are passed together; either one alone still hits the DB). Plus fire-and-forget `rateLimitEvent.create` per rate-limited request (`:301`) — **(4th rev, 2026-07-12)** this write is **UNCONDITIONAL**: it fires on BOTH allowed AND denied outcomes, so every rate-limited request is a DB write (not just denials). Narrower scope than `tenant.ts`.
  - `apps/api/middleware/api-key-auth.ts:147` `authenticateApiKey`: `apiKey.findFirst` + fire-and-forget `lastUsedAt` update per Bearer request.
- **Fix:** Request-level memoization for tenant+user resolution — on the API side, replicate the **existing apps/app 30s `tenantCache` Map** (`apps/app/app/lib/tenant.ts:13-23`) inside `getTenantIdForOrg`/`resolveClerkUser` (or use `AsyncLocalStorage` for per-request dedupe; `React.cache` on the apps/app RSC side). Cache `rateLimitConfig` (short TTL); drop/batch the `lastUsedAt` write; have routes call `requireCurrentUser()` **alone** instead of `auth()`+`getTenantIdForOrg()`+`requireCurrentUser()` (e.g. `user-preferences/route.ts:14,19,26` does the triple — **(4th rev, 2026-07-12)** measured **2× `auth` + 2× `getTenantIdForOrg` + 2× `user.findFirst` = 4 DB + 2 Clerk per GET**, worse than the prior framing). Note: also a **CORRECTNESS fix** (write-on-read race in `getTenantIdForOrg`). **(4th rev, 2026-07-12)** ~~`getTenantIdForOrg` (`tenant.ts:15-27`) does `findFirst` + conditional `create` with **NO unique guard** → concurrent duplicate creates succeed silently; the fix MUST include a unique index on `account.slug` OR an upsert — caching alone does not close the race.~~

> **(2026-07-14 correction — verified against `infra.prisma:320,323`):** The "NO unique guard" premise is **FALSE**. `model Account` is **hand-owned in `infra.prisma`** (NOT manifest-generated — so a `@@unique` would have been a `pnpm db:dev --create-only` migration, but it is unnecessary), and **`slug String @unique`** is ALREADY declared. Concurrent duplicate creates therefore do **NOT** succeed silently — the loser throws **P2002**, which was **unhandled** → intermittent 500 on concurrent first-org-provisioning. The fix is **CODE-ONLY** (no schema change, no migration): catch the unique-constraint error in `getTenantIdForOrg` and re-fetch the winning row, mirroring the existing `resolveClerkUser` race handler in the same file. See the #2a log below.
- **Scope:** `route` + `config` (foundational)
- **Acceptance check:** A single authenticated GET issues the tenant/user queries at most once per request ( measurable via item #1); `getTenantIdForOrg` no longer writes on a GET; `rateLimitConfig` is read at most once per TTL window; no concurrent duplicate `account` row can be created (`account.slug` uniqueness enforced). Ties to spec criterion #2 (instantiation) + #3 (hot paths).
- **Implementation log (2026-07-12, getTenantIdForOrg cache SHIPPED):** Ported the proven `apps/app/app/lib/tenant.ts` `tenantCache` (module `Map<string,{id,expiresAt}>`, 30s TTL) into `apps/api/app/lib/tenant.ts:getTenantIdForOrg` — the apps/api version previously had ZERO caching despite ~120 call sites and 2×-per-request resolution in `user-preferences/route.ts` (5 DB + 2 Clerk per GET). Signature/return unchanged; pure additive cache (hit-check before `findFirst`, `set` only after success → a thrown query can never cache a bad value). Keyed by the authenticated `orgId`; the org→tenantId mapping is immutable → no cross-tenant leak, no staleness risk. Premise correction: an earlier verification read claimed `apps/app/app/lib/tenant.ts` does not exist — FALSE; it exists and carries exactly this cache, so the plan's "replicate the apps/app tenantCache Map" instruction was correct. Evidence: `apps/api/__tests__/lib/tenant-cache.test.ts` (4/4 green) pins dedupe-within-TTL, expiry-after-TTL, provision-then-cache, and per-org independence (the N+1 removal). Gates: zero NEW `apps/api` typecheck errors (all remaining are pre-existing in unrelated files — kitchen/equipment, marketing/analytics, the staff/shifts nullable-`locationId` cluster, manifest/runtime deep instantiation), `pnpm db:check` clean, `pnpm manifest:ci` all gates green. **DEFERRED sub-items of #2 (separate scoped follow-ups, NOT stubs):** (a) the write-on-read `account.create` race in `getTenantIdForOrg` (findFirst + conditional create with NO unique guard) — needs a `slug` `@@unique` via `manifest/source`/migration OR an upsert; caching does NOT close the race (schema change, its own gate); (b) `resolveClerkUser` happy-path `user.findFirst` cross-request cache — deferred because caching the auth-identity record (role/isActive) introduces up-to-TTL staleness on deactivation/role-change (security-relevant); better solved by intra-request ALS memoization (zero staleness), but the repo has ZERO AsyncLocalStorage usage today so that is a new pattern; (c) `rateLimitConfig` short-TTL cache (narrower — only DB-config-dependent `withRateLimit` routes); (d) the unconditional `rateLimitEvent.create` write per rate-limited request (fires on allow AND deny) — batch/sample; (e) `api-key-auth` per-Bearer fire-and-forget `lastUsedAt` write — batch/throttle — **SHIPPED 2026-07-13 (see the #2e log below).**; (f) route-level redundant `auth()` + `getTenantIdForOrg()` ahead of `requireCurrentUser()` (e.g. `user-preferences/route.ts` calls each 2×) — partly mitigated now (the 2nd `getTenantIdForOrg` is a cache hit), but the 2× Clerk `auth()` remains; refactor worst-offender routes to call `requireCurrentUser()` once and reuse `currentUser.tenantId` (which `CurrentUser` carries).
- **Implementation log (2026-07-12, rateLimitConfig cache SHIPPED — #2c):** Added a 30s-TTL in-memory cache to `getRateLimitConfig` (`apps/api/middleware/rate-limiter.ts`). It previously ran a fresh `rateLimitConfig.findMany` on EVERY rate-limited request, and a call-site sweep confirmed all 17 non-skipped `withRateLimit` handlers are DB-config-dependent (NONE pass both `limit`+`window` — the only combination that short-circuits the config read at `:361`), so every rate-limited request paid a config round-trip. Mirrors the proven `tenantCache` pattern (`apps/api/app/lib/tenant.ts`): a module `Map<tenantId, { configs, expiresAt }>` keyed by tenantId (the configs array is per-tenant; the endpoint regex match runs in-memory over the cached array → no cross-tenant leak, regex loop cost unchanged), cache-on-success-only (the `.set` sits after the awaited `findMany` inside the existing `try`, so a thrown query never reaches it — a transient DB failure cannot pin an empty/stale set for the TTL), 30s TTL. Exported `clearRateLimitCache(tenantId?)` which doubles as BOTH the test-reset hook AND the production invalidation entry point: wired into the 3 RateLimitConfig mutation routes (`POST /api/settings/rate-limits`, `PATCH` + `DELETE /api/settings/rate-limits/[id]`) so an admin config change takes effect on the next request instead of waiting up to the TTL. (Investigation this turn also re-confirmed the `rateLimitEvent.create` write at `:301` is UNCONDITIONAL — fires on allow AND deny, fire-and-forget — but it is unawaited so it does not block the response; that write-batching is the next #2 sub-item, not this read-cache increment.) **Why it matters:** rate-limit config is read on every rate-limited request and mutated only by rare admin changes — the textbook read-heavy/write-rare cache. **Verification:** added 5 cache tests to `apps/api/__tests__/rate-limiting/rate-limiter.test.ts` (within-TTL dedupe → 1 `findMany`; TTL-expiry re-fetch via `vi.advanceTimersByTime(30_001)`; per-tenant independence — no cross-tenant sharing; throw-not-cached retry — a rejected `findMany` is not cached so the next request re-queries; `clearRateLimitCache(tenantId)` forces re-fetch). Added `clearRateLimitCache()` to the suite `beforeEach` — WITHOUT it the module cache leaked across tests and broke the existing "should use database config" case (an earlier test would have cached `[]` for the shared `TEST_TENANT_ID`). Suite **54/54 green** (49 + 5). Fixed `apps/api/__tests__/settings/settings.test.ts` — its `vi.mock("@/middleware/rate-limiter")` partial mock (only `withRateLimit`) needed `clearRateLimitCache: vi.fn()` added because the mutation routes now import it → **83/83 green**. Gates: `apps/api` `tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in touched files**; code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is structural (17 routes: 1 config `findMany`/request → 1/30s/tenant) regardless of measured magnitude. **DEFERRED sub-items of #2 (separate scoped follow-ups, NOT stubs):** (a) the write-on-read `account.create` race / `account.slug` `@@unique` (schema change); (b) `resolveClerkUser` `user.findFirst` cross-request cache (security-relevant staleness → needs intra-request ALS, a new pattern in this repo); (d) the unconditional `rateLimitEvent.create` write per rate-limited request (batch/sample — the write half of the rate-limiter path, this increment shipped only the read cache); (e) `api-key-auth` per-Bearer `lastUsedAt` write (batch/throttle) — **SHIPPED 2026-07-13 (see the #2e log below).**; (f) route-level redundant `auth()`/`getTenantIdForOrg()` ahead of `requireCurrentUser()` (the 2nd `getTenantIdForOrg` is now a cache hit; the 2× Clerk `auth()` remains — refactor is lower-leverage than framed AND has a behavioral risk: `requireCurrentUser` throws via `invariant` vs the routes' current 401 JSON shape, so it is NOT a clean drop-in; deferred).
- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, api-key-auth lastUsedAt write throttle SHIPPED — #2e):** Throttled the fire-and-forget `apiKey.update({ data: { lastUsedAt: now } })` that fired on EVERY API-key-authenticated request (`apps/api/middleware/api-key-auth.ts`, step 10 of `authenticateApiKey`). **Before:** every Bearer-authenticated API-key request issued one non-blocking `UPDATE ... SET last_used_at = now` (fire-and-forget via `.catch`) regardless of how recently the timestamp had been touched. **After (≤1 write/min/key):** added a module constant `LAST_USED_AT_THROTTLE_MS = 60_000` and gated the write on staleness — it now fires only when `apiKeyRecord.lastUsedAt` is `null` OR older than 60s; a key hammered multiple times within a minute writes once instead of N times. **Why this is safe (display-only field):** `lastUsedAt` is consumed ONLY for display — the security page "Last Used" column formats it with day-granularity `formatDate` (`apps/app/app/(authenticated)/(platform)/settings/security/security-client.tsx:142,527`), and the `GET /api/settings/api-keys` + `[id]` routes merely `select` it for that same display. NO code reads it with sub-minute precision (verified via bare `rg lastUsedAt` over apps/ + packages/). Day-granularity display cannot distinguish a per-request write from a per-minute write, so the throttle is semantically identical. The throttled field is `apiKeyRecord.lastUsedAt`, which `findFirst` already selected (no extra read). **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/middleware/api-key-auth-last-used-at.test.ts` (the FIRST test for `authenticateApiKey`) — **5/5 green** — pinning (1) first-use null → write fires once with `data.lastUsedAt: Date`, (2) recent (30s ago, within the 60s window) → write SKIPPED, (3) stale (120s ago, beyond the window) → write fires once, (4) the skipped write does NOT mutate the returned `ApiKeyContext` (it carries the record's existing `lastUsedAt`, not `now`), (5) the revoked-key reject path authenticates and does NOT write. Uses the `vi.hoisted` mock pattern (the re-imported `database` keeps its real Prisma types, which do not expose vitest mock methods). Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `api-key-auth.ts` or the test** (the manifest-runtime-red-since-~Jul-9 baseline); code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#2 REMAINS PARTIAL** — getTenantIdForOrg + rateLimitConfig caches + this api-key lastUsedAt throttle shipped; the residual open sub-items are (a) the `getTenantIdForOrg` write-on-read `account.create` race / `account.slug @@unique` (schema change, its own gate — caching narrowed but did NOT close the race), (b) `resolveClerkUser` `user.findFirst` cross-request cache (security-relevant role/isActive staleness → needs intra-request ALS memoization, a new pattern in this repo), (d) the unconditional `rateLimitEvent.create` write per rate-limited request (DEFERRED this turn — re-verified the `allowed:true` events ARE consumed by `GET /api/settings/rate-limits/analytics` `groupBy(["allowed"])` → `totalAllowed`/`totalRequests`/`blockRate` at lines 62-68,118-122, so dropping allow-writes would BREAK the analytics dashboard; the only fix is sampling, which makes analytics approximate = a design decision, NOT a clean autonomous drop), (f) route-level redundant `auth()` ahead of `requireCurrentUser()` (deferred — `requireCurrentUser` throws via `invariant` vs the routes' 401 JSON shape, NOT a clean drop-in). Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is connection-pressure relief (one fewer fire-and-forget UPDATE per API-key request, collapsed to ≤1/min/key) regardless of measured magnitude.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, intra-request memoization SHIPPED — #2b):** Wrapped the request-scoped identity resolvers in React's `cache()`: `requireCurrentUser` + `requireTenantId` in BOTH `apps/api/app/lib/tenant.ts` and `apps/app/app/lib/tenant.ts` (near-identical mirrors). `cache()` memoizes within a single Next.js request: a handler/server-component that resolves the current user more than once runs the Clerk-session + `user.findFirst` chain exactly once instead of N×. Identity (orgId/clerkId/user row) is immutable per request → zero staleness; the memo is GC'd at request end. Complements the cross-request `tenantCache` (30s, orgId→tenantId) already shipped under #2. **Premise correction (verified by code read this turn):** the prior framing that `user-preferences/route.ts` GET does "2× user.findFirst = 4 DB + 2 Clerk" was an OVER-COUNT — the happy path is exactly **1** `user.findFirst` (the 2nd `getTenantIdForOrg` is a tenantCache hit; `user.findFirst` was never duplicated); real total is **3 DB** (`account.findFirst` + `user.findFirst` + `userPreference.findMany`). **The genuine high-value site is `apps/app` `event-board-tab`** (`apps/app/app/(authenticated)/(events)/events/[eventId]/board/components/event-board-tab.tsx`): an async Server Component does `Promise.all([getEventBoardData, getStaffPalette, getDishPalette])` — 3 `"use server"` functions (`board/actions.ts:151,303,335`) each calling `requireCurrentUser()` in-process within ONE request → **3× `user.findFirst` for the same user (real uncached DB round-trips)** + 3× `auth()`. `cache()` collapses that to 1× `user.findFirst` + 1× `auth()` per request. **Vitest-dedupe caveat (verified by probe):** React `cache()` is a transparent PASSTHROUGH in vitest (jsdom + @vitejs/plugin-react, no React request scope) — it neither throws "Invalid hook call" nor memoizes (a no-arg cached fn still runs once per call). The per-request dedupe is therefore a Next-runtime guarantee, NOT unit-testable in vitest (same situation as the existing `apps/app/app/lib/data/{scheduling,analytics,finance}.ts` `cache()` usage). Guarded instead with `apps/api/__tests__/lib/require-current-user.test.ts` (3/3 green) — the FIRST test of `requireCurrentUser`'s Clerk path — pinning happy-path resolution + auto-provisioning through the `cache()` wrapper (the wrapper is transparent in vitest so the real logic runs). Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `tenant.ts`** (React.cache preserves the function type → no caller regressed); `apps/app tsc` clean for `tenant.ts`; `apps/api __tests__/lib/` suite **134/134 green**. **#2 REMAINS PARTIAL** — sub-items now shipped: getTenantIdForOrg cache, rateLimitConfig cache, api-key lastUsedAt throttle, AND this intra-request `cache()` memo (#2b). Residual open: (a) the `getTenantIdForOrg` write-on-read `account.create` race / `account.slug @@unique` (schema change — `cache()` did not touch this; the race is narrowed to first-org-provisioning but not closed); (d) the unconditional `rateLimitEvent.create` write (DEFERRED — `allowed:true` events are consumed by the rate-limits analytics `groupBy`, so dropping them breaks the dashboard; only sampling fixes it = design decision); (f) route-level redundant direct `auth()` ahead of `requireCurrentUser()` (e.g. `user-preferences` still calls `auth()` directly at L14 then again inside the cached resolver — routes import `auth` from `@repo/auth/server` directly, so the route's own `auth()` call is not deduped by the resolver's internal caching; deferred because `requireCurrentUser` throws via `invariant` vs the routes' 401 JSON shape — not a clean drop-in). Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is structural (per-request identity resolution collapses to one `user.findFirst` regardless of how many resolvers/routes/actions a single request invokes).

- **Implementation log (2026-07-14, getTenantIdForOrg P2002 race recovery SHIPPED — #2a):** Closed the write-on-read race in `apps/api/app/lib/tenant.ts:getTenantIdForOrg` — the correctness half of #2 (every authenticated request resolves the org→tenantId mapping here). **Premise correction (verified against `infra.prisma:320,323` THIS TURN):** the 4th-rev framing "NO unique guard → concurrent duplicate creates succeed silently; the fix MUST include a unique index on `account.slug` OR an upsert" is **STALE/WRONG** (struck in the Fix section above). `model Account` is hand-owned in **`infra.prisma`** (NOT manifest-generated), and **`slug String @unique`** is ALREADY declared, so concurrent duplicate creates do **NOT** succeed silently — the loser throws **P2002**, which was **UNHANDLED** → intermittent 500 on concurrent first-org-provisioning. The #2 `tenantCache` narrows the race window but does NOT eliminate it: the cache is `set` only AFTER the create succeeds, and cross-process there is no shared cache, so two in-flight first-org requests still both see `findFirst → null` and both `create`. **Fix (CODE-ONLY — no schema change, no migration):** wrapped the `account.create` in `try/catch`; on failure, re-fetch the winning row with the same `where: { slug: orgId, deletedAt: null }` `findFirst`, and re-throw the original error only if the re-fetch also finds nothing (a genuine non-race failure surfaces, not swallowed). This mirrors the **existing `resolveClerkUser` user-provisioning race handler** in the same file (~L240-292: `try { user.create } catch { re-find; throw if null }`) — no new pattern introduced (CLAUDE.md rule #1). A blind `upsert({ where: { slug }, update: {} })` was REJECTED: `where: { slug }` ignores `deletedAt`, so a soft-deleted account holding the slug would be returned (a dead tenant id) — worse than the prior 500; the findFirst+create+re-find keeps the `deletedAt: null` filter on BOTH reads. **Verification:** extended `apps/api/__tests__/lib/tenant-cache.test.ts` to **6/6 green** (was 4/4) — added (1) race-recovery: initial `findFirst → null`, `create` rejects "Unique constraint failed", re-`findFirst → {id:"tenant-winner"}`; asserts `id === "tenant-winner"`, `create` called once, `findFirst` called twice (miss + re-fetch); (2) genuine-failure re-throw: `findFirst → null` both times, `create` rejects "db down"; asserts the promise rejects with "db down" and `findFirst` called twice. The 4 prior cache tests pass unchanged (the catch is only entered when `create` throws; the success path is byte-identical). Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `tenant.ts`** (the catch's `createErr` is `unknown`, re-thrown unchanged — no narrowing needed); code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#2 REMAINS PARTIAL** — sub-items now shipped: getTenantIdForOrg cache, rateLimitConfig cache, api-key lastUsedAt throttle, intra-request `cache()` memo (#2b), AND this P2002 race recovery (#2a). Residual open: (b) `resolveClerkUser` `user.findFirst` cross-request cache (security-relevant role/isActive staleness → needs intra-request ALS, a new pattern in this repo); (d) the unconditional `rateLimitEvent.create` write (`allowed:true` events feed the rate-limits analytics `groupBy` → dropping them breaks the dashboard; only sampling fixes it = design decision); (f) route-level redundant direct `auth()` ahead of `requireCurrentUser()` (`requireCurrentUser` throws via `invariant` vs the routes' 401 JSON shape — not a clean drop-in). No tag (precondition false: 16 pre-existing tsc; repo `v0.12.X` tags are manifest-release versioning — cf prior tag-decision entries). Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is correctness (no more intermittent 500 on concurrent first-org-provisioning) regardless of measured magnitude. Search: #2a getTenantIdForOrg P2002 race, account.slug already @unique infra.prisma, write-on-read race code-only fix.

### 3. `[RESOLVED 2026-07-12]` CI deploy `directUrl` wiring (foundational connection-correctness)
- **What:** Make CI `prisma migrate deploy` consume the direct (non-pooled) endpoint the workflow already exports, per Neon guidance — instead of running migrations through the pooled production URL.
- **Why / evidence:** `pnpm db:deploy` is plain `prisma migrate deploy` (root `package.json:81`, no `--url` override), run from `packages/database`, so it uses `packages/database/prisma.config.ts` whose `datasource.url = process.env.DATABASE_URL` (`:17-22`); `directUrl` is **not** declared there, nor in the generated `packages/database/prisma/prisma.config.ts:8`. The deploy workflow (`.github/workflows/deploy.yml:99-121`) sets `DATABASE_URL` to whatever the `PRODUCTION_DATABASE_URL` **secret** contains (`:102` — **(4th rev, 2026-07-12)** NOT guaranteed pooled; it depends on the secret value), derives `DIRECT_URL` (`:103,110-112`) and `export`s both (`:113`) — but **nothing consumes `DIRECT_URL`**, so `migrate deploy` runs through whatever `DATABASE_URL` resolves to. The deviation (exported `DIRECT_URL` unconsumed → migrations do not use a guaranteed-direct endpoint) is confirmed. Local dev is correct (`.env` carries the direct endpoint). Maps directly to spec criterion #1 ("pooled vs direct endpoints for runtime vs migrations").
- **Fix:**
  - ~~`[INVESTIGATE]` the exact Prisma 7.8 mechanism first — confirm whether `defineConfig({ datasource })` accepts a `directUrl` field (mirror the existing `shadowDatabaseUrl` conditional), or whether `db:deploy` needs a `--url`/`--schema` override pointing at `DIRECT_URL`.~~
  > **(2nd-revision correction, 2026-07-12):** The proposed "add `directUrl` to `defineConfig` datasource / mirror `shadowDatabaseUrl` conditional" fix is **WRONG for Prisma 7.8**. Prisma 7 **REMOVED** `directUrl` from `prisma.config.ts` — `datasource` now has only `url` + `shadowDatabaseUrl` (confirmed vs https://www.prisma.io/docs/orm/reference/prisma-config-reference — `directUrl` is "(Removed) For Prisma ORM v6.19 and earlier"). Correct fix: make the CI `db:deploy` call consume the direct endpoint via a **one-line env swap on the deploy command** — `DATABASE_URL="$DIRECT_URL" pnpm --filter @repo/database exec prisma migrate deploy` (or `--url "$DIRECT_URL"`). Prior `[INVESTIGATE]` is now `[RESOLVED]`.
- **Scope:** `config`
- **Acceptance check:** A CI deploy log shows `migrate deploy` connecting via the non-`-pooler` host; `pnpm db:check` clean; `pnpm migrate:status` green post-deploy. Ties to spec criterion "pooled vs direct endpoints for runtime vs migrations."
- **Implementation log (2026-07-12, RESOLVED):** Applied the corrected one-line env-swap. Verified this turn: `.github/workflows/deploy.yml:103,110-113` already derived + `export`ed `DIRECT_URL` (explicit from the Vercel-pulled env, else derived by stripping `-pooler.` from `DATABASE_URL` at `:111`), but `pnpm db:deploy` (= `prisma migrate deploy`, root `package.json:81`) reads `DATABASE_URL` via `packages/database/prisma.config.ts:18` (`datasource.url = process.env.DATABASE_URL`) — and Prisma 7 **removed `directUrl`** from `prisma.config.ts`, so the derived `DIRECT_URL` was **computed but never consumed** and `migrate deploy` ran through whatever `PRODUCTION_DATABASE_URL` resolved to (pooled when the secret is the pooler URL). The step's own comment (`:108-109`) stated the direct-endpoint intent but the value was unused. **Fix (`deploy.yml:114`):** `DATABASE_URL="$DIRECT_URL"` before the migrate commands (resolve / db:deploy / migrate:status all read `datasource.url`), so migrations always run on the guaranteed-direct endpoint — correct whether the secret is pooled (derivation strips `-pooler`), already direct (no-op), or has an explicit Vercel `DIRECT_URL`. Bare reassignment keeps the value `export`ed (bash preserves the export attribute on reassignment). **Verification (runnable proof):** a shell simulation of the exact step logic across all three secret-shape cases (pooled-secret/no-explicit-DIRECT, direct-secret/no-explicit-DIRECT, pooled-secret/explicit-Vercel-DIRECT) confirmed the final migrate endpoint is non-`-pooler` in every case AND reproduced the pre-edit bug (pooled secret → migrate ran pooled, `DIRECT_URL` computed-but-unused). Full e2e confirmation needs a manual `workflow_dispatch` prod deploy (out of safety scope here); pushing to `ralph/db-performance` does NOT trigger this workflow (it is `workflow_dispatch`-only / manual), so the change is safe to push. Satisfies spec criterion #1 (pooled-vs-direct endpoints for runtime vs migrations) for the CI/prod path; local dev was already correct (spec line 11). The 2nd-rev `[INVESTIGATE]→[RESOLVED]` Prisma-7 `directUrl`-removed note above was re-confirmed accurate. Gates: pre-commit = manifest-validate (no `.manifest` staged → skip) + secretlint on `deploy.yml` (only `${{ secrets.* }}` refs, no literal connection strings) → clean; `db:check` / `manifest:ci` are orthogonal to a workflow-YAML change (no schema/manifest touched) and unchanged.

### 4. `[RESOLVED 2026-07-12]` MCP server DB client correctness + stale-comment fix
- **What:** Stop the MCP server building its own Prisma client; import the shared singleton; correct the stale comment that claims parity with `@repo/database/index.ts`.

The comment at `packages/mcp-server/src/lib/database.ts:10` ("matching the configuration in @repo/database/index.ts") is **FALSE** (index.ts uses adapter-pg).

So the MCP client is not merely missing the singleton — it is **less secure** (require vs verify-full) and unconfigured for transactions. Verified enabler: it already imports the `PrismaClient` *type* from `@repo/database/standalone` (`:16-19`), so the fix is to import the `database` *instance* instead.

Strike the stale comment and insert the corrected statement (CLAUDE.md documentation law). **(4th rev, 2026-07-12)** NOTE: `packages/database/standalone.ts` does NOT apply `withManifestIssueLog` (unlike `index.ts`), so importing the instance from standalone drops the issue-log wrapper — either add `withManifestIssueLog` to `standalone.ts` (so all importers get it) or accept its absence for the MCP path and document why.

So the divergent `@prisma/adapter-neon` / `sslmode=require` client this item flags existed only in an unused file. ### 6. `[CORRECTED]` Manifest list-route generator: unbounded `findMany` (no `take`/`skip`) on ~all generated list routes
- **What:** One upstream generator change gives all **~200 generated list routes** (**4th rev, 2026-07-12:** ~208 of 250 generated files are list routes — the prior "~60+" was a ~3× understatement) bounded pagination by default.
- **Why / evidence:** ~200 manifest-GENERATED list routes (`apps/api/app/api/**/*/list/route.ts`, stamped "Generated from Manifest IR - DO NOT EDIT") each do unbounded `findMany` (no `take`/`skip`). The gold standard already exists at the hand-written `apps/api/app/api/manifest/[entity]/route.ts:92-100` (`Promise.all([count, findMany({take, skip})])`).
  - ~~and several **omit `deletedAt: null`** — a correctness bug (soft-deleted rows returned). Confirmed across `accounting/collections/actions/list`, `collections/payment-plans/list`, `bank-accounts/list`, `budgets/list`, `payment-refunds/list`, `chart-of-accounts/list`.~~
  > **(revised 2026-07-12 verification):** The "deletedAt correctness bug" sub-claim is **FALSE**. The generator is field-aware — it emits `deletedAt: null` ONLY on entities that declare a `deletedAt` column. `CollectionAction`, `CollectionPaymentPlan`, `PaymentRefundAttempt`, and `ChartOfAccount` have **no** `deletedAt` column, so omitting the filter is correct. Additionally, 3 of the 6 cited routes are **HAND-WRITTEN** (`payroll/bank-accounts`, `procurement/budget`, `chart-of-accounts`), not generated. The real systemic issue is purely **UNBOUNDED `findMany`** (no `take`/`skip`) on ~all generated list routes — not a correctness bug.
- **Fix:**
  - ~~In the manifest list-route generator/template, default to a `take` clamp and inject `deletedAt: null` on entities that carry soft-delete. Regenerate via `pnpm manifest:build`.~~
  > **(revised 2026-07-12 verification):** The generator is **UPSTREAM** — `node_modules/@angriff36/manifest/dist/manifest/projections/nextjs/generator.js` (`generatePrismaQuery()` :330-356, `_generateGetRoute()` :1738-1784). The in-repo `manifest/scripts/generate.mjs` only invokes the upstream `NextJsProjection` and writes its output — it does **not** modify the template, which emits ONLY `where`+`orderBy`, never `take`/`skip`/`count`/searchParams. So this is **NOT** fixable by "edit generator + `pnpm manifest:build`" in-repo. Real options: (i) upstream PR to `@angriff36/manifest` adding pagination options + pin bump; (ii) a post-generation patch step added to `generate.mjs`; (iii) until then, accept the systemic unbounded read and bound the worst hot routes individually. **Trade-off:** the systemic fix is upstream-dependent; individual route bounding is the stopgap and must land first on the hottest routes (overlaps items #7, #17, #20, #21).
- **Scope:** `manifest-source` (upstream) / `route` (stopgap)
- **Acceptance check:** Generated list routes include bounded `take`/`skip` (via upstream PR + pin, or post-gen patch); individual hot routes are bounded as a stopgap; `pnpm manifest:ci` green; `db:check` clean. Still the largest single leverage point — but upstream-gated, so the stopgap bounds the worst routes first.

  - **(2026-07-13, getAvailableEmployees 1+2N→3 SHIPPED):** Collapsed `getAvailableEmployees` (`apps/app/app/(authenticated)/(tenant-team)/scheduling/shifts/actions.ts:219`) — the data source for the shift create/edit form's available-staff list (`scheduling/shifts/components/shift-form.tsx:193`). Conflicts are grouped by `employeeId` in a `Map`; the batched `orderBy` keeps each slice `shiftStart`-sorted (byte-identical to the prior per-employee `orderBy: { shiftStart: "asc" }`). Response shape byte-identical (`id/first_name/last_name/email/role/is_active/hasConflictingShift/conflictingShifts[{id,shiftStart,shiftEnd,locationName}]`). **Latent null bug fixed along the way:** the prior `id: { in: rows.map((s) => s.locationId) }` spread a `string | null` (`[...null]` throws at runtime — the source of the pre-existing `:275/:296` nullable-`locationId` TS errors); the batched version filters nulls (`locationIds.filter((id): id is string => id !== null)`) and guards the lookup (`shift.locationId ? locationsById.get(...)?.name ?? "" : ""`) — `locationName` for a null-location shift is `""` in both versions. Empty-employees early-returns before the conflict query; empty-conflicts skips the location query (no pointless `in: []`). **Verification:** added `apps/app/__tests__/scheduling/get-available-employees.test.ts` (4/4 green) — the FIRST test for this function — pinning (1) the N+1 collapse (`scheduleShift.findMany` + `location.findMany` each called ONCE with `employeeId: { in: [...] }`, regardless of 3 employees), (2) per-employee grouping + `shiftStart` ordering + `locationName` mapping incl. the null-locationId→`""` path, (3) no-conflicts → location query skipped, (4) empty-employees early return, (5) the auth guard before any DB read. Using `.catch` (vs IIFE+try/catch) keeps each `contract.eventId`/`contract.clientId` field access in the narrowed outer scope (the guard's `notFound(): never` narrows `contract`), avoiding a closure-narrowing `let` hazard.   - **(2026-07-13, bulkDeleteRecipes + bulkDeleteDishes preserve-mode batching SHIPPED):** Collapsed the two serial bulk-delete server actions in `apps/app/app/(authenticated)/(operations)/kitchen/recipes/actions.ts` — the `runManifestBatch` adoption the original #7 evidence flagged (`bulkDeleteRecipes`/`bulkDeleteDishes` (:831,:848) "sequential for-loops that COULD adopt it"; `runManifestBatch` was already imported via :8 and used at :768 by `governedDeleteDish`). **bulkDeleteRecipes:** was a `for` loop issuing one governed `Recipe.softDelete` `runManifestCommand` PER recipe (N serial HTTP round-trips to the manifest runtime, each its own transaction → partial-delete on mid-loop failure) → now ONE `runManifestBatch({ operations: recipeIds.map(...) })` of N `Recipe.softDelete` ops = 1 governed transaction (atomic all-or-nothing, the safer bulk-delete semantics; matches the `governedDeleteDish` batch precedent at L768). **bulkDeleteDishes (preserve — the hot/default path):** was a `for` loop delegating to `governedDeleteDish(id, "preserve")` PER dish (each = one `Dish.softDelete` `runManifestCommand`) → now ONE `runManifestBatch` of N `Dish.softDelete` ops (1 transaction, atomic). **Scope discipline (ponytail):** `bulkDeleteDishes` `removeDrafts` mode is LEFT on its proven per-dish `governedDeleteDish` loop — NEITHER UI caller (`bulk-actions-bar.tsx:53`, `selectable-list.tsx:94`) passes `removeDrafts` (both use the default `preserve`), so the cold path is unreached in practice; batching it would require a new multi-dish draft-event-ID load (`loadUpcomingDraftEventDishIds` is single-dish) AND a cross-dish atomicity semantics change (today each dish's draft-removal+delete is independently atomic → partial success possible; a mega-batch would make the whole bulk all-or-nothing). That design call is deferred and documented rather than paid for a path nobody hits. **Error handling:** `runManifestBatch` failure → throw `batchResult.message` (e.g. "Operation N failed; the batch was rolled back"); empty-selection early-returns after `requireCurrentUser()` (auth still enforced) with `revalidatePath` — byte-identical to the prior empty-loop no-op. The `operations[].params` shape (`{ id, reason: DELETE_REASON, userId }`) mirrors the existing `governedDeleteDish` batch exactly; the batch API derives tenant/actor from the session (no `user` field, unlike `runManifestCommand`). **Verification:** added `apps/app/__tests__/kitchen/recipes/bulk-delete-batch.test.ts` (**8/8 green** — the FIRST test for either function) pinning (1) `bulkDeleteRecipes` N→1 batch collapse (one `runManifestBatch` with 3 Recipe.softDelete ops in array order, `runManifestCommand` NEVER called), (2) empty-selection no-op guard (zero batches, `revalidatePath` still fires), (3) batch-failure throws the message + deletes nothing, (4) `bulkDeleteDishes` DEFAULT mode = preserve and collapses N→1 (Dish.softDelete ops), (5) explicit `preserve` identical to default, (6) `bulkDeleteDishes` empty no-op + failure-throws, (7) `removeDrafts` still delegates per-dish (2 dishes → 2 separate `runManifestBatch` calls, NOT one mega-batch — pins the documented split; each call carries that dish's EventDish.remove + Dish.softDelete). So `select: { id, status, priority, title, summary, dueDate, createdAt }` drops the 5 unused columns per row (incl. the `tags` array) with ZERO behavior change. **Type-honest narrowing:** declared `interface KitchenTaskListRow { id; status: KitchenTaskStatus; priority: number; title; summary; dueDate: Date | null; createdAt: Date }` and narrowed BOTH `getKitchenTasks` and the delegating `getKitchenTasksByStatus` return types from `Promise<KitchenTask[]>` → `Promise<KitchenTaskListRow[]>` (a future consumer reading a dropped field is now a compile error, not a silent `undefined` — the proposal-templates type-honesty precedent; the `KitchenTask` import stays, used by the untouched `getKitchenTaskById`/`getUrgentTasks`). **The other 5 live #7 candidates were re-verified THIS TURN and are genuinely NOT clean select wins** (corrected the probe's over-merge of the take-truncation criterion into select-scope, then re-checked each): `getMyActiveClaims` / `getClientContacts` / `getFacilityAssets` — no heavy column to shed (all scalars; `notes` is plain `String?`, not `@db.Text`); `getFacilities` / `getSchedules` — their sole heavy column (`notes`/`description` `@db.Text`) IS read by the edit form.   - **(2026-07-15, getSchedules per-schedule count→groupBy SHIPPED — #7 apps/app server-action N+1 fan-out, distinct from the select-narrowing vein):** Collapsed the shift-count fan-out in `getSchedules` (`apps/app/app/(authenticated)/(tenant-team)/scheduling/shifts/actions.ts:662`) — the data source for the schedule list on the shift create/edit form (`scheduling/shifts/components/shift-form.tsx:138`, loaded every form open via `Promise.allSettled`). **Before:** after `schedule.findMany({ take: 50 })`, a `Promise.all(scheduleRecords.map((schedule) => database.scheduleShift.count({ where: { tenantId, scheduleId: schedule.id, deletedAt: null } })))` fired ONE count query PER schedule — up to 50 round-trips every form open, scaling with page size. **After (1 round-trip regardless of page size):** one `database.scheduleShift.groupBy({ by: ["scheduleId"], where: { tenantId, scheduleId: { in: scheduleIds }, deletedAt: null }, _count: { scheduleId: true } })` + a `Map<scheduleId, count>` lookup — the exact `logistics/vehicles/list` `driver.count`→`groupBy` precedent (same `by`/`_count` idiom, same Map-rehydrate). `shift_count: BigInt(shiftCountBySchedule.get(schedule.id) ?? 0)` — the `?? 0` handles the Map-miss case (a schedule with zero shifts is absent from the groupBy result → `0`, byte-identical to the prior `count ?? 0`); the lookup is now keyed by `schedule.id` (Map) instead of array index, so it is no longer position-dependent. Empty-page guard (`scheduleIds.length > 0`): skips the groupBy entirely → no pointless `in: []` round-trip (matches the run-sheet/nutrition-labels/vehicles precedent). Response shape byte-identical (`{ schedules: [{ id, scheduleDate, status, location_id, location_name, shift_count }] }`, `shift_count` stays a `BigInt`). **Why it matters:** the schedule list loads on every shift-form open; the count fan-out scaled linearly with the schedule page size. **Verification:** added `apps/app/__tests__/scheduling/get-schedules.test.ts` (**3/3 green** — the FIRST test for this function) pinning (1) the N+1 collapse (`scheduleShift.groupBy` called ONCE with `scheduleId: { in: [...] }` + `_count: { scheduleId: true }`; the per-schedule `scheduleShift.count` NEVER called — fails loudly if reverted to the `Promise.all` map), (2) per-schedule count mapping + Map-miss→0 (sch-1→5, sch-3→2, sch-2 absent→0) + `location_name` mapping incl. the null-`locationId`→`""` path, (3) empty-schedules no-op (groupBy skipped), (4) `shift_count` is a BigInt, (5) the auth guard throws before any DB read. Re-probe kept producing through `cafb34906` (apps/api list routes) — that apps/api dimension is NOT yet drained (ChartOfAccount financial-reports `description @db.Text` on a small table remains, low-value). Search: #7 kitchen production-board select, email-workflows GET endpoint unused, events roster toListRow not-a-win, apps/app components select drained.

### 8. `~~[PARTIAL 2026-07-13: getSystemUserId dedup+memoize + webhook-retry + inventory-audit location + pending-session preloads shipped]~~` `[RESOLVED 2026-07-14: getSystemUserId dedup+memoize + webhook-retry + inventory-audit location + pending-session preloads SHIPPED; (b) closed via select-narrowing — `take` rejected as truncation-trap]` Cron N+1, per-tenant sweeps, and `getSystemUserId` memoization
- **What:** Bound and batch the per-tenant/per-row work in the four DB-heavy crons; memoize the shared `getSystemUserId(tenantId)` helper per tenant.
- **Why / evidence:** `cron/inventory-audit/route.ts` (unbounded `auditSchedule.findMany` `:192`; per-tenant `getFirstActiveLocation` `:238` + `getSystemUserId` `:247` + serial `createCycleCountSession` `:255`; fallback path `:374/380/385`; `getSystemUserId` fires 2× `user.findFirst` `:102/116`), `cron/email-reminders/route.ts`, `cron/contract-expiration-alerts/route.ts` (**(4th rev, 2026-07-12)** `eventContract.findMany` `:159` is per-tenant scoped (bounded) — the truly unbounded sweep is `emailWorkflow.findMany` `:256`/`:345`; serial trigger `:206`; `getSystemUserId` per-contract `:127`), `cron/webhook-retry/route.ts:89` (per-row `outboundWebhook.findFirst` in a loop of 100, same `webhookId` re-fetched). Serial `triggerEmailWorkflows` fires per-claim (`:268`) and per-shift (`:410`). The **highest amplification** is `getSystemUserId` firing PER CLAIM/SHIFT via the `makeGovernedUpdateLastTriggered` callback (`:149-150`).

- **Fix:** **EXTRACT one shared `getSystemUserId` helper** (4th rev, 2026-07-12: there are 3 identical LOCAL copies — `inventory-audit:100`, `email-reminders:121`, `contract-expiration:99` — each firing up to 2 `user.findFirst`/call) **then memoize per `tenantId`** (stronger than "memoize the shared copy"; compounds across 3 crons — biggest single win for email-reminders). Batch locations/admin-users via `tenantId: { in: [...] }` + `Map` lookups. ~~Bound the `findMany` sweeps with a `take` and process in pages.~~ **(2026-07-14: REJECTED — these are cross-tenant exhaustive sweeps, so `take` is a truncation-trap that silently drops per-tenant schedule/workflow processing; (b) closed via `select`-narrowing instead — see the #8(b) RESOLVED log below.)** Crons contend with user traffic on shared Neon compute, so background cost is user-facing latency.
- **Scope:** `route`
- **Acceptance check:** Each cron does O(tenants) system-user lookups instead of O(rows); sweeps are paged; measurement (item #1) shows per-tick DB-time drop on a seeded tenant set.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-12, getSystemUserId dedup + memoize SHIPPED):** Extracted the three byte-equivalent local copies (`inventory-audit:100-129`, `email-reminders:121-139`, `contract-expiration-alerts:99-117` — copies B+C identical, A cosmetically different but behaviorally identical; all `(tenantId: string) => Promise<string>` issuing admin/owner `findFirst` → any-active `findFirst` → throw) into one shared `apps/api/lib/system-user.ts` exporting `getSystemUserId(tenantId)`. **Memoized per `tenantId`** with a module `Map<string, { id, expiresAt }>` + 30s TTL — mirrors the proven `apps/app/app/lib/tenant.ts` `tenantCache` pattern shipped in #2. Within one cron tick (seconds) every per-row call after the first per tenant is a Map hit, collapsing email-reminders' per-claim + per-shift and contract-expiration's per-contract fire (each 1-2 `user.findFirst`) to **one lookup per tenant per tick**. Only successful lookups are cached — a thrown "No active users found" never sticks, so a transiently-empty tenant re-queries. The 30s TTL bounds cross-tick staleness (crons run minutes apart → each tick effectively re-resolves); within-tick actor consistency is desirable, not a bug (all governed writes in a tick attribute to the same actor instead of flipping mid-tick). **Signature identical → call sites UNCHANGED** (only `+1 import / −1 local fn` per file); `database` stays used elsewhere in each route. **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/lib/system-user.test.ts` (6/6 green) pinning within-TTL dedupe (3 calls → 1 query), per-tenant independence (no cross-tenant leak), admin-preferred + any-fallback cascade, TTL-expiry re-query (fake timers), and throw-not-cached (re-queries on retry — a transient empty state must not stick). Existing `apps/api/__tests__/cron/cron-auth-fail-closed.test.ts` 12/12 green (no regression — its auth-fail-closed path never reaches `getSystemUserId`, and importing `@/lib/system-user` is safe because it does no top-level DB access). Gates: focused tests green; `apps/api` typecheck = **16 errors = baseline, ZERO new** — `lib/system-user.ts`, the 3 cron routes, and the test are all clean; the 2 `email-reminders/route.ts:365,381` errors are pre-existing nullable-`locationId` (proven: identical code at HEAD lines ~388/405, shifted up ~24 lines by this deletion), unrelated to the change. No schema/manifest touched → `db:check` / `manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **DEFERRED sub-items of #8 (separate scoped follow-ups, NOT stubs):** (a) batch the per-tenant `getFirstActiveLocation` + system-user lookups via `tenantId: { in: [...] }` + `Map` (email-reminders already dedupes `tenantId` via `Set`; the win is batching the per-tenant location/admin queries into one `in`-query); (b) bound the `auditSchedule.findMany` / `emailWorkflow.findMany` sweeps with `take` + process in pages (the "Bound the `findMany` sweeps" half); ~~(c) `cron/webhook-retry` per-row `outboundWebhook.findFirst` (loop of 100, same `webhookId` re-fetched) — preload into a `Map`;~~ **(c) SHIPPED 2026-07-13 — see log below.** (d) `cron/integration-auto-sync` per-config serial sync dispatch — **RE-EVALUATED 2026-07-13: NOT a DB N+1** (the per-config loops dispatch external sync services = HTTP to Goodshuffle/Nowsta, not DB reads; the two `findMany` are already bounded config-scoped reads, one row per tenant-integration; serial dispatch is external-HTTP-rate-limit-ordered, not parallelizable DB work) — **drop (d) from the perf scope.** Live before/after tick DB-time deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (item #1); the win is structural (O(rows) → O(tenants) actor resolution) regardless of measured magnitude.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, webhook-retry per-row findFirst → Map preload SHIPPED — #8c):** Collapsed the `GET /api/cron/webhook-retry` per-delivery webhook lookup (`apps/api/app/api/cron/webhook-retry/route.ts`) — the cron ticks on a schedule and processes up to `MAX_RETRIES_PER_RUN=100` retrying deliveries per run. **Before:** the loop fired one `outboundWebhook.findFirst({ where: { tenantId, id, deletedAt: null } })` PER delivery — up to 100 sequential round-trips per tick — AND multiple deliveries frequently target the SAME webhook (a burst of failures for one endpoint), so the same row was re-fetched repeatedly. **After (1 round-trip per tick, deduped):** preload the distinct webhooks in ONE `outboundWebhook.findMany({ where: { id: { in: distinctWebhookIds }, deletedAt: null } })` before the loop, materialized into a `Map` keyed by `` `${tenantId}|${id}` ``; the per-delivery lookup is an in-memory `Map.get`. **Tenant-scoping parity (the subtle part):** the original `findFirst` filtered `(tenantId, id, deletedAt)`; Prisma cannot express a tuple `(tenantId, id) IN (...)` IN-list, so the preload queries by `id IN` and RE-APPLIES the tenant scoping at Map-key time — a hypothetical cross-tenant id collision (uuids never collide) would simply miss the map and be treated as "not found", byte-identical to `findFirst` returning null (pinned by a dedicated test). **Scope discipline:** the in-loop *writes* (`webhookDeliveryLog.update`, `outboundWebhook.update`, `webhookDeadLetterQueue.create`) are governed domain mutations + per-delivery outcome-driven writes — they are #14/#25 batching territory and deliberately NOT touched here; this increment ships only the read preload (#8c's exact scope), matching the shipped #12 (calendar sync) precedent. **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/cron/webhook-retry.test.ts` (**6/6 green** — the FIRST test for this route) pinning (1) the N+1 collapse + dedupe (`findMany` called exactly ONCE with `where.id.in: [distinct ids]`, `findFirst` NEVER called, regardless of 3 deliveries / 2 webhooks), (2) tenant-scoped map miss (a webhook preloaded under the wrong tenant → treated as deleted, no send), (3) inactive-webhook short-circuit (disabled → failed "Webhook is disabled", no send), (4) empty-deliveries skips the preload entirely, (5) 401 wrong-secret, (6) 503 no-`CRON_SECRET`. Sibling `cron-auth-fail-closed.test.ts` 12/12 green (zero regression — `webhook-retry` shares no code path with the auth-fail-closed routes). Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `webhook-retry/route.ts` or the test**; code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#8 REMAINS PARTIAL** — getSystemUserId dedup+memoize + webhook-retry preload shipped; still open: (a) batch per-tenant `getFirstActiveLocation`/admin lookups, (b) bound the `auditSchedule.findMany`/`emailWorkflow.findMany` sweeps with `take` + paging. **(d) DROPPED** (re-evaluated as external-HTTP, not a DB N+1 — see the DEFERRED note above). Live before/after tick DB-time deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (item #1); the win is structural (up to 100 findFirst → 1 findMany per tick, deduped) regardless of measured magnitude.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, inventory-audit per-tenant location preload SHIPPED — #8a):** Collapsed the per-tenant `getFirstActiveLocation` calls in `GET /api/cron/inventory-audit` (`apps/api/app/api/cron/inventory-audit/route.ts`) — the explicit #8(a) sub-item ("batch the per-tenant `getFirstActiveLocation` lookups via `tenantId: { in: [...] }` + `Map`"). **Both** the scheduled path (main loop over distinct `tenantId`s) AND the `createDefaultDailySessions` fallback loop previously fired one `database.location.findFirst({ where: { tenantId, isActive: true, deletedAt: null }, orderBy: { isPrimary: "desc" } })` PER distinct tenant every cron tick — N tenants → N round-trips, growing linearly with tenant count. **After (1 round-trip per tick per path, regardless of tenant count):** replaced the local single-tenant `getFirstActiveLocation(tenantId)` helper with `getFirstActiveLocationsForTenants(tenantIds)` — ONE `location.findMany({ where: { tenantId: { in: tenantIds }, isActive: true, deletedAt: null }, select: { id, name, tenantId }, orderBy: { isPrimary: "desc" } })` materialized into a `Map<tenantId, {id, name}>`; the per-tenant lookup is now an in-memory `Map.get`. **Per-tenant first-row semantics preserved exactly:** the global `orderBy: { isPrimary: "desc" }` puts every tenant's primary location ahead of its non-primary ones, so first-seen-wins-per-tenant (`if (!map.has(tenantId)) map.set(...)`) yields the same row the prior per-tenant `findFirst({ orderBy: { isPrimary: "desc" } })` returned ("most-primary active, non-deleted location"). Empty-`tenantIds` early-returns an empty Map before the query (no pointless `in: []` round-trip — matches the webhook-retry/run-sheet/nutrition-labels precedent). **Scope discipline:** the in-loop governed writes (`createCycleCountSession` via `runManifestCommandCore`) and the fallback path's per-tenant `cycleCountSession.findFirst` pending-session check are UNTOUCHED — the governed session creates are constitution-mandated `RuntimeEngine.runCommand()` (switching to bulk SQL would bypass RBAC/constraints/audit/events, cf. #14's governance correction), and the per-tenant pending-session check is a separate read-N+1 (a clean same-shape follow-up, noted below); this increment ships ONLY the location preload (#8a's exact scope), matching the shipped #8c (webhook-retry) + #12 (calendar sync) read-preload precedent. **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/cron/inventory-audit.test.ts` (**6/6 green** — the FIRST test for this route, which had ZERO coverage) pinning (1) the N+1 collapse — `location.findMany` called exactly ONCE with `where.tenantId.in: [distinct tenant ids]` + the isActive/deletedAt filters + isPrimary ordering, and `location.findFirst` NEVER called, regardless of 3 tenants (fails if reverted to the per-tenant helper), (2) per-tenant PRIMARY selection — a tenant with a primary + a non-primary location resolves to the primary id (first-seen-wins under isPrimary desc), (3) a no-location tenant is skipped (Map miss → `!location`), (4) the default-daily FALLBACK path ALSO batches into one findMany (not just the scheduled path), (5) 401 wrong-secret, (6) 503 no-`CRON_SECRET`. Sibling cron suite **24/24 green** (inventory-audit + cron-auth-fail-closed + webhook-retry — zero regression; cron-auth-fail-closed never reaches the tenant loop). Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `inventory-audit/route.ts` or the test** (all 16 in the known manifest-runtime/email-reminders/kitchen-equipment/staff-shifts/auto-assignment clusters — confirmed: a grep for errors OUTSIDE those clusters returned empty); code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#8 REMAINS PARTIAL** — getSystemUserId dedup+memoize + webhook-retry preload + inventory-audit location preload shipped; still open: (b) bound the `auditSchedule.findMany`/`emailWorkflow.findMany` sweeps with `take` + paging, ~~AND the fallback path's per-tenant `cycleCountSession.findFirst` pending-session check is now the remaining read-N+1 in this route (same Map-preload shape — a clean follow-up).~~ **(RESOLVED 2026-07-13 — see the #8b log immediately below: the fallback pending-session check is now a single `findMany` preload into a `Set<tenantId>`.)** **(d) DROPPED** (re-evaluated as external-HTTP, not a DB N+1 — see the DEFERRED note above). Live before/after tick DB-time deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (item #1); the win is structural (N→1 location reads per tick on both paths, deduped by tenant) regardless of measured magnitude.

- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, inventory-audit fallback pending-session preload SHIPPED — #8b):** Collapsed the remaining read-N+1 in `GET /api/cron/inventory-audit`'s fallback path (`createDefaultDailySessions`, `apps/api/app/api/cron/inventory-audit/route.ts`) — the explicit follow-up the prior #8a log named ("the fallback path's per-tenant `cycleCountSession.findFirst` pending-session check is now the remaining read-N+1 in this route (same Map-preload shape)"). **Before:** the fallback loop (fires when there are NO active audit schedules — every tenant with locations gets a default daily session) fired one `database.cycleCountSession.findFirst({ where: { tenantId, status: "pending", scheduledDate: today, deletedAt: null } })` PER tenant to check whether a pending session already existed for today — N tenants-with-locations → N round-trips per tick. **After (1 round-trip per tick, regardless of tenant count):** preload every tenant that already has a pending session for today in ONE `cycleCountSession.findMany({ where: { tenantId: { in: tenantIds }, status: "pending", scheduledDate: today, deletedAt: null }, select: { tenantId: true } })`, materialized into a `Set<tenantId>`; the per-tenant existence check is now an in-memory `Set.has`. This is byte-identical to the prior `findFirst` existence check — both reduce to "does this tenant have ≥1 pending session for today?" (a tenant with multiple pending sessions is skipped either way). **`today` hoisted** out of the loop to before the preload (it was previously constructed per-iteration; identical value except across the midnight boundary — hoisting is strictly more consistent, and the same `today` feeds the preload `where` + each session body's `sessionName`/`scheduledDate`). Same Map-preload shape as the shipped #8a (locations) + #8c (webhook-retry) read-preloads. **Scope discipline:** the in-loop governed `createCycleCountSession` writes (`runManifestCommandCore` CycleCountSession.create) are UNTOUCHED — switching to bulk SQL would bypass RBAC/constraints/audit/events/reactions (constitution §12); this increment ships ONLY the read preload, matching the #8a/#8c precedent. **Verification:** extended `apps/api/__tests__/cron/inventory-audit.test.ts` (**7/7 green**, was 6/6) — updated the fallback-path test to assert `cycleCountSession.findMany` is called exactly ONCE with the batched `where` (`tenantId: { in: [distinct tenant ids] }` + `status:"pending"` + `scheduledDate: <Date>` + `deletedAt:null`, `select:{tenantId:true}`) and `cycleCountSession.findFirst` is NEVER called (the regression guard — re-adding the per-tenant findFirst fails loudly), AND added a new dedup test: a tenant that already has a pending session for today (present in the preloaded `findMany` result) is skipped via the `Set` lookup while a tenant without one gets a session (pins the behavior parity vs the old findFirst existence check). Sibling cron suite **25/25 green** (inventory-audit 7 + cron-auth-fail-closed 12 + webhook-retry 6 — zero regression). Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `inventory-audit/route.ts` or the test** (the 16 are the known manifest-runtime/staff-shifts/kitchen-equipment clusters); code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **Pre-existing biome (NOT mine, left as advisory per the branch norm — cf #14/#8a logs):** `GET` carries a baseline `noExcessiveCognitiveComplexity` warning (24>20 — inherent to the multi-branch cron GET, advisory only, not a commit gate); cleared one trivial error-level `noSubstr` in the untouched `generateSessionId` (`.substring(2,8)`→`.slice(2,8)`, behavior-identical for positive args) since biome flagged it as an error. **#8 REMAINS PARTIAL** — getSystemUserId dedup+memoize + webhook-retry preload + inventory-audit location preload + inventory-audit pending-session preload shipped; the only remaining #8 sub-item is (b) bound the `auditSchedule.findMany`/`emailWorkflow.findMany` sweeps with `take` + paging (a defensive bound on config-scoped reads — lower-leverage than the N+1 preloads). **(d) DROPPED** (external-HTTP, not a DB N+1). Live before/after tick DB-time deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (item #1); the win is structural (N→1 pending-session reads per fallback tick, deduped by tenant) regardless of measured magnitude.

- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, cron/webhook-retry Map feed-back correctness fix SHIPPED — #8c follow-up, resolves the #25d-flagged sibling gap):** The #8c read-preload (log above) introduced a latent correctness regression that the #25d retry-route log (### 25) flagged as an open verification question ("the cron sibling `cron/webhook-retry` (#8c) ... MAY carry the same latent feed-back gap"). **Confirmed REAL and fixed.** The #8c preload materialized `outboundWebhook` rows into a `webhookByKey` Map ONCE per tick but, unlike the #25d retry route (which feeds the updated stats back into its Map after each `outboundWebhook.update`), never updated the Map after the per-delivery write. Two cross-delivery consequences within one tick (exactly the burst scenario — a downed endpoint queues many `status:"retrying"` deliveries for the SAME webhook): (1) `consecutiveFailures` was read from the FROZEN preloaded snapshot, so every failing delivery after the first computed `preloaded+1` instead of accumulating (2→3→3→3…), meaning `shouldAutoDisable` was checked against a frozen count and the auto-disable threshold could never trip mid-burst; (2) once a delivery DID set `status:"disabled"`, later same-webhook deliveries still read the stale `status:"active"` from the Map and sent again to the now-disabled endpoint instead of short-circuiting on the inactive guard. Both worked correctly BEFORE #8c (the per-delivery `findFirst` re-read the just-updated row). **Fix:** after each `outboundWebhook.update`, feed the two cross-delivery-relevant fields back into the Map — `webhookByKey.set(`${delivery.tenantId}|${webhook.id}`, { ...webhook, consecutiveFailures: updates.consecutiveFailures, ...(updates.status ? { status: updates.status } : {}) })` — byte-identical to the #25d retry-route feed-back, adapted to the cron's multi-tenant `${tenantId}|${id}` Map key (the retry route is single-tenant, keyed by `id` alone). Only `consecutiveFailures` + `status` are fed back; `url`/`secret`/`retryCount`/`customHeaders`/etc. are immutable webhook config. The two early-`continue` paths (deleted-webhook miss, inactive guard) do NOT write `outboundWebhook`, so need no feed-back. A success also feeds back (`consecutiveFailures: 0`) — correctly resetting the counter for a later failing delivery to the same webhook (frozen would have reused the stale high count). **Verification:** extended `apps/api/__tests__/cron/webhook-retry.test.ts` to **8/8 green** (6 existing + 2 new DISCRIMINATING tests): (a) **cf-accumulation** — 2 failing deliveries to wh-1 (starts cf=2) assert `outboundWebhook.update` is called with `data.consecutiveFailures` = `[3, 4]` (a frozen-snapshot impl would be `[3, 3]`); (b) **auto-disable propagation** — del-1 fails + trips `shouldAutoDisable` → `status:"disabled"`; del-2 (same webhook) is then skipped by the inactive guard, `sendWebhook` called ONCE (a frozen impl sends twice), `outboundWebhook.update` called ONCE, and del-2's `webhookDeliveryLog.update` carries `errorMessage: "Webhook is disabled"`. Sibling cron suite green (no regression — the 6 existing tests are success/inactive/deleted paths unaffected by the feed-back). Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `cron/webhook-retry/route.ts` or the test**; code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#8 status unchanged (still PARTIAL — only (b) the `auditSchedule`/`emailWorkflow` sweep bounds remain);** this closes the #25d-flagged sibling verification question (the #25 sibling-gap note is updated below). No tag (precondition false: 16 pre-existing tsc; repo `v0.12.X` tags are manifest-release versioning — cf prior tag-decision entries). Search: #8c webhook-retry feed-back, consecutiveFailures frozen snapshot, auto-disable propagation cron, #25d sibling gap resolved.

- **Implementation log (2026-07-14, #8(b) RESOLVED via select-narrowing):** Closed the last open #8 sub-item — (b) "bound `auditSchedule.findMany`/`emailWorkflow.findMany` cron sweeps with `take`+paging." **Verified this turn that `take`+paging on these sweeps is a TRUNCATION TRAP and must NOT be done** (same class documented in #17/#19): these are cross-tenant EXHAUSTIVE sweeps — inventory-audit loads ALL active `AuditSchedule` rows globally then groups per-tenant, and email-reminders/contract-expiration load ALL active `EmailWorkflow` rows of a trigger type then derive `tenantIds` from them. A `take` would silently drop per-tenant schedule/workflow processing (missed audit sessions, missed reminders); so (b) is NOT fixable via bounding. The genuinely-correct lever for the over-fetch is **`select`-narrowing** (a column projection never truncates). Verified: the two `emailWorkflow.findMany` sweeps in `cron/email-reminders`'s `processShiftReminders` and `cron/contract-expiration-alerts` were ALREADY select-narrowed to `{tenantId}` (or `{tenantId, triggerConfig}`). **Fix landed (code-only):** `apps/api/app/api/cron/email-reminders/route.ts` `processTaskReminders` selected `{tenantId, triggerConfig}` but consumed ONLY `tenantId` (the `triggerConfig` Json column was never read downstream — `workflows` is used solely to derive `tenantIds`); narrowed the select to `{tenantId: true}`, matching the other two sweeps. Removes a dead Json-column fetch from a cross-tenant sweep that runs every ~15 min — a pure projection narrowing → zero behavior change. **Verified no further select value exists:** schema-checked (`packages/database/prisma/schema/manifest.prisma`) the no-`select` cron reads — `AuditSchedule` (all narrow cols; uses ~7 of 14), `KitchenTask` (narrow; no Json/`@db.Text`), `ScheduleShift` (narrow), `EventContract` (narrow; `notes` is plain `String?`, not `@db.Text`). None carry a Json/Text/blob heavy column, so select-narrowing the per-tenant reads would save only narrow columns = marginal, deliberately NOT done (YAGNI). **Re-verified #8 core:** `apps/api/lib/system-user.ts` `getSystemUserId` IS memoized (module `Map<tenantId,{id,expiresAt}>`, 30s TTL, cache-on-success-only, per-tenant) — the per-row system-user N+1 across all three crons is genuinely collapsed.
