### 9. `[PARTIAL 2026-07-13: waste+staff + multi-location per-location GROUP BY + events/advanced topDishes parallelization + events SELECT narrow SHIPPED; advanced "add LIMIT" = truncation-trap documented; profitability route already SQL GROUP BY]` Analytics per-location N+1 + missing `location_id` filters → `GROUP BY`
- **What:** Collapse the per-location loops that fire N raw SQL each into single `GROUP BY location_id` queries; fix the genuinely-missing `location_id` predicates; drop the dead aggregate.
- **Why / evidence:**
  - ~~`analytics/consolidated/route.ts:153-178` (inventory — no location filter), `:221-236` (`recipe.count` — no location filter), `:251-269` (waste), `:284-298` (staff), `:351-417` (`GET_LOCATIONS` — `inventoryCount` no location filter)~~
  > **(revised 2026-07-12 verification):** Only the **inventory** loop (`:153-178`) and the **`recipe.count`** loop (`:221-236`) genuinely **MISS** the `location_id` filter (correctness); `GET_LOCATIONS` `inventoryCount` (`:354-358`) also misses it. The **waste** loop (`:251-269`, filters at `:256`) and **staff** loop (`:284-298`, filters at `:288`) **BOTH already filter by `locationId`** — they are N round-trips (volume/connection-pressure), NOT correctness bugs. So missing-filter bugs = inventory (×2) + `recipe.count` + `GET_LOCATIONS`-inventoryCount only. **(5th-rev note, 2026-07-12)** The `recipe.count` "missing location_id" sub-item is DESIGN-GATED, not mechanical: the route carries an explicit code comment *"Recipe doesn't have locationId directly, this is for illustration"* — `Recipe` has no `locationId` column, so a correct fix requires a JOIN through a location-bearing relation (a schema/design decision), not a one-line predicate. Treat that one sub-item as NEEDS-DESIGN; ~~the other two missing-filter bugs (inventory loop + `GET_LOCATIONS.inventoryCount`, both on `inventoryItem` which DOES carry `location_id`) remain mechanical~~. **(6th-rev correction, 2026-07-12 — RE-VERIFIED against `manifest.prisma:2815-2860`):** that is **FALSE** — `InventoryItem` has **NO `location_id` column** (fields: id, tenantId, deletedAt, item_number, name, description, category, unitOfMeasure, unitCost, quantityOnHand, quantityReserved, parLevel, reorder_level, supplierId, tags, fsa_status, fsa_temp_logged, fsa_allergen_info, fsa_traceable, createdAt, updatedAt — NO location dimension). So the inventory loop + `GET_LOCATIONS.inventoryCount` are **NOT mechanical missing-filter bugs** — they are **architecturally impossible** without a location dimension on the model (same class as the `Recipe` sub-item): today they silently return the SAME tenant-wide number for every location (a duplicated-data correctness bug), and a real fix needs a JOIN through a location-bearing relation (e.g. `InventoryStock` if it carries location) or a schema change — a design decision, NOT a one-line predicate. Treat the inventory + `GET_LOCATIONS.inventoryCount` sub-items as NEEDS-DESIGN alongside `recipe.count`. The `waste` + `staff` per-location loops DO filter correctly (those models carry `location_id`); their GROUP BY fix remains mechanical.
  - `analytics/multi-location/route.ts:200-479` fires 11×N concurrent queries (all DO filter — cost is volume/connection-pressure, not a filter bug).
  - `analytics/events/advanced/route.ts:109-142` — unbounded 12mo events fetch, no `LIMIT`.
  - `[CORRECTED 4th rev, 2026-07-12]` the tenant-wide inventory aggregate (`analytics/consolidated/route.ts:133-143`) is **PARTIALLY LIVE** — `totalItems`/`totalValue` ARE used; only `lowStockItems:0` is dead. Drop just the dead `lowStockItems` computation, not the whole aggregate.
  - `[CORRECTED 4th rev, 2026-07-12]` **`getTenantIdForOrg` is DUPLICATED (not triplicated)** across the analytics routes — only `advanced` + `profitability` define a local copy; CSV-export IMPORTs the shared module (no local copy). (Write-on-read race ×2; see item #2.) Fold into item #2's request-level memo.
- **Fix:** Rewrite each per-location loop as one `GROUP BY location_id` raw query; add the missing `location_id` predicate on the inventory/recipe/GET_LOCATIONS paths; add a `LIMIT` to the events fetch; delete only the dead `lowStockItems` computation (the aggregate is partially live — see correction above); let item #2 dedupe the duplicated tenant resolver.
- **Scope:** `route`
- **Acceptance check:** 11×N queries collapse to ~1 per metric; results unchanged for the single-location case and now correct per-location on the 3 previously-leaking paths; dead aggregate gone; before/after on the analytics routes from item #1.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, waste + staff per-location GROUP BY SHIPPED):** Collapsed the two mechanical per-location N+1 loops in `GET /api/analytics/consolidated` (`apps/api/app/api/analytics/consolidated/route.ts`). **Before:** the waste loop (`:251-269`) fired one `wasteEntry.aggregate` PER location and the staff loop (`:284-298`) fired one `employeeLocation.count` PER location — a 10-location tenant paid 20 round-trips on every consolidated-dashboard load. **After (1 round-trip per metric, independent of location count):** each loop is a single `$queryRaw` `GROUP BY location_id`, materialized into a `Map<locationId, …>`, then the response arrays are built by `.map`-ing over the already-fetched `locations` list (preserving its `isPrimary`/`name` order) with `?? 0` zero-fill for locations absent from the group set — byte-identical output to the prior per-location aggregates. Waste query: `SELECT location_id, COUNT(*)::bigint AS entry_count, COALESCE(SUM("totalCost"),0)::text AS total_cost FROM tenant_kitchen.waste_entries WHERE tenant_id=$1 AND deleted_at IS NULL AND location_id IS NOT NULL AND created_at BETWEEN $2 AND $3 GROUP BY location_id` — `BETWEEN` is inclusive = the prior `gte`/`lte`; `"totalCost"` is the column's literal camelCase name (`manifest.prisma:6836` `totalCost Decimal? @map("totalCost")`); `location_id IS NOT NULL` drops the null-location group which never matched a real location under the prior `locationId: location.id` equality predicate anyway. Staff query: `SELECT location_id, COUNT(*)::bigint AS employee_count FROM tenant_staff.employee_locations WHERE tenant_id=$1 AND deleted_at IS NULL GROUP BY location_id` — `employee_locations.location_id` is non-nullable, so no null guard needed. Both queries are guarded by `if (locations.length > 0)` so an empty location set skips the round-trips entirely (matches the run-sheet/nutrition-labels/vehicles `in: []` precedent). Schema verified THIS TURN: `WasteEntry` → `@@map("waste_entries")` `@@schema("tenant_kitchen")`, `location_id` nullable (`manifest.prisma:6820-6854`); `EmployeeLocation` → `@@map("employee_locations")` `@@schema("tenant_staff")`, `location_id` NOT null (`infra.prisma:682-697`). **The inventory loop (`:153-178`) + recipe loop (`:221-236`) + `GET_LOCATIONS` are INTENTIONALLY UNTOUCHED** — those are the NEEDS-DESIGN sub-items (`InventoryItem`/`Recipe` carry NO `location_id`, so a per-location fix needs a JOIN through a location-bearing relation or a schema change — architectural, not a one-line predicate; the `recipe.count` loop even carries an explicit *"Recipe doesn't have locationId directly"* comment at `:226`). **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/analytics/consolidated.test.ts` (**5/5 green**) — the FIRST test for this route — pinning (1) the N+1 collapse (`wasteEntry.aggregate` + `employeeLocation.count` NEVER called; exactly ONE waste GROUP BY + ONE staff GROUP BY regardless of 3 locations), (2) per-location value mapping + zero-fill (waste row only on loc-1 → 3/150.5, others 0; staff row only on loc-2 → 5, others 0) + the `waste.total`/`totalCost`/`staffing.total` sums, (3) the empty-locations no-op (both GROUP BYs skipped), (4) 401 before any DB read, (5) 404 tenant-not-found before any DB read. Sibling analytics dir **42/42 green** (3 files, zero regression). Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `consolidated/route.ts` or the test** (the 16 are the known staff/shifts nullable-`locationId` + manifest-runtime-`ai-suggestions` clusters); code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#9 REMAINS OPEN** — the waste+staff mechanical GROUP BYs shipped; the inventory/recipe/`GET_LOCATIONS` per-location loops are NEEDS-DESIGN (no `location_id` on those models), and the `analytics/multi-location` 11×N + `analytics/events/advanced` unbounded 12mo fetch + the dead `lowStockItems` aggregate are still pending. Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is structural (N→1 round-trip per metric on the consolidated dashboard) regardless of measured magnitude.
  - **(2026-07-13, multi-location 12×N→11 GROUP BY SHIPPED):** Collapsed `GET /api/analytics/multi-location` (`apps/api/app/api/analytics/multi-location/route.ts`) — the largest remaining analytics N+1 and a #9 sub-item. **Before:** the route fetched the tenant's active locations, then ran an outer `Promise.all` over **12 metric buckets** where EACH bucket was `locations.map(async (location) => database.$queryRaw(... WHERE location_id = ${location.id}::uuid ...))` = **1 + 12×N round-trips** per dashboard load (a 10-location tenant paid 121 queries every load); one bucket (staffing) was a per-location `employeeLocation.count`. **After (1 + 11 round-trips, independent of location count):** each bucket is a single `$queryRaw` `SELECT location_id, <aggregate> ... WHERE tenant_id = $1::uuid AND deleted_at IS NULL AND location_id IN (${Prisma.join(locationIds)}) AND <date predicates> GROUP BY location_id`; the 11 group result-sets are mapped to per-location camelCase arrays matching the prior bucket return shapes, so the ENTIRE downstream pipeline (the `locationMetrics` Map, the 9 population loops, every KPI/benchmark/ranking) is byte-identical — only the fetch structure changed. The dead `_previousLaborRows` bucket (fetched but never read — no population/aggregation referenced it) was dropped (12→11). `Prisma.join` for the `IN` list follows the proven `apps/api/app/api/conflicts/detect/route.ts:446` idiom (`e.status NOT IN (${Prisma.join(...)})` — no per-element cast; Postgres resolves the param types against the uuid column). Date predicates preserved EXACTLY per metric (half-open `>= / <` for revenue/labor/waste/margin; closed `<=` for events; none for inventory/staffing) — only `location_id = ${id}::uuid` → `location_id IN (...)` + `GROUP BY location_id` changed. The empty-locations early-return (before the fetch block) guarantees `locationIds` is never empty → no empty-`IN` edge case. **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/analytics/multi-location.test.ts` (**5/5 green** — the FIRST test for this route) pinning (1) the N+1 collapse (`$queryRaw` called exactly **11** times regardless of 3 locations, `employeeLocation.count` NEVER called, every call's SQL contains `GROUP BY` + `location_id IN`), (2) per-location mapping + zero-fill (loc-1 revenue/labor/waste/events/staffing, loc-2 margin/inventory, loc-3 all-zero) + derived KPIs (total-revenue 1000, labor-utilization 80, profit-margin 25 revenue-weighted, event-completion 0.8, inventory-value 5000) + summary totals, (3) empty-locations no-op (`$queryRaw` skipped), (4) 401 before any DB read, (5) 404 tenant-not-found. The mock discriminates by table/column text in the `Prisma.sql` `.sql` string (catering_orders / budgeted_labor / avg_margin+total_revenue / waste_entries / completed_count / event_count / inventory_items / employee_locations) — the `consolidated.test.ts` table-discriminating pattern extended to multi-location's 11 metrics. Full analytics dir **55/55 green** (6 files, zero regression). - **(2026-07-13 correction — the `lowStockItems` "dead aggregate" is NOT deletable; #9 sub-item is a NO-OP as written):** Re-verified `analytics/consolidated/route.ts` this turn. `lowStockItems` is NOT dead code — it is a hardcoded `0` in the no-location branch (`:184`, `lowStockItems: 0, // Would need additional query`) while the location branch computes a real `low_stock_count` from raw SQL (`:176`). It is a no-op FIELD in the response shape, not removable code: deleting it breaks the `{ inventory: { lowStockItems } }` contract, and "fixing" it means adding a real low-stock count query (the `qty < reorder_level` column-to-column predicate Prisma `where` cannot express — the #19 inventory low-stock correctness work owns that). The #9 "drop the dead lowStockItems computation" line is therefore a NO-OP; left as-is, documented so a future loop does not re-attempt the deletion.

- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, analytics/events/advanced topDishes parallelization + events SELECT narrow SHIPPED — and the "add LIMIT" sub-item is a TRUNCATION TRAP, documented):** Reduced over-fetch + latency on `GET /api/analytics/events/advanced` (the executive advanced-analytics dashboard; loads on every open). **Two faithful changes, neither a truncation trap:**
  - **(1) Folded the independent `topDishes` read into the initial parallel batch.** The top-dishes `$queryRaw` (top-20 dishes by menu_count) is keyed ONLY on `tenantId` — it has no data dependency on the events/profitability window — yet it was `await`ed dead-last (~line 378), after ~200 lines of JS aggregation over the events set. Moved it into the opening `Promise.all([events, profitabilityData, topDishes])`; its result is consumed later (where `topMenuItems` is built, using the JS-computed `averageMargin`). The route's serial rounds drop **3 → 2** (the clients read is the only one that genuinely depends on a prior result — the events' `clientIds` — so it stays after the batch). Same [[parallelization-mock-order-pattern]] spirit; the existing test's order-independent table-keyed `mockImplementation` router needed no change.
  - **(2) Narrowed the events `SELECT`** to drop `title`, `venue_id`, `location_id` — verified unread this turn (only `id`/`event_type`/`event_date`/`guest_count`/`client_id`/`venue_name` are read; the route's own `$queryRawUnsafe<Array<{…}>>` type annotation was widened to match, so a future read of a dropped column is a compile error, not a silent `undefined`). 3 unused columns × every event in a 3/6/12-month window no longer materialized.
  - **Why the headline #9 "add a `LIMIT` to the events fetch" is a TRUNCATION TRAP (do NOT do it):** the events query result drives EVERY aggregate this route returns — `summary.totalEvents`/`totalRevenue`/`averageMargin`/`averageGuestCount`, the first-half-vs-second-half `revenueTrend`/`marginTrend` (computed by slicing the date-ordered array in JS), `profitabilityTrends` (monthly GROUP BY in JS), `eventTypeAnalysis`, `clientPreferences` (top-10), and the `predictiveInsights` forecast (`monthlyEventRate = totalEvents / months`). A `LIMIT` would silently corrupt every one of those dashboard metrics — exactly the battle-boards #7 dead-end shape. The correct fix is a SQL `GROUP BY` rewrite (cf #15 marketing analytics), but that is a large, high-risk change on user-facing analytics numbers whose correctness cannot be verified against the empty dev DB this increment (the seeded-DB measurement pass #1 is deferred) — deferred, not forced. Documented here so the next loop does not re-attempt the naive `LIMIT`.
  - **Stale-claim correction (per verify-before-asserting; source fixed here):** the multi-location #9 log above flagged "sibling profitability query ~line 124-147 also unbounded" — that refers to the `profitabilityData` (`event_profitability`) query INSIDE the advanced route (the 2nd element of the initial Promise.all), NOT the separate `apps/api/app/api/analytics/events/profitability/route.ts`. The separate profitability route is ALREADY a clean SQL `GROUP BY TO_CHAR(event_date,'YYYY-MM')` returning O(months) rows — it is NOT an unbounded materialization and needs no bound. (The in-advanced `profitabilityData` query feeds a JS `profitMap` joined against events; bounding it would drop events from the aggregates = same truncation trap, so it stays window-scoped.)

### 10. `[RESOLVED 2026-07-12: apps/api Promise.all; 2026-07-14: MAX_QUERY_LENGTH + Cache-Control parity (#10b) shipped; tsvector GIN + route reconcile deferred]` Search route waterfall + knowledge-base tsvector GIN index
- **What:** Parallelize the **`apps/api`** global search waterfall and add a tsvector GIN index for knowledge-base `ILIKE`.
- **Why / evidence:** `apps/api/app/api/search/route.ts` + ~~`apps/app/app/api/search/route.ts`~~: when `type` is omitted, ~15 sequential `findMany`+`count` blocks (serial waterfall) — **(4th rev, 2026-07-12)** 15 blocks × 2 = **30 queries worst-case** (prior "~14" understated), no server debounce. Knowledge-base `ILIKE` on content (`search/route.ts:327`) is an unindexed full-text scan.
  - ~~The plan claims BOTH apps/api and apps/app search routes are serial waterfalls.~~
  > **(2nd-revision correction, 2026-07-12):** **FALSE.** `apps/app/app/api/search/route.ts` **ALREADY wraps all entity queries in a single `Promise.all`** (parallel). **Only `apps/api/app/api/search/route.ts` is the 15-block serial waterfall** (30 round-trips, no type filter). KB `ILIKE` on `@db.Text` content confirmed **unindexed** (`KnowledgeBaseEntry` is in `manifest.prisma:3272`; no `tsvector`/GIN anywhere) → index via `manifest/source`. NEW: **two divergent `/api/search` routes (15 types vs 7)** — possible double load / contract drift; reconcile during the fix.
- **Fix:** Wrap the independent search blocks in `apps/api` in `Promise.all`; add server-side debounce. Add a tsvector GIN index on the knowledge-base content column (via `manifest/source` since the model is generated) + use it for the KB clause. Reconcile the two divergent `/api/search` route shapes.
- **Scope:** `route` (apps/api) + `manifest-source` (the tsvector GIN index)
- **Acceptance check:** `apps/api` omni-type search does one round-trip batch, not 15; KB search hits the GIN index (`EXPLAIN` confirms); before/after on the search route.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-12, apps/api search Promise.all SHIPPED):** Collapsed the `apps/api/app/api/search/route.ts` omni-search waterfall. Premise correction (re-verified this turn): the plan's "15 sequential findMany+count blocks" framing was correct that the ENTITY BLOCKS were serial, but each block's findMany+count was ALREADY a `Promise.all`. The real cost was the 15 entity blocks running serially when `type` is omitted (the default omni-search) = 15 serial rounds (30 queries). Fix: each `if (shouldSearch(...))` block now pushes its findMany+count promise into an `entries` array via a module-scope `searchGroup` helper WITHOUT awaiting; one trailing `Promise.all` resolves every active group in a single concurrent round → omni-search drops from N serial rounds to 1. Scoped (`type=…`) search still runs exactly one group. Exact query shapes (`where`/`select`/`orderBy`/`take`/`skip`) preserved byte-for-byte; the knowledge-block `status: "published"` gained `as const` because extracting `where` to a `const` lost the inline contextual narrowing (the inline original narrowed via the `findMany({ where })` contextual type). **Call-order preservation (reusable technique, cf. [[parallelization-mock-order-pattern]]):** entries are pushed in the same sequence as the prior serial `if`-blocks, and within each push the findMany promise is constructed before the count promise — so the synchronous DB call order is identical to the serial version. The existing `apps/api/__tests__/search/search.test.ts` mocks `@repo/database` via `vi.importActual` + persistent `mockResolvedValue` (NOT order-dependent `mockResolvedValueOnce`), so all **28/28 tests pass unchanged**. **apps/app search route was ALREADY fully parallel** (`apps/app/app/api/search/route.ts` wraps all 7 entity groups in a single `Promise.all`, each group's findMany+count also parallel) — so the "reconcile two divergent routes" sub-item is lower-urgency than framed: apps/app is the parallel exemplar and apps/api was the laggard (now fixed on parallelism). Gates: `apps/api` typecheck = **17 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `search/route.ts`** (the refactor introduced 3 transient errors — knowledge `status` widening + `noUncheckedIndexedAccess` on `results[index]` — both fixed: `as const` + async-map assignment); Biome = no errors (1 pre-existing baseline warning `noExcessiveCognitiveComplexity` 21>20, identical to the original committed GET — the 15 `if(shouldSearch)` blocks dominate and cognitive-complexity scores nested-function branches separately, so the module-scope extractions `searchGroup`/`makeBaseFilter`/`WHITESPACE` were correct but could not drop GET's score below baseline; non-blocking, left as baseline). No schema/manifest touched → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **DEFERRED sub-items of #10 (separate scoped follow-ups, NOT stubs):** (a) the knowledge-base tsvector GIN index — bare `rg "tsvector"`, `rg "GIN"`, `rg "to_tsvector"` = ZERO repo-wide; the manifest `searchable` modifier on `KnowledgeBaseEntry.title` (`manifest/source/knowledge-base/knowledge-base-rules.manifest:12`) is declarative-only (no projection), and the KB `content` `@db.Text` ILIKE (`apps/app/app/api/search/route.ts:323-326`) is a genuine unindexed full-text scan → needs a tsvector+GIN via `manifest/source` + `pnpm manifest:build` and a query rewrite to use it (manifest-source change, its own gate); (b) server-side debounce / `MAX_QUERY_LENGTH` parity on the apps/api route (apps/app already has `MAX_QUERY_LENGTH=200` + `Cache-Control`); (c) reconciling the two `/api/search` route type-lists (apps/api 15 vs apps/app 7) now that both are parallel — a contract decision (which types each surfaces), lower priority. Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (item #1).
- **Implementation log (2026-07-14, apps/api search MAX_QUERY_LENGTH + Cache-Control parity SHIPPED — #10b):** Added the two guardrails the apps/app sibling search route already carries to `apps/api/app/api/search/route.ts` — the (b) sub-item the prior #10 log deferred. **(1) `MAX_QUERY_LENGTH = 200` upper bound:** the GET already early-returned on `q.length < 2` (min-length) but had NO upper bound, so a pathologically long `q` (e.g. a 10KB string) drove the full omni-search fan-out — up to 15 `findMany` + 15 `count` ILIKE scans — before any result. Now `if (!q || q.length < 2 || q.length > MAX_QUERY_LENGTH)` early-returns the same empty-success shape (`{ groups: [], total: 0 }`) with ZERO DB reads. Mirrors `apps/app/app/api/search/route.ts:21,77` (`MAX_QUERY_LENGTH = 200`); the constant is `export`ed so the route test pins the boundary against the single source of truth (no duplicated magic number). **(2) `Cache-Control` on the success response:** `private, max-age=30, stale-while-revalidate=300` — set via `response.headers.set(...)` on the `manifestSuccessResponse` return (a constructed `NextResponse` has mutable headers, so the shared helper is untouched). Deliberately **`private` (NOT `public`)** — unlike the apps/app route's `public`: search results are authenticated + tenant-scoped, so a shared CDN caching by URL alone could serve tenant A's `/api/search?q=foo` body to tenant B (cross-tenant leak); `private` restricts caching to the end-user's browser only, keeping the repeat-search benefit (search-as-you-type reuses the 30s browser cache) without the leak. The apps/app `public` is a latent leak to flag separately (out of this increment's scope — surgical changes). **Verification:** extended `apps/api/__tests__/search/search.test.ts` (**31/31 green**, was 28) — added (a) over-bound rejection: `q = "a".repeat(201)` → 200 + `{groups:[],total:0}` AND `event.findMany`/`knowledgeBaseEntry.findMany`/`lead.findMany` NEVER called (pins the fan-out skip), (b) boundary-exclusive: `q = "a".repeat(200)` PROCEEDS to search (`event.findMany` called — pins `>` not `>=`), (c) the success response carries `Cache-Control` containing `private` + `max-age=30` and NOT `public`. Drive-by: fixed a PRE-EXISTING biome `useIterableCallbackReturn` error in the unrelated multi-token AND test (`.map` with a bare `return;` → ternary that always returns; behavior-identical — the `undefined` branch was never hit, the assertion still passes `["john","smith","catering"]`). Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `search/route.ts` or the test**; biome = only the PRE-EXISTING `noExcessiveCognitiveComplexity` 21>20 advisory warning on GET (documented baseline in the prior #10 log — the 15 `if(shouldSearch)` blocks dominate; the added `||` operand did not raise it); code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#10 status:** the apps/api Promise.all parallelization (2026-07-12) + this MAX_QUERY_LENGTH/Cache-Control parity (#10b) are DONE; the residual deferred sub-items are (a) the KB `content` tsvector GIN index (manifest-source + migration, its own gate) and (c) reconciling the apps/api-15 vs apps/app-7 search type-lists (a contract decision). Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is structural (a pathologically long query can no longer drive 30 ILIKE scans, + 30s browser caching of identical omni-searches) regardless of measured magnitude. Search: #10b apps/api search MAX_QUERY_LENGTH Cache-Control private parity, no upper bound fan-out guard.

### 11. `[RESOLVED 2026-07-12]` Public proposal/contract parallel queries
- **What:** Collapse the serial independent reads on the public proposal and contract token routes.
- **Why / evidence:** `public/proposals/[token]/route.ts:33-188` runs 1 prerequisite (proposal) + 5 serial independent queries (lineItems, client, lead, event, account) — **(4th rev, 2026-07-12)** parallelize the 5, not all 6 (they depend on the proposal row); `public/contracts/[token]/route.ts:32,71,85` runs triple `findFirst` on the same `signingToken`. These are user-facing (externally shared links). (Cross-ref item #21 for the unauthenticated `public/contracts/[token]/sign/route.ts:75` over-fetch.)
- **Fix:** One `Promise.all` for the independent reads; collapse the triple `findFirst` to one query with `select` (**(4th rev, 2026-07-12)** the first `select` omits `eventId`/`clientId`, forcing the 2nd/3rd — add those fields to the first `select`).
- **Scope:** `route`
- **Acceptance check:** Public proposal route does 1 round-trip batch instead of 6; contract route 1 instead of 3; before/after measured.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-12, RESOLVED):** Collapsed both public token routes' serial reads into single `Promise.all` batches — these are **unauthenticated, externally-shared links** (no Clerk session), so every proposal/contract view paid the full serial cost up front.
  - **Proposal** (`apps/api/app/api/public/proposals/[token]/route.ts`): 6 serial round-trips → **2** (1 prerequisite `proposal.findFirst` + 1 batch of `lineItems`/`client`/`lead`/`event`/`tenant`). The `lead` branch is gated `!proposal.clientId && proposal.leadId`, which is provably equivalent to the original serial `!client && proposal.leadId` (since `client` was assigned only when `clientId` existed) — so the lead query is data-independent of the client result and can join the batch.
  - **Contract** (`apps/api/app/api/public/contracts/[token]/route.ts`): the prior "3 findFirst on the same token" framing **under-counted** — it was actually **7 serial round-trips** (contract select + a `eventId` findFirst **nested inside the event query's `where`** + the event query + a standalone `clientId` findFirst + the client raw query + signatures + tenant). Fix: added `eventId`+`clientId` to the first `select` (killing both redundant same-row fetches) and batched `event`/`client`/`signatures`/`tenant` → **2 round-trips**. Also incidentally fixed a latent bug where a null `eventId` made the event query filter on `id: undefined` (Prisma treats as no-filter → returned an arbitrary tenant event); now guarded on `contract.eventId`.
  - **Why it matters:** the public contract view is the worst offender of the two (3 of its 7 round-trips re-fetched the SAME row); this is exactly the kind of cold-start tax a recipient hits when they open a shared link.
  - **Verification:** existing `apps/api/__tests__/public/contracts-proposals.test.ts` **35/35 green**. **Reusable technique for future parallelization items (#7/#23/etc.):** the suite uses order-dependent `mockResolvedValueOnce` on a single mocked `$queryRaw` `vi.fn`. `Promise.all` invokes its array elements left-to-right synchronously, so **ordering the batch array to match the original serial call order preserves mock-call sequence** — the 5 proposal-route `$queryRaw` tests pass **unchanged**. Only the 2 contract-route tests that asserted the redundant token refetches needed edits (merged `eventId`/`clientId` into the single main-select mock + dropped the 2 extra `findFirst` mock chains); the 3 contract tests that return before the reads (404/410/500) were untouched. `apps/api` typecheck: **17 pre-existing errors, ZERO in the two touched route files**. No schema/manifest touched → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` baseline unchanged. Live before/after latency (item #1's instrumentation) deferred to a seeded-DB measurement pass.

### 12. `[RESOLVED 2026-07-12]` Calendar sync N+1 batch preload
- **What:** Batch-load existing events once per calendar sync instead of per external event.
- **Why / evidence:** `calendar/sync/trigger/route.ts:262,270,371,377` — `syncGoogleCalendar` + `syncOutlookCalendar`: up to 250 external events × `await database.event.findFirst(...)` per iteration ≈ 500 sequential round-trips per sync.
- **Fix:** Pre-load existing events matching the batch by `(title, eventDate, eventType)` into a `Map`; in-memory lookup per external event.
- **Scope:** `route`
- **Acceptance check:** Per-sync round-trips drop from ~500 to ~1 preload + writes; before/after measured.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-12, RESOLVED):** Collapsed the per-external-event `event.findFirst` in both `syncGoogleCalendar` and `syncOutlookCalendar` (`apps/api/app/api/calendar/sync/trigger/route.ts`) — each looped up to 250 external events × one `findFirst` (tenantId+title+eventDate+eventType+deletedAt) = up to ~500 sequential round-trips per sync — into a single preload. Added two module helpers: `loadExistingEventIds(database, tenantId, eventType)` = one `event.findMany({ where: { tenantId, eventType, deletedAt: null }, select: { id: true, title: true, eventDate: true, eventType: true } })`, and `eventDedupKey(title, eventDate, eventType)` = `` `${title}|${eventDate.toISOString()}|${eventType}` ``, building a `Map<string, string>` (key → existing.id) BEFORE each loop; the per-event existence check is now an in-memory `Map.get`. `eventType` (constant per function — `"external_google"`/`"external_outlook"`) was hoisted out of the loop to drive the preload. **The preload is scoped by tenant+type only (NO date window) — this EXACTLY preserves the original `findFirst` dedup semantics** (which also had no date window), so zero behavior change / zero duplicate-creation risk; a manual sync loading one tenant's external events once is cheap relative to the 250 sequential queries it replaces. `eventDate` is normalized to `.toISOString()` in the key (Date objects use reference equality as Map keys — without normalization every lookup would miss). Update branch reuses the matched id (`{ ...eventPayload, id: existingId }` + `instanceId: existingId`); create branch unchanged. **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/calendar/sync-trigger.test.ts` (3/3 green) — the FIRST tests for the sync routes (existing `calendar.test.ts` covered only GET/PATCH). Pins (1) the N+1 collapse: `event.findFirst` NEVER called + `event.findMany` exactly once for a 3-event Google batch and a 2-event Outlook batch (fails if reverted to per-event findFirst); (2) behavior parity — a pre-existing event routes to `update` with the correct `instanceId`, the rest to `create`; (3) Map-key parity — same title+type but a different `eventDate` does NOT match → `create` (not `update`). Mocks use `mockResolvedValue` (not order-dependent `mockResolvedValueOnce`) per the [[parallelization-mock-order-pattern]] spirit. Gates: focused calendar suite **45/45 green** (3 new + 42 existing — zero regression); `apps/api` typecheck = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO new** (none in `route.ts` or the test); no schema/manifest touched → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). Incidental cleanup: converted the file's PRE-EXISTING `type ManifestUser = {...}` → `interface ManifestUser` (biome `useConsistentTypeDefinitions` error the file already carried at HEAD; repo convention is 311 `interface` vs 13 `type X={}` in apps/api — converting aligned with both). Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (item #1); the win is structural (~500 → 2 round-trips per sync) regardless of measured magnitude.

### 13. `[RESOLVED 2026-07-14: dedicated governed Lead.setScore command SHIPPED → 2N→N governed round-trips + atomic score/event write; non-atomic dual-write removed; within-batch parallelism still N-serial (blocked on NEEDS-RYAN runtime rework shared with #14/#18/#25)]` CRM scoring batch recompute + dual-write anti-pattern
- **What:** Stop the per-lead governed round-trips in score calculation; recompute in memory and batch. Also fix the dual-write non-atomicity.
- **Why / evidence:** `crm/scoring/calculate/route.ts:136-148,177-209` loops every lead calling `runManifestCommand` + `updateMany` per row (2N serial governed round-trips) on both the zero-rules and happy paths.
  - `[NEW MED, 2nd Revision — add]` **Dual-write anti-pattern:** `runManifestCommand` fires a governed update with body `{id, tenantId}` then a **separate** `lead.updateMany` writes the score → **non-atomic** (a failure between the two leaves a stale entity event / mismatched score). Recompute-and-batch should also make the score write atomic with the governed event (single governed update carrying the score, or a single batched updateMany with no competing governed write).
- **Fix:** Recompute scores in memory from the loaded rules + leads; one batched `updateMany` (or chunked) per tenant; collapse the dual-write so the score and the governed event land atomically.
- **Scope:** `route`
- **Acceptance check:** Score recompute is O(leads) in memory + O(chunks) writes, not 2N governed calls; score + governed event are atomic; correctness parity on a seeded tenant.
- **Investigation + deferral log (2026-07-13):** Investigated for this pass; **DEFERRED as too risky for a clean autonomous increment** (pivoted to #7 getAvailableEmployees). Re-verified the route (`apps/api/app/api/crm/scoring/calculate/route.ts`, POST-only): it recomputes scores in memory (already O(leads) — `leadMatchesRule` is pure, fully independent per lead) then writes per-lead: a governed `runManifestCommand({entity:"Lead",command:"update",body:{id,tenantId}})` (body carries NO score) followed by a SEPARATE plain `database.lead.updateMany({data:{score,scoreBreakdown}})` — the non-atomic dual-write (L191-208; identical pattern in the zero-rules branch L136-148). Loads are BEFORE the loop (rules raw-SQL L110; leads `findMany` L157) so recompute-and-batch is structurally viable. **Blocker on the clean fix:** the route's own comments (L130-131, L189-190) call score/scoreBreakdown "non-IR derived fields **not modeled** in Lead manifest entity," but `manifest/source/sales/lead-rules.manifest:20,35` DOES declare `property score: int = 0` + `property scoreBreakdown: json = {}` — a **stale/contradicted comment**. Whether the governed `Lead.update` actually PERSISTS `score`/`scoreBreakdown` from the body is UNVERIFIED, and per [[generic-prisma-store-occ-silent-data-loss]] governed writes can silently drop fields (7 unfixed) — so the plan's "single governed update carrying the score" option risks **silent data loss** (HTTP 200, score never written). The safe alternative (keep the separate Prisma write + batch the governed touches via `runManifestBatch` + a raw-SQL bulk `UPDATE ... FROM (VALUES)` for per-lead-distinct scores) introduces raw-SQL lead writes + keeps a batched dual-write + changes governance/event semantics (1 batch tx vs N events) on a manifest-runtime baseline that is RED on typecheck since ~Jul 9. **Defer until:** (a) governed `Lead.update` writability of `score`/`scoreBreakdown` is verified against the IR (or the stale L130-131/L189-190 comment is reconciled — the fields ARE modeled per the manifest source), AND (b) the manifest-runtime typecheck baseline is green. Left for the same owner to avoid a half-fix.
- **(2026-07-14 unblock + comment fix SHIPPED):** A focused verification pass RESOLVED the two open questions that made the 2026-07-13 deferral "too risky," and the route's justifying comment was PROVEN FALSE on two counts (documentation law → fixed). **(1) The writability question is ANSWERED:** the governed `Lead.update` does NOT persist `score`/`scoreBreakdown` — NOT because they are "not modeled" (the route comment L130-131/L189-190 claimed both "non-IR derived fields" AND "not modeled in Lead manifest entity") but because the `Lead.update` command's parameter list + `mutate` block (`manifest/source/sales/lead-rules.manifest:104,122-132`) omit them. They ARE declared stored properties (`lead-rules.manifest:20 property score: int = 0`, `:35 property scoreBreakdown: json = {}`) AND real Prisma columns (`packages/database/prisma/schema/manifest.prisma:3344 score Int @default(0)`, `:3359 scoreBreakdown Json`). The route works today ONLY because the separate `database.lead.updateMany` bypasses the governed command. The governed `Lead.update` body `{id, tenantId}` is effectively a NO-OP write (emits `LeadUpdated` + audit, mutates nothing). **(2) The typecheck-blocker is NARROWER than framed:** apps/api `tsc --noEmit` = **14 errors, NONE in `crm/scoring/calculate/route.ts` or the Lead manifest runtime path** (the 14 = `manifest/runtime/.../ai-suggestions.ts` ×4 + `kitchen/equipment/list` ×3 + the `staff/shifts` nullable-`locationId` cluster ×7 — all pre-existing, all unrelated to Lead). So the Lead path is clean; the global baseline being RED is orthogonal. **Comment fix (doc law, shipped this turn):** replaced both false comments with the verified explanation + a `TODO(db-perf #13)` pointing at the fix (the comment was the artifact that trapped the prior deferral into the "silent-data-loss risk" framing). **Safe-fix path (next increment, NOT rushed this turn — manifest-source + regen deserves a focused pass):** add a DEDICATED governed command `Lead.setScore(score, scoreBreakdown)` whose `mutate` writes exactly those two fields (NO blast radius on the existing `Lead.update` — adding `mutate score` to `update` would RESET score to default on every unrelated Lead edit, the dangerous option). The route then calls `setScore` per lead instead of the no-op `update` + `updateMany` → **2N→N governed round-trips AND atomicity** (score + `LeadUpdated` event land in one governed write, removing the non-atomic dual-write). Still N serial governed round-trips (the within-batch parallelism stays blocked on the runtime-rework NEEDS-RYAN per #14/#18/#25 — the runtime is NOT concurrent-safe). **Verdict:** the perf fix is now UNBLOCKED + low-risk-via-dedicated-command (the silent-data-loss concern that framed the deferral does NOT apply to a NEW command that explicitly mutates only score/scoreBreakdown); it is teed up as the next #13 increment (manifest-source edit + `pnpm manifest:build` regen + route swap + test). Search: #13 CRM scoring unblock, Lead.update omits score scoreBreakdown, route comment proven false, dedicated setScore command, dual-write non-atomic.
- **(2026-07-14, dedicated governed Lead.setScore command SHIPPED — resolves the #13 dual-write + 2N→N perf fix teed up by the unblock above):** Added a NEW governed command `Lead.setScore(score: number, scoreBreakdown: json)` to `manifest/source/sales/lead-rules.manifest` (placed right after `Lead.update`). Its body is `guard self.deletedAt == null "Cannot score an archived lead"` + `mutate score = score` + `mutate scoreBreakdown = scoreBreakdown` + `emit LeadUpdated` — the proven `json`-param + `mutate X = X` shape from `email-template-rules.manifest:23-51` (`mergeFields: json`). **Why a dedicated command, NOT adding score/scoreBreakdown to `Lead.update`:** `update`'s params are all `optional` with `mutate X = X != null ? X : self.X`; adding `score`/`scoreBreakdown` there would reset them to defaults on EVERY unrelated Lead edit (the dangerous option the unblock log named). `setScore` mutates ONLY those two fields → zero blast radius on `Lead.update`. **Why `emit LeadUpdated` (not a new `LeadScored` event):** the route ALREADY emitted `LeadUpdated` per lead today via the no-op `Lead.update` call, so reusing it preserves the EXACT current audit/event channel (smallest behavioral delta, matches the unblock log's "score + LeadUpdated event land in one governed write"); and `rg crm.lead|LeadUpdated` over `manifest/source` confirmed NO reactions are wired to `crm.lead.updated` → no fan-out risk. The `guard self.deletedAt == null` deliberately OMITS the converted-lead guard (the route recomputes scores for ALL non-deleted leads incl. converted ones — adding it would break scoring of converted leads). **Regen:** `pnpm manifest:build` → 1071 commands (+1; crm chunk now 11 entities / 58 commands). Compiled Zod schema: `Lead.setScore: z.object({ score: z.number(), scoreBreakdown: z.unknown() })` — both required, matching the route's inputs. **`manifest.prisma` is UNCHANGED** (verified: not in `git status`) — adding a command changed no Lead column shape → no migration, no drift. **Route swap** (`apps/api/app/api/crm/scoring/calculate/route.ts`): BOTH loops (zero-rules L129-154 + happy-path L176-199) now issue ONE `runManifestCommand({entity:"Lead",command:"setScore",body:{id,tenantId,score,scoreBreakdown},user,instanceId})` per lead; the two `database.lead.updateMany({data:{score,scoreBreakdown}})` raw writes are REMOVED (the non-atomic dual-write + the raw score-persisted-outside-governance bypass). Per-lead: was 1 governed `update` (no-op, body `{id,tenantId}` mutates nothing) + 1 raw `updateMany` = **2N** round-trips; now **N** governed `setScore` writes, each atomic (score + `LeadUpdated` event + audit land in one governed write). **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/crm/scoring-calculate-set-score.test.ts` (**3/3 green** — the FIRST test for the `/calculate` route) pinning (1) the happy path: 2 leads + 1 rule → exactly 2 governed dispatches, EVERY one `entity:"Lead"/command:"setScore"` (never the old `update`), the per-lead bodies carry the computed score + breakdown (matching lead + `+25`, non-matching lead `0`/`{}`) + actor context from `resolveCurrentUser`, AND the distribution math (`cold:2`); (2) the zero-rules branch: all leads reset to `score:0/scoreBreakdown:{}` via `setScore`; (3) the 401-before-any-DB-read auth guard. The discriminating **regression guard:** `@repo/database` is mocked WITH a `lead.updateMany` spy asserted `not.toHaveBeenCalled()` — reverting to the dual-write fails it loudly. CRM suite **144/144 green** (10 files, incl. the sibling `scoring-post-governed.test.ts` — zero regression). Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **14 errors = pre-existing baseline** (manifest-runtime-red-since-~Jul-9 `ai-suggestions.ts` + `staff/shifts` cluster), **ZERO in the route or test**; `pnpm manifest:ci` **all gates green** (prisma "No drift", openapi/field-hints/feature-ownership in sync); `pnpm db:check` **exit 0**. **#13 RESOLVED (core)** — the dual-write non-atomicity (the `[NEW MED]` finding) is GONE and the round-trip count halves (2N→N) + the score write is now governed (no more raw `lead.updateMany` bypass). **Residual (blocked, NOT in #13's achievable scope):** within-batch parallelism stays N-serial — concurrent governed `runtime.runCommand` on a shared runtime is UNSAFE (settled under #18: shared `readCache` + re-entrant eval budget in `manifest-runtime-factory.ts:673,522`); the N→O(chunks) concurrent win needs the NEEDS-RYAN runtime rework shared with #14/#18/#25. Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is structural (governance + atomicity + 2N→N round-trips on every score recompute) regardless of measured magnitude. Search: #13 Lead.setScore shipped, crm scoring calculate setScore, dual-write removed, 2N→N governed round-trips atomic score. `[PARTIAL 2026-07-14: inventory-import + events/documents/parse read-preloads + outbox publish published-write batching + timecards/bulk read-N+1 SHIPPED]` Await-in-loop N+1 sweep (governed writes + per-row reads)
- **What:** Collapse the verified await-in-loop sites into batched writes / preloaded maps. Worst-first.
- **Why / evidence (file:line):**
  - `kitchen/allergens/detect-conflicts/route.ts:250` — **NESTED O(guests×dishes)** governed warning writes (highest cost).
  - `apps/app/app/api/inventory/import/route.ts:157` — `$queryRaw` existence check + `runManifestCommand` create/update per item = N+1 upsert.
- **(2026-07-13 governance correction — read-only assessment verified against `manifest/runtime/src/manifest-runtime-factory.ts:787-790`):** the inventory-import WRITES are GOVERNED `runManifestCommand({entity:"InventoryItem", command:"update"|"create"})` calls, NOT raw Prisma. Switching them to `createMany`/`updateMany` would bypass RBAC, constraints, audit (PostgresAuditSink, constitution §12), emitted events, and reactions — a constitution violation. The ONLY batchable part of this site is the READ-SIDE per-item `$queryRaw` existence check (`SELECT id ... WHERE item_number IN (...)` once, materialized into a `Set`/`Map`); the governed per-row writes must stay on `RuntimeEngine.runCommand()`. Scope any fix here to the read preload only.
  - **Read-preload gotcha (2026-07-13, noticed during assessment):** `apps/app/app/api/inventory/import/route.ts:160-166` does the per-item `$queryRaw` existence check (`SELECT id FROM tenant_inventory.inventory_items WHERE tenant_id=$1 AND item_number=$2 AND deleted_at IS NULL LIMIT 1`) keyed on `item_number`, all items share one `tenantId`, and only `id` is needed as the lookup value — so a single `WHERE tenant_id=$1 AND item_number IN (...)` → `Map<item_number,id>` preload is structurally viable (N reads → 1). **BUT a naive preload changes behavior for duplicate `item_number`s WITHIN one import:** the current per-item serial code dedupes-by-update (if the same `item_number` appears twice in the Excel sheet, the 2nd iteration's existence check finds the row the 1st just created → UPDATE). A Map snapshot taken BEFORE any creates would make the 2nd occurrence attempt a CREATE → likely unique-constraint failure (caught as an error). To preserve exact behavior, the preload must ALSO track `item_number`s created during the loop and feed each new id back into the Map so a duplicate updates the in-batch create. No test covers this route today; add one covering the duplicate-`item_number` dedup path before/after. (The `runManifestCommand` create result presumably carries the new id — confirm before relying on it.)
  - ~~`app/outbox/publish/route.ts:127` — `outboxEvent.update` per pending event, up to 100.~~
  > **(2nd-revision correction, 2026-07-12):** Path is **`apps/api/app/outbox/publish/route.ts:127`** (NOT `app/outbox/publish`). `outboxEvent.update` per pending event, up to 100.
  - `payroll/timecards/generate/route.ts:216` — `runManifestCommand` per shift.
  - `crm/proposal-automation/route.ts:195` — `generateForEvent` per event.
  - `staff/availability/batch/route.ts:93,131` — two per-pattern loops (validation + create).
  - `administrative/trash/list/route.ts:279` + `administrative/trash/analyze/route.ts:490` — `delegate.findMany` per entity/dependent type.
  - ~~… up to 10.~~
  > **(2nd-revision correction, 2026-07-12):** `trash/analyze` max is **9 dependent types** (`Event`), **not 10**.
- **Fix:** Batch via `updateMany`/`createMany`/`VALUES` CTE where the governed-write constitution allows; preload existence-check rows into a `Set`/`Map`; keep domain mutations on `RuntimeEngine.runCommand()` (no raw-SQL bypass). Conceptually overlaps item #18's per-row-write batching — prioritize the nested allergen loop + inventory import + outbox publish first.
- **Scope:** `route`
- **Acceptance check:** Each cited loop collapses to O(1) or O(chunks) round-trips; transaction/governance semantics preserved; before/after on allergen-conflict + inventory-import.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, inventory-import read-preload SHIPPED — resolves the prior-turn gotcha):** Collapsed the per-row existence check in `POST /api/inventory/import` (`apps/app/app/api/inventory/import/route.ts`) — the route the prior turn assessed + recorded the duplicate-`item_number` gotcha for (commit `2e227c16b`). **Before:** the upsert loop fired one `$queryRaw\`SELECT id … WHERE tenant_id=$1 AND item_number=$2 AND deleted_at IS NULL LIMIT 1\`` PER uploaded row → an N-row sheet paid N sequential existence round-trips before the first governed write. **After (1 round-trip, independent of N):** preload every existing id for the import's `item_number`s in ONE `SELECT item_number, id … WHERE tenant_id=$1 AND item_number IN (${Prisma.join(itemNumbers)}) AND deleted_at IS NULL`, materialized into a `Map<item_number, id>` (first-row-per-`item_number` wins, mirroring the prior per-item `LIMIT 1`); the per-row lookup is an in-memory `Map.get`. All rows share the resolved `tenantId` and only `id` is needed. The governed writes (`runManifestCommand` InventoryItem update/create per row) are UNTOUCHED — switching them to `createMany`/`updateMany` would bypass RBAC/constraints/audit/events/reactions (constitution §12), so only the READ side collapsed (exactly the governance-corrected scope this item's investigation established). **Gotcha resolved (the duplicate-`item_number`-within-one-import case the prior turn flagged):** `InventoryItem` has NO unique constraint on `item_number` (verified `manifest.prisma:2819` bare `item_number String`, no `@unique`/`@@unique`), so the prior serial code's behavior was "a repeated SKU in one sheet finds the row the 1st iteration just created → UPDATE." A naive Map snapshot taken BEFORE any creates would make the 2nd occurrence CREATE a 2nd row (silent data divergence). Preserved exactly by **feeding each successful create's new id back into the Map** — `result.result.id` is the created-entity projection (verified: `runManifestCommand` success carries `result: payload.result` per `apps/app/lib/manifest-command.ts:193-206`, and apps/app call sites already read it — `board-canvas.tsx:581`, `log-waste-entry.ts:84`, `agent-loop.ts:497` "result.id per the dispatcher's success envelope"); on a create, `existingByItemNumber.set(item.item_number, createdId)` so a later duplicate UPDATEs the just-created row. The id is read defensively (`typeof createdId === "string"` guard on a cast `{id?:string}` of the `unknown` `result`) so a future dispatcher shape change degrades to "create" (the rare duplicate path) rather than throwing. **Verification:** added `apps/app/__tests__/inventory/inventory-import.test.ts` (**3/3 green** — the FIRST test for this route, which had ZERO coverage) pinning (1) the N+1 collapse + preload routing (`$queryRaw` called exactly ONCE for a 3-row sheet; 1 pre-existing → `update`, 2 absent → `create`), (2) the duplicate-`item_number` feed-back dedup (same SKU twice: first `create`, second `update` of the fed-back id — the behavior the prior turn's gotcha said MUST be preserved), (3) the 401 auth guard before any DB read. Builds a real `Inventory` `.xlsx` (header pinned at row index 3 — `sheet_to_json({header:1})` SKIPS blank rows, so the 3 leading filler rows carry a non-empty cell to survive the parse) + a `FormData`/`File` POST via `NextRequest`. Mocks `@repo/database` fully (no `importOriginal` → no real Prisma client instantiation) with a stub `Prisma.Decimal` (no parameter property — repo tsconfig `erasableSyntaxOnly`) + stub `Prisma.join`; the Decimal value is never serialized (governed writes are mocked) so the stub never needs real decimal.js behavior. Gates: `apps/app tsc --noEmit` = **9 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `inventory/import/route.ts` or the test** (the 9 = scheduling/shifts `mapShiftRows` ×2 + 3 staff/training Zod-v4 + 3 chart-catalog Vega-Lite + 1 analytics/kitchen nullable — all documented pre-existing); code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **Pre-existing biome (NOT mine, left as-is per surgical-changes):** the route carries a baseline `noExcessiveCognitiveComplexity` warning (64>20) on the 250-line POST + a `noNamespaceImport` error on `import * as XLSX` — BOTH verified firing at HEAD before this edit (the XLSX import predates this change); fixing the namespace import would mean rewriting `XLSX.read`/`XLSX.utils.*` call sites, an unrelated refactor expanding the diff, so it is left (advisory; not a commit gate — the pre-commit hook runs manifest-validate + secretlint, not biome). **#14 REMAINS OPEN** — the inventory-import read-preload (the read-side half this item's governance-corrected scope named for it) shipped; the remaining #14 sites are governed-WRITE batching (allergen nested O(guests×dishes) warnings, outbox `update` per pending event, payroll/timecards per-shift, proposal-automation per-event, staff/availability per-pattern) which need `runManifestBatch`/batched-tx work that respects the governed-write constitution, + the inventory-import duplicate-`item_number` WRITE path could later adopt a within-batch governed batch. Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is structural (N→1 existence reads per import, the largest read-N+1 in this item) regardless of measured magnitude.

- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, outbox publish `published`-write batching SHIPPED — #14's teed-up write-batching win):** Collapsed the per-event `published` status writes in `runPublishLoop` (`apps/api/app/outbox/publish/route.ts`) — the outbox drain cron (Vercel Cron every minute, `apps/api/vercel.json:48`; GET default limit 100 / POST up to 500) that previously fired ONE `outboxEvent.update({ where:{id}, data:{status:"published", publishedAt, error:null} })` PER fanned-out event = up to 100-500 serial UPDATE round-trips per tick. **After (1 round-trip for the published bucket, regardless of N):** accumulate fanned-out ids into `publishedIds[]` during the loop, then ONE guarded `database.outboxEvent.updateMany({ where:{ id:{ in: publishedIds } }, data:{ status:"published", publishedAt: new Date(), error:null } })` after the loop. **Failure paths stay per-event** (PAYLOAD_TOO_LARGE + PUBLISH_ERROR carry per-event-varying error strings — `${messageSize}` / `${message}` — and are rare; keeping them per-event preserves exact error semantics + avoids a raw-SQL `UPDATE FROM VALUES` drift on the `tenant.OutboxEvent` infra table). **`OutboxEvent` is infra** (`infra.prisma:1216`, `@@schema("tenant")`, `@@map("OutboxEvent")`, `OutboxStatus` enum `pending|published|failed`) — NOT a governed domain entity → `updateMany` is allowed here (no RBAC/audit/event bypass; cf the governance correction that keeps the inventory-import WRITES on `RuntimeEngine.runCommand()`). **Correctness improvement folded in:** the old per-event `published` update sat INSIDE the loop's try/catch, so a status-write blip was caught + FALSELY marked a successfully-fanned-out event `failed` (`PUBLISH_ERROR`); the batched write's OWN try/catch now leaves such events `pending` for the next tick (at-least-once — SSE consumers dedupe by event id) — strictly more correct than before. **At-least-once amplification (documented trade-off, NOT a new guarantee break):** deferring the status write widens the window in which a crash/blip → re-delivery; the existing design already assumes idempotent re-processing (`FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED` fetch `route.ts:109-117` + the `status !== "pending"` double-check `:129`), so this amplifies an ACCEPTED property rather than introducing a new failure mode. **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/outbox/publish.test.ts` (**5/5 green** — mocked, pins the batching) — (1) N fanned-out events → ONE `updateMany` with `where.id.in:[all ids]` + the `published` data, and `update` NEVER called for the published path (fails if reverted to per-event); (2) failure paths stay per-event (oversized→`PAYLOAD_TOO_LARGE` update with size-specific error, fanout-throw→`PUBLISH_ERROR` update, the one published event→batched `updateMany`); (3) a rejected `updateMany` does NOT crash (returns 200) and leaves events pending (no false `failed` marking — pins the correctness fix); (4) empty-published bucket skips the `updateMany` (no pointless `in:[]`); (5) 401 before any DB read. The discriminating `publishToChannel` mock throws by envelope `data.id` (the oversized event never reaches fanout — it fails the size check first — so a `mockReturnValueOnce` queue would misalign; a `mockImplementation` keyed on `data.id` is deterministic — this was the bug in the first draft). The real-DB `publish.integration.test.ts` (977 lines, asserts OUTCOMES not call counts) is transparent to the batching — left to run under `pnpm test:integration` (needs a live DB + seeded events; not runnable in this code-only increment). **Import-path gotcha (reusable):** the route lives at `apps/api/app/outbox/publish/route.ts` (NOT under `app/api/` — the cron path is `/outbox/publish` with no `/api/` prefix, and `proxy.ts` lists it in `isPublicRoute`); the test imports it via the RELATIVE `../../app/outbox/publish/route` (matching the integration test) because the `@/app/outbox/publish/route` alias FAILED to resolve under vitest even though `@/app/api/...` works for the api/ routes — the outbox route's non-`api/` location is the differentiator. Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `outbox/publish/route.ts` or the test** (first draft's mock callback params hit `noImplicitAny` TS7006 ×2 — fixed by annotating `(_channel: string, message: { data: { id: string } })`); code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#14 REMAINS OPEN** — inventory-import read-preload + outbox-publish published-write batching shipped; the remaining #14 sites are governed-WRITE batching on DOMAIN entities (allergen nested O(guests×dishes) warnings, payroll/timecards per-shift, proposal-automation per-event, staff/availability per-pattern) which need `runManifestBatch`/batched-tx work that respects the governed-write constitution — the outbox win was uniquely clean BECAUSE `outboxEvent` is infra (not governed). Live before/after tick DB-time deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is structural (up to 100-500 serial published UPDATEs → 1 `updateMany`/tick on a per-minute cron) regardless of measured magnitude.

- **Implementation log (2026-07-14, events/documents/parse menu-import read-preload SHIPPED — a #14 read-N+1 the prior turns missed):** Collapsed the per-menu-item existence reads in `importMenuToEvent` (`apps/api/app/api/events/documents/parse/route.ts` — the document-parse menu importer; `importMenuToEvent` is now exported for focused testing). This route was NOT covered by any prior #14 increment (inventory-import + outbox-publish shipped; this is a third instance of the same anti-pattern surfaced by a bounded `.map(async)` / await-in-loop sweep). **Before:** for each aggregated menu item the loop fired up to **3 serial READ round-trips** — `dish.findFirst({ name:{ equals, mode insensitive }})`, `recipe.findFirst({ name:{ equals, mode insensitive }})` (only when the dish was new), and `findExistingEventDishLink` `$queryRaw\`SELECT id … WHERE event_id AND dish_id=${dishId} LIMIT 1\`` — before the governed writes. A 30-dish menu import paid ~90 existence reads (plus the governed creates). **After (3 batched reads, independent of N):** (1) `dish.findMany({ where:{ tenantId, deletedAt:null, name:{ in: distinctNames, mode insensitive }}, select:{ id, name }})` → `Map<lowercaseName,{id}>` (aggregated keys are lowercased + unique, so first-match-per-name wins — matches the prior findFirst-without-orderBy "first row"); (2) `recipe.findMany` for the NEW dish names only (`distinctNames` minus existing) → `Map<lowercaseName, recipeId>`; (3) ONE link `$queryRaw\`SELECT id, dish_id … WHERE tenant_id AND event_id AND dish_id IN (${Prisma.join(existingDishIds)}) AND deleted_at IS NULL\`` → `Map<dishId, linkId>` — scoped to EXISTING dish ids only, because a newly created dish has no prior links (the preload covers every case a link could exist). The per-item loop then resolves dish/recipe/link from the Maps; the governed writes (Recipe.create, Dish.create, EventDish.create via `execCommand`→`runManifestCommandCore`) stay SERIAL — the manifest runtime is not concurrent-safe (cf. #14 inventory-import + #18), so only the READ side collapsed. **No within-payload feed-back needed** (unlike #25a's dup-SKU case): `aggregateMenuItems` dedupes by lowercased name, so each name is processed exactly once → no second occurrence of a created dish/recipe. Removed the now-dead `findExistingEventDishLink` helper. **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/events/documents-parse-menu-import.test.ts` (**3/3 green** — the FIRST test for this read path) pinning (1) the N+1 collapse in a mixed existing/new scenario: `dish.findMany` once with `name.in:[burger,salad,pasta]`, `recipe.findMany` once with `name.in:[pasta]` (new names only), `$queryRaw` once whose SQL contains `event_dishes`/`dish_id IN`/`deleted_at IS NULL`, and the per-entry `dish.findFirst`/`recipe.findFirst` NEVER called; per-item branching preserved (existing+link→`eventDish.updateMany`, existing no-link→create EventDish, new dish→create Dish + create EventDish, recipe reused) + summary counts; (2) all-new dishes skip the link preload entirely (`$queryRaw` NOT called — no existing dishes → nothing could be linked yet); (3) empty menu short-circuits with zero DB reads. Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **14 errors = pre-existing baseline (down from 16 — commit `4b69d43e4`'s staff/shifts null-guard locationId fixed 2 of the cluster), ZERO in the route or test**; biome clean on both files. **Reusable gotcha (reconfirmed [[biome-autofix-drops-new-import-mid-batch]]):** removing `findExistingEventDishLink` made the `Prisma` import transiently unused → the per-edit biome auto-fix stripped `Prisma` from `import { database, Prisma }` mid-batch → the later edit re-adding `Prisma.sql`/`Prisma.join` usage hit `noUndeclaredVariables`; re-added the import (value usage already present, so no re-drop). Also converted the file's pre-existing `type ManifestUser = {...}` → `interface` to satisfy `useConsistentTypeDefinitions` surfaced by touching the file (trivial, in-file). **#14 REMAINS OPEN** — three read-preloads now shipped (inventory-import, events/documents/parse menu-import) + the outbox infra-write batch; the remaining #14 sites are governed-WRITE batching on DOMAIN entities (allergen nested O(guests×dishes) warnings, payroll/timecards per-shift, proposal-automation per-event, staff/availability per-pattern) — BLOCKED on the runtime rework (manifest runtime not concurrent-safe). Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is structural (up to 3N existence reads → 3 batched reads per menu import) regardless of measured magnitude.

- **Implementation log (2026-07-14, timecards/bulk POST read-N+1 collapse SHIPPED — a #14 read-N+1 a bounded await-in-loop sweep surfaced that prior turns missed):** Collapsed the two per-iteration READ loops in `POST /api/timecards/bulk` (`apps/api/app/api/timecards/bulk/route.ts` — the bulk approve/reject + edit-request + flag-exception handler; both loops run inside one interactive `database.$transaction`). **(1) `processEditRequests`** — was a `for` loop issuing `tx.timeEntry.findUnique({ where:{tenantId_id:{tenantId,id:editRequest.timeEntryId}}, select:{employeeId} })` PER edit request (N reads) before a serial `tx.timecardEditRequest.findFirst` + update/create per request. Now ONE `tx.timeEntry.findMany({ where:{tenantId, id:{ in: editRequests.map(r=>r.timeEntryId) }}, select:{id,employeeId} })` → `Map<id,employeeId>` before the loop; the per-request lookup is an in-memory `Map.get`. **2N → N+1** (the N `timecardEditRequest.findFirst` + update/create stay serial). **(2) `processExceptionFlags`** — was a `for` loop issuing `tx.timeEntry.findUnique({…, select:{notes}})` + `tx.timeEntry.updateMany` PER flag (appending to `notes`). Now groups flags by `timeEntryId`, ONE `tx.timeEntry.findMany({…, select:{id,notes}})` → `Map`, then ONE `updateMany` per unique entry with the accumulated note string. **N reads → 1, N writes → unique-count.** **Why the probe's stronger "2N→2" claim was corrected (correctness-first):** `timecardEditRequest.findFirst` in (1) CANNOT be naively batched — a `create` in iteration K is visible to iteration K+1's `findFirst` for the SAME `timeEntryId` (the route's de-dup semantics: one edit request per time entry), so a pre-loop snapshot would create DUPLICATE edit requests if the body held duplicate `timeEntryId`s; kept serial. And the `notes` read in (2) is read-after-write dependent for a duplicate `timeEntryId` (each `updateMany` mutates the `notes` the next iteration re-reads → sequential-append accumulation), so a naive batch would LOSE appends; the group-by-`timeEntryId` + JS-accumulate produces a byte-identical final notes string in one write per entry (pinned by a dedicated dup-timeEntryId test). **Parity (verified by code read):** `findUnique` does NOT filter `deletedAt` → neither does the batched `findMany` (validated entries are non-deleted upstream; a soft-deleted row's `notes` is read but the `updateMany`'s `deletedAt:null` filter no-ops it, same as before); `findUnique→null` skip matched by a `Map.get→undefined` check (`=== undefined`, NOT truthiness — an empty-string `employeeId` would otherwise diverge). **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/timecards/bulk.test.ts` (**5/5 green** — the FIRST test for this route, which had ZERO coverage) pinning (1) the edit-requests N→1 collapse (`timeEntry.findMany` exactly 2 calls = validate + batch, the batch carrying `select:{id,employeeId}` + `id.in:[3 ids]`; `findFirst` serial ×2 for the 2 valid requests with the missing-entry request skipped before `findFirst`; update-vs-create routing + `editRequestCount:3`), (2) the exception-flags N→1 collapse (one batched notes `findMany` + one `updateMany` per distinct entry incl. the null-base→`""` prefix shape), (3) duplicate-`timeEntryId` accumulation correctness (two flags for one entry → ONE `updateMany` with `"base [EXCEPTION: A] a1 [EXCEPTION: B] b1"`), (4) 401-before-transaction, (5) 400 empty-`timeEntryIds`. Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **14 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `timecards/bulk/route.ts` or the test** (the 14 = kitchen/equipment/list ×3 + staff/shifts nullable-`locationId` cluster ×6 + auto-assignment ×2 + manifest-runtime `ai-suggestions` ×4 — all documented pre-existing); biome clean on both files; code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#14 REMAINS OPEN** — four read-preload/N+1-collapses now shipped (inventory-import, outbox-publish infra-write, events/documents/parse menu-import, timecards/bulk); the remaining #14 sites are governed-WRITE batching on DOMAIN entities (allergen nested O(guests×dishes) warnings, payroll/timecards per-shift, proposal-automation per-event, staff/availability per-pattern) — BLOCKED on the runtime rework (manifest runtime not concurrent-safe, NEEDS-RYAN shared with #18/#25). Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is structural (2N→N+1 + N→1 read round-trips on every bulk timecard approve-with-edits/flags, inside one tx) regardless of measured magnitude. Search: #14 timecards bulk read N+1, processEditRequests findUnique→findMany batch, processExceptionFlags group-by-timeEntryId notes accumulation, findUnique no-deletedAt-filter parity.

### 15. `[RESOLVED 2026-07-12]` Marketing analytics SQL `GROUP BY`
- **What:** Push the in-memory JS aggregation of email logs + leads into SQL.
- **Why / evidence:** `marketing/analytics/route.ts:34-88` does unbounded `emailLog` + `lead` `findMany` materialized into memory for JS aggregation (could be 100k+ rows). The SMS query in the same file already does the SQL `GROUP BY` correctly — a repo pattern to copy.
- **Fix:** Rewrite the email/lead aggregation as SQL `GROUP BY` mirroring the existing SMS query.
- **Scope:** `route`
- **Acceptance check:** No unbounded materialization; row count read is O(groups); before/after on the marketing analytics route.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-12, RESOLVED):** Replaced the two unbounded `findMany` (whole-window `emailLog` + `lead` materialized into JS, counted via `.filter`/`.reduce`) with indexed SQL `GROUP BY` queries returning O(groups) rows — mirroring the existing `tenant_admin.sms_logs` query already in the file. The `Promise.all` now runs 7 reads: 5 `$queryRaw` aggregates + the 2 small config `findMany` (`emailWorkflow`, `smsAutomationRule`, which stay — they are bounded config, not metric rows). **Cross-schema reality (verified this turn against `manifest.prisma`/`infra.prisma`):** `email_logs` is in schema **`tenant_admin`** (`infra.prisma:615`, filters on `sent_at`, columns `tenant_id`/`workflow_id`/`status` enum `email_status`); `leads` is in a **different** schema **`tenant_crm`** (`manifest.prisma:3368`, filters on `created_at` + `deleted_at IS NULL`); `sms_logs` is `tenant_admin`. Raw SQL is therefore schema-qualified (`tenant_admin.email_logs`, `tenant_crm.leads`). **Metric parity preserved exactly** (response shape unchanged): email `totalSent`=Σstatus counts; `opened`=`opened`+`delivered` counts (delivered-counted-as-opened behavior preserved deliberately — `openRate` has always included it); `bounced`=`bounced` count; per-workflow `sent`/`opened` via `COUNT(*) FILTER (WHERE status IN ('opened','delivered'))`, null `workflow_id`→`unlinked`; leads `totalLeads`=Σstatus, `convertedLeads`=`converted` count, `leadsBySource` groups by `source` with null/`""`→`manual` (matches the prior `l.source || "manual"`); SMS unchanged. Status literals (`'opened'`/`'delivered'`/`'bounced'`/`'converted'`) are hardcoded enum values, not user input → safe inside the SQL text; tenantId/startDate/now are bound via the `${...}` tagged-template parameters (same as the SMS query). **Bonus:** the refactor deleted the old `leads.filter((l) => l.status === "converted")` line, removing the pre-existing TS2367 no-overlap typecheck error at `marketing/analytics/route.ts:100` (the `LeadStatus` enum vs `"converted"` mismatch flagged in "Pre-existing issues noticed") — SQL handles it. **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/analytics/marketing-analytics.test.ts` (7/7 green) following the `analytics.test.ts` mock pattern — pins auth-guard, metric math from grouped output (incl. the `leadsBySource` null+`""`→`manual` merge and per-workflow join with a no-logs workflow → `openRate:null`), empty-aggregate zeros/nulls, error propagation, and a **regression guard** `expect(database.$queryRaw).toHaveBeenCalledTimes(5)` + a mock with NO `emailLog`/`lead` accessors (a regression to unbounded `findMany` would throw). Reusable: the [[parallelization-mock-order-pattern]] — the 5 `$queryRaw` tagged templates are queued in the route's `Promise.all` destructure order (email-status, email-workflow, lead-status, lead-source, sms), so `mockResolvedValueOnce` is sequenced to match. Gates: focused test 7/7 green; `apps/api` typecheck **16 errors = baseline−1** (the removed marketing line), **ZERO in `marketing/analytics/route.ts`**; no schema/manifest touched → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **NOTICED (documented, not fixed — out of #15 scope):** the marketing route has **no try/catch** around its GET body (unlike the sibling finance/kitchen/staff analytics routes, which return a structured JSON 500), so a DB error rejects unstructured — the test pins current behavior via `rejects.toThrow`; a future small hardening pass could add the try/catch for parity. Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (item #1); the win is structural (O(rows)→O(groups) memory + latency) regardless of measured magnitude.

### 16. `[PARTIAL 2026-07-13: local-copy dedupe + 30s cache shipped; GET-write elimination remains #2(a)]` Analytics write-on-read fix (duplicated resolver)
- **What:** Remove the findFirst-then-conditional-create on a GET in the analytics routes (and dedupe the **duplicated** `getTenantIdForOrg` — **(4th rev, 2026-07-12)** 2 local copies, not 3).
- **Why / evidence:** `analytics/events/advanced/route.ts:7-24` and `analytics/events/profitability/route.ts:7-24` — `getTenantIdForOrg` does `findFirst` + conditional `create` on a GET (write-on-read; also a race). Correctness + perf.
  - `[CORRECTED 4th rev, 2026-07-12]` **`getTenantIdForOrg` is DUPLICATED (not triplicated)** — only `advanced` + `profitability` define a local copy; the CSV-export routes IMPORT the shared module (no local copy). Both carry the same write-on-read race. (Root cause + dedupe target lives in item #2; this item covers the analytics-specific GET-write removal.)
- **Fix:** Make the tenant resolution read-only on GET (create elsewhere, e.g. first write); or use an upsert anchored to a non-GET path. Collapse the **two** local copies into the shared, memoized resolver from item #2.
- **Scope:** `route`
- **Acceptance check:** GET analytics routes issue no writes; no race; the two local copies are gone; before/after measured.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, local-copy dedupe + 30s cache SHIPPED):** Collapsed the two local `getTenantIdForOrg` copies in `GET /api/analytics/events/advanced` + `GET /api/analytics/events/profitability` into the shared cached resolver (`apps/api/app/lib/tenant.ts:getTenantIdForOrg`, the 30s-TTL `tenantCache` shipped in #2). These two were the ONLY analytics routes still carrying a local copy — verified this turn via `rg "function getTenantIdForOrg|getTenantIdForOrg ="` over `apps/api/app/api/analytics`: all 8 sibling routes (`bottlenecks`, `menu-engineering`, `staff/employees/[id]`, `staff/summary`, `kitchen`, `consolidated`, `multi-location`, `finance`) already `import { getTenantIdForOrg } from "@/app/lib/tenant"`. Both local copies were byte-identical AND **uncached** (`account.findFirst` + conditional `account.create` on the primary `database` on EVERY GET), so every advanced/profitability dashboard load paid the full findFirst (+ create on first-ever hit) on the primary — the worst write-amplification of any analytics route. After the swap they hit the shared `tenantCache` → after the first resolution per server process, write-on-read stops entirely for the 30s TTL window (the cache is org-keyed, immutable mapping, no cross-tenant leak). Signature/return identical → call sites unchanged. Also dropped the now-unused `database` import from both routes (each uses ONLY `analyticsDatabase` for its OLAP reads — `database` was referenced solely by the deleted local provisioning fn) and removed the now-obsolete *"OLAP reads route to the read replica; the account provisioning write below stays on the primary `database`"* comment (it described the removed local write; the primary-vs-replica rationale now lives in the shared resolver + `packages/database/analytics-database.ts`). The shared resolver uses the primary `database` for the account write, so the write still lands on the primary exactly as before (a read replica rejects writes) — the swap is semantically identical re: which DB the write hits. **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/analytics/{events-advanced,events-profitability}.test.ts` (**8/8 green** — the FIRST tests for these routes) pinning (1) the dedupe — `getTenantIdForOrg` (mocked from `@/app/lib/tenant`) is called exactly once with the authenticated `orgId`, AND the local-provisioning methods `account.findFirst`/`account.create` are NEVER called (the regression guard: re-adding the local copy would call them → test fails loudly), (2) the resolved `tenantId` is threaded into every OLAP read (advanced: all 4 `$queryRawUnsafe` calls bind it as `$1`; profitability: the tagged-template `$queryRaw` call's 2nd arg), (3) the mapped response shape (advanced summary/eventType/topMenuItems/clientPreferences; profitability monthly-row numeric conversion), (4) the 401 auth guard before any DB read, (5) profitability's structured-500 + `captureException` + `log.error` error path. Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `advanced/route.ts`, `profitability/route.ts`, or either test** (the import swap + dropped `database` import type cleanly); Biome = **zero errors** on the 4 touched files (7 PRE-EXISTING warnings in the untouched `advanced/route.ts` GET body — `noNestedTernary` at `:424`, `noExcessiveCognitiveComplexity`, etc. — none in the edited import region); code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#16 REMAINS PARTIAL — the "GET analytics routes issue no writes" acceptance half is NOT met by this increment:** the shared `getTenantIdForOrg` STILL does `findFirst` + conditional `create` (write-on-read) on a cache MISS — eliminating that is **#2(a)'s scope** (needs an `account.slug` `@@unique` via `manifest/source` + migration, OR an upsert, OR a dedicated read-only resolver design decision so the other 120 call sites' auto-provisioning behavior is not changed). This increment shipped the dedupe + caching (the "two local copies are gone" + "no duplicate-write race within the TTL window" acceptance halves); the residual write-on-read affects ALL 10 analytics routes + ~120 other sites via the shared resolver, not just these 2, so closing it belongs to #2(a). Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is structural (2 uncached GET routes → shared 30s cache, + ~34 lines of duplicated provisioning code removed) regardless of measured magnitude.
