- **Implementation log (2026-07-14, SHIPPED: recalculate waterfall collapse — the parallelization the `1a17a2c94` entry above teed up as "separate atomic family"):** `POST /api/events/profitability/commands/recalculate` ran 3 serial independent reads after the existence gate — `eventBudget.findFirst` + `event.findUnique` (inside `calculateBudgetTotals`) then `cateringOrder.findMany` (inside `calculateActualTotals`), all keyed only on `(tenantId, eventId)` = **gate + 3 rounds = 4**. Collapsed to **2 rounds** (gate + one parallel wave): (1) the two `calculateBudgetTotals` reads are now `const [eventBudget, event] = await Promise.all([...])`; (2) the two helper calls are now `const [budget, actuals] = await Promise.all([calculateBudgetTotals(...), calculateActualTotals(...)])` → all three reads dispatch in one synchronous tick after the gate. Reads are pure (no shared mutable state) → concurrent dispatch safe; `Promise.all` array order `[eventBudget, event]` and `[budget, actuals]` preserves the prior synchronous DB-call order. Budget/actual math byte-identical (only await structure changed). **Verification:** added 1 discriminating concurrency test to `apps/api/__tests__/events/profitability-recalculate.test.ts` (now **5/5**) — holds `eventBudget.findFirst` pending and asserts `event.findUnique` + `cateringOrder.findMany` fire while it is unresolved (impossible in the serial layout → a revert times out at `vi.waitFor`); the existing 4 select/math/401/404 tests pass unchanged (order-independent `mockResolvedValue`). ### 18. `[PARTIAL 2026-07-13: convert-to-po + prep-lists/create $transaction 120s-ceiling caps shipped]` Transaction scope — N governed writes inside one interactive `$transaction`
- **What:** Shrink the long-running interactive transactions that hold a connection + (in one case) a `FOR UPDATE` row lock while doing N serial governed round-trips.
- **Why / evidence (file:line):**
  - `kitchen/prep-lists/save-db/route.ts:58-139` — `$transaction` over `PrepList` create + N `PrepListItem` governed `runCommand` in a double for-loop (default 5s tx timeout risk on large lists).
  - `kitchen/recipes/[id]/composite/update-with-version/service.ts:536` + `kitchen/recipes/composite/create-with-version/route.ts:171` — `$transaction` over recipe update + version create + N ingredient + N step governed creates — **35+ serial governed round-trips in one tx**.
  - command-board commit (`command-board/[boardId]/commit/route.ts:82-98`) + `commit-event-board-drafts.ts:248-269` — `FOR UPDATE` row lock + reads active `eventStaff` inside the locked tx. **(4th rev, 2026-07-12)** `loadActiveStaff` is scoped to the ONE event's staff (bounded) — NOT "ALL active eventStaff" as previously framed; the lock-hold concern is real but bounded, so this sub-item's severity is demoted.
  - `[MOVED 4th rev, 2026-07-12]` **`apps/api/lib/manifest/execute-command.ts:318-363`** — the generic manifest **batch** endpoint's `$transaction` pool-exhaustion vector (one tx over all N user ops, timeout up to 120s) has been **SPLIT OUT into a standalone foundational-tier item (#29, availability-grade)** rather than left in this MED code-fix item. This item retains only the in-tx governed-write code cleanups below.
  - `[NEW, 2nd-rev]` More governed-write-in-tx sites of the same shape: `procurement/requisitions/[id]/convert-to-po/route.ts:157-224` (per-line `PurchaseOrderItem` create), `kitchen/ai/bulk-generate/prep-tasks/service.ts:413-455` (N generated-task creates), `kitchen/prep-lists/commands/create/route.ts:129-170` (second prep-list path), `apps/api/lib/payroll/manifest-payroll-data-source.ts:166` (`PayrollRun.create` + `process` + per-line-item governed commands — timeout already raised above the 5s default because the governed path is heavy).
- **Fix:** Move governed writes out of the long tx where the constitution allows, or batch them; cap the generic batch endpoint's tx size/timeout; bound the in-lock reads (e.g. precompute the `eventStaff` set before acquiring the lock, or scope it to the board's event).
- **Scope:** `route`
- **Acceptance check:** Each cited tx holds its connection/lock for O(1) or O(chunks) round-trips, not O(N); governance semantics preserved; before/after on `recipes/composite/create-with-version` + command-board commit.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, convert-to-po + prep-lists/create $transaction 120s-ceiling caps SHIPPED — the two #29 siblings):** The two bespoke orchestration routes #29 explicitly named ("Two bespoke siblings replicate the same 120s-capped multi-op-`$transaction` pattern … item #18 territory; same fix shape applies") now use the proven `batchTransactionTimeout(opCount)` helper (capped at the 30s app-wide tx ceiling, `apps/api/lib/manifest/batch-timeout.ts`, shipped in #29) instead of the inline `Math.min(items.length*2000+base, 120_000)` scaling that could pin a `max:20` pool connection for up to 120s and starve every other request (Prisma P2024 after the 10s `maxWait`). **`apps/api/app/api/procurement/requisitions/[id]/convert-to-po/route.ts`** (PurchaseOrder.create → N×PurchaseOrderItem.create → PurchaseOrder.updateTotals → PurchaseRequisition.convertToPo = N+3 governed writes): `timeout: batchTransactionTimeout(items.length + 3)` (opCount = N line items + the 3 fixed governed writes the old `+10_000` base was accounting for); the OLD `Math.min(100*2000+10_000, 120_000)` = 120s → NEW `batchTransactionTimeout(103)` = 30s. **`apps/api/app/api/kitchen/prep-lists/commands/create/route.ts`** (PrepList.create → N×PrepListItem.create): `timeout: batchTransactionTimeout(items.length)` — an EXACT drop-in for the old `Math.min(items.length*2000+5000, 120_000)` (only the ceiling changes 120s→30s; small-batch headroom byte-identical). Both keep `maxWait: 10_000` (connection-acquisition wait, unrelated to the duration cap — mirrors #29's `execute-command.ts:364` wiring). **Scope discipline (a sweep, NOT left as a guess):** `rg "120[_]?000" apps/api/{app,lib}` found exactly TWO more `timeout: 120_000` sites, both deliberately-FLAT heavy-operation timeouts (NOT the scaling pool-exhaustion vector) and already classified by #18's own evidence — `apps/api/lib/payroll/manifest-payroll-data-source.ts:239` (PayrollRun.create + process + per-line-item governed commands; "#18: timeout already raised above the 5s default because the governed path is heavy") and `apps/api/app/api/command-board/[boardId]/commit/route.ts:79` (a `FOR UPDATE` row-lock commit scoped to ONE event; #18 4th rev DEMOTED its severity as "real but bounded"). Capping either at 30s risks breaking a real payroll run / board commit, so they are LEFT AS-IS — their long hold is deliberate, not the unbounded-batch vector #29/#18-siblings target. The remaining #18 sites (`recipes/[id]/composite/update-with-version/service.ts:536` + `recipes/composite/create-with-version/route.ts:171` 35+ serial round-trips; `prep-lists/save-db/route.ts:58-139`) are a DIFFERENT shape (latency from many round-trips, not a 120s ceiling) needing round-trip batching, not a timeout cap. **Verification:** added the FIRST focused tests for both routes — `apps/api/__tests__/procurement/requisitions/convert-to-po-tx-timeout.test.ts` (3/3) + `apps/api/__tests__/kitchen/prep-lists-create-tx-timeout.test.ts` (3/3) — each pinning the discriminating guard: a 100-item request yields `timeout === batchTransactionTimeout(...)` = the 30s ceiling (the OLD inline formula gave 120_000), a small request gets proportional headroom BELOW the ceiling (convert-to-po also pins opCount = items+3, guarding the fixed-write accounting), and an auth failure (InvariantError) returns 401 before any `$transaction`. Existing `requisition-end-to-end.test.ts` **17/17 green** (zero regression). Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in either route or test**; code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal. **Pre-existing RED noticed this turn (documented, NOT a regression, NOT mine):** `governance/no-raw-sql-writes.test.ts` fails because its `KNOWN_VIOLATIONS` allowlist (last audited 2026-06-07) has STALE path prefixes — it omits the `(events)`/`(operations)` route groups now in the filesystem (e.g. allowlist `app/app/(authenticated)/events/importer.ts` vs real `app/app/(authenticated)/(events)/events/importer.ts`), so `startsWith` no longer matches the 26 flagged apps/app files (all KNOWN intentional raw-SQL sites; ZERO overlap with this change — these routes are in apps/api). Updating that allowlist is a separate, path-verification-bound maintenance task, not a #18 db-perf concern. No tag (precondition false: 16+9 pre-existing tsc; repo `v0.12.X` tags are manifest-release versioning). **#18 REMAINS PARTIAL** — the two #29 siblings are capped; composite-recipe round-trip batching, payroll/commit deliberate-flat timeouts, and prep-lists/save-db are separate shapes for separate increments. Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is availability (a large convert/prep-list create can no longer pin a pool connection for 120s) regardless of measured magnitude.

- **(2026-07-13 investigation — composite-recipe round-trip batching ASSESSED, DEFERRED on governed-runtime concurrency):** Re-investigated the two composite sites this turn (`composite/create-with-version/route.ts:171` + `[id]/composite/update-with-version/service.ts:536`). Structure CONFIRMED (don't re-read): each `$transaction` builds a tx-bound runtime via `createManifestRuntime({ user, prismaOverride: tx })`, then runs Recipe.create → RecipeVersion.create → a `for` loop of N `runtime.runCommand("create",...,{entityName:"RecipeIngredient"})` → a `for` loop of N `runtime.runCommand("create",...,{entityName:"RecipeStep"})` = 2+N+N serial governed round-trips (update-with-version factors the two loops into `createIngredients`/`createSteps` helpers). The ingredient + step creates are PAYLOAD-DRIVEN (sortOrder from the pre-computed `allIngredients` array / `stepNumber` from input, ids via `crypto.randomUUID()`) — NO shared counter, NO inter-item ID dependency → structurally parallelizable. **`runManifestBatch` does NOT compose** with the outer tx — it opens its OWN `$transaction` (`execute-command.ts:319`) and runs ops through `runManifestCommandCore` (sequentially); calling it inside the outer tx would nest interactive transactions (Prisma/Neon rejects). The viable batching is therefore `Promise.all` over the governed `runtime.runCommand` calls INSIDE the existing tx (option A). **Concurrent-in-tx is PROVEN safe for RAW Prisma `tx.*`** by the `inventory/purchase-orders/[id]/complete` precedent (and reused this turn for #25c) — BUT that precedent does NOT cover governed dispatch: concurrent `runtime.runCommand` (which internally issues audit/event/outbox/constraint writes through `tx`) has NO precedent in this repo (`runManifestBatch` deliberately runs sequentially). Risk if parallelized without verification: concurrent governed commands racing on shared runtime state or outbox/audit writes inside the tx → possible corrupted recipe-version data. **Defer until** a read of `createManifestRuntime`/`runCommand` internals confirms the runtime is stateless-per-command under concurrent dispatch (or each command creates its own runtime instance / the constraint-evaluation has no cross-row shared state). Existing tests: `update-with-version-route.test.ts` exists; `create-with-version` has NO test. The ONLY remaining unknown is the runtime-concurrency question — the code structure + the runManifestBatch-non-composition finding above are settled.

- **(2026-07-13, governed-runtime-concurrency question RESOLVED — definitively closes the #18/#14/#25 governed-write-batching blocker):** Read the runtime the deferral above gated on (`manifest/runtime/src/manifest-runtime-factory.ts`). **Answer: the runtime is NOT stateless-per-command — concurrent `runtime.runCommand` on a shared runtime instance is UNSAFE.** Evidence: `buildStoreProvider` (factory `:673`) is called ONCE per `createManifestRuntime` (NOT once per `runCommand`, despite its inline comment at `:516-521` claiming "called once per runCommand") and constructs a single `readCache = createRequestStoreReadCache()` (`:522`) shared across EVERY `runCommand` on that runtime instance — its own comment frames it as "the window in which the trigger, parent-context resolver, and fired reactions all re-load the same subjects." Separately, the engine's evaluation budget is re-entrant/shared across a command's whole cascade (`:1929-1938`). So a `Promise.all` of governed `runtime.runCommand` calls on the SAME runtime (the batching shape #18/#14/#25 need) shares two pieces of mutable per-instance state — the request-scoped read cache + the eval budget — and each command's ~65-entry middleware pipeline (`:930-1871`) issues store loads that would contaminate across concurrent commands (stale/cross-command cached reads feeding guards + constraint evaluation). **Conclusion:** governed writes inside a `$transaction` MUST stay SERIAL until either (a) the runtime is reworked to build a fresh storeProvider/readCache per `runCommand` (or per-command runtime instances), or (b) the native companion-runtime rewrite the factory's own `NEEDS-RYAN` deletion-target header (`:4-13`) ships. **DO NOT re-attempt concurrent governed dispatch** on the current factory — this is settled, not an open question. The raw-Prisma `tx.*` concurrent-in-transaction precedent (`inventory/purchase-orders/[id]/complete`, reused by #25c) does NOT extend to governed `runtime.runCommand` — it covers only stateless raw Prisma ops, not the stateful runtime. **Implications:** #18 composite-recipe (2+N+N governed creates) stays serial; #14 `kitchen/allergens/detect-conflicts` O(guests×dishes) governed-warning writes stay serial (its READ side is already clean — verified this turn: 3 batched queries, an event guard + `eventGuest.findMany` + a single `$queryRaw` dishes JOIN; the cost is purely the governed WRITE loop); #25 governed-write batching stays serial. Verified 2026-07-14 by reading the full files: the recipes composite (create-with-version + [id]/composite/update-with-version/service) and prep-lists/save-db "35+ serial round-trips" are overwhelmingly GOVERNED writes (runtime.runCommand / runManifestCommandCore on Recipe/RecipeVersion/RecipeIngredient/RecipeStep/PrepList/PrepListItem) — NOT batchable (manifest runtime is not concurrent-safe on a shared runtime); only a negligible raw-Prisma read fraction is batchable. This residue stays BLOCKED on the NEEDS-RYAN governed-runtime rework (shared with #14/#25).

### 19. `[PARTIAL 2026-07-14: inventory low-stock + run-sheet + nutrition-labels + logistics/vehicles + logistics/dispatch board select (2026-07-15) + ai/suggestions getContextData + events/export/csv select + ai/summaries waterfall + ai/bulk-tasks/confirm parallelization + inventory-forecasting alerts N+1 batch SHIPPED; 2026-07-14: shipments/route.ts list findMany narrowed with top-level select dropping signatureData base64 blob + reference — 85cfff5bf; 2026-07-15: shipments/[id]/route.ts detail GET include→select dropping the signatureData base64 blob (separate-blob pattern — the response exposes signature=signatureText and NEVER exposed signatureData, so the blob was pure read-side waste; HTTP response byte-identical) + items.item narrowed from the full InventoryItem row to {id,name,item_number}; regression guard apps/api/__tests__/logistics/shipments/shipment-detail-select.test.ts (3/3 green); tsc clean in touched files (apps/api baseline 14, ZERO new); last shipments read path now narrowed (list + tracking + detail). NOTE (ruled out this pass): events/contracts/[id]/signatures/route.ts:201 list is NOT a clean signatureData drop — its response map copies signatureData at :215 (SignatureListResponse declares it), so unlike shipments it IS exposed; dropping it is a response-contract change (needs frontend-render audit), not an autonomous select-narrowing]` MED cluster: event / AI / kitchen / logistics over-fetch + N+1
- **What:** Bundle of medium-impact route cleanups: parallelize independent reads, add `take:1` / `select`, push JS filters to SQL; fold in the corrected low-severity findings.
- **Why / evidence:**
  - ~~`events/[eventId]/run-sheet/route.ts:66-157` (8 sequential queries; `recipeVersion.findMany` `:93` missing `take:1`, fetches all versions and picks latest in JS)~~

  > **(4th rev, 2026-07-12 re-correction):** run-sheet is actually **~8-10 sequential awaits** — the 2nd-rev "6 not 8" correction was itself off (direction holds: it's a MED-cluster waterfall). Also `ai/suggestions` `getContextData` runs **8 sequential awaits** (more than framed).

- **Implementation log (2026-07-12, inventory low-stock correctness SHIPPED):** Fixed the `inventory/items` GET low-stock filter — a dual correctness bug that made the feature completely non-functional. Root cause: stock status compares `quantity_on_hand` against `reorder_level`, a **column-to-column predicate Prisma `where` cannot express**. The prior code set `where.quantityOnHand = { lte: 0 }` for `low_stock` (fetching out-of-stock rows) then JS-post-filtered, so `stock_status=low_stock` **ALWAYS returned an empty list**; `in_stock` used `{ gt: 0 }` which **leaked low-stock items**; and the `low_stock` `total` used the post-filter page count (always 0 → broken pagination). Fix (`apps/api/app/api/inventory/items/route.ts`): when `stock_status` is set, resolve the matching page of IDs + the total via parameterized `$queryRaw` SQL whose `CASE WHEN quantity_on_hand <= 0 THEN 'out_of_stock' WHEN quantity_on_hand <= reorder_level THEN 'low_stock' ELSE 'in_stock' END = $status` mirrors `calculateStockStatus` exactly for all three statuses, then hydrate full rows via `findMany({ id: { in } })` (preserving Prisma's camelCase Decimal mapping the response shape depends on) and remap to the SQL-determined page order. Count is a separate raw query (always-correct total — no window-function empty-page edge). The non-stock path is byte-for-byte unchanged. Added module-scope `mapInventoryItemWithStatus` (pure transform — the JS stock post-filter is gone, SQL owns filtering) + `buildStockStatusConditions` (parameterized; tenant/search/category/supplier/fsa/tags + the CASE; mirrors the Prisma `where` filters). Imported `Prisma` as a value (for `Prisma.sql`/`Prisma.join`), matching the `timecards/route.ts` pattern. **Verification:** `apps/api/__tests__/inventory/inventory-item-crud.test.ts` **69/69 green** — added a `low_stock` regression test (pins the always-empty bug is fixed), an empty-match edge test (total 0, no hydration query fires), and converted the `out_of_stock`/`in_stock` tests from implementation-assertions on `where.quantityOnHand` to behavioral assertions on the SQL path (`findMany` hydrates by `id`, no qty predicate); the no-filter "calculate stock status" test + all pagination/search/category/supplier/fsa/tags/error tests pass unchanged (non-stock path untouched). `apps/api` `tsc --noEmit` **ZERO errors** in the touched files (full apps/api typecheck clean). Code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#19 REMAINS OPEN** — only the inventory low-stock sub-item shipped this increment; run-sheet ~8-10 sequential awaits, AI-summary dependency chain, nutrition-labels per-recipe N+1, logistics `driver.count`→groupBy, and events/export over-fetch are still pending. **bulk-assignment null-filter sub-item is SCHEMA-GATED, not a code fix:** `ScheduleShift.employeeId` is **non-nullable** (`employeeId String @map("employee_id") @db.Uuid`, no `?` — verified `manifest.prisma:5276`), so the intended `employeeId: null` ("unassigned shifts") filter is impossible and the route already carries an explicit TODO documenting it. Fixing requires making `employeeId` nullable (a `manifest/source` schema change + migration), not a query tweak; **removed from the mechanical-fix scope** (moved to NEEDS-SCHEMA). Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (item #1); the win is correctness (a broken user-facing filter now works) regardless of measured magnitude.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-12, run-sheet SHIPPED):** Collapsed the flagship `GET /api/events/[eventId]/run-sheet` (`apps/api/app/api/events/[eventId]/run-sheet/route.ts`) — a flagship event-detail route (every event's prep/service run sheet) — from a **10-deep serial waterfall** (`event` → `battleBoard` → `eventDishLinks` → `dish` → `recipeVersion` → `recipeIngredient` → `ingredient` → `eventStaff` → `staffMember` → `eventTimeline`) into **6 rounds** by respecting the real data-dependency graph:
  - **Tier 0 — `Promise.all([battleBoard, eventDishLinks, eventStaff, eventTimeline])`:** all four depend ONLY on `(eventId, tenantId)`, never on each other or on the `event` row (beyond the 404 guard). In the prior serial layout `eventStaff`/`eventTimeline` ran 8th/10th — *behind the entire dish chain* — so this single batch is the biggest win.
  - **Tier 1 — `Promise.all([dish, staffMember])`:** `dish` depends on `eventDishLinks`, `staffMember` on `staffAssignments`; the two chains are independent of each other, so the staff fetch now races the dish fetch instead of trailing the whole recipe chain.
  - **Inherently-serial dish/recipe chain preserved:** `recipeVersion` → `recipeIngredient` → `ingredient` each needs IDs from the prior step (genuine data dependency — not parallelizable); left serial.
  - **Correctness sub-fix (the plan's `take:1` sub-item):** `recipeVersion.findMany` previously fetched **every** version then JS-picked the latest (`:108-116` dedup map). Added `distinct: ["recipeId"]` (paired with the existing `orderBy: { versionNumber: "desc" }`) so the read returns **one row per recipe (the latest)** instead of all versions. The dedup map is kept as the correctness floor (with `orderBy desc` it is idempotent under `distinct`); literal `take:1` would have been WRONG here — it returns one row total across all recipes, not one-per-recipe.
  - Query shapes (`where`/`select`/`orderBy`), every `Map` (`dishById`, `latestVersionByRecipe`, `ingredientsByVersion`, `ingredientNameById`, `staffMemberById`), the shopping-list scaling aggregation, and the response shape are byte-identical; only the await structure + the `distinct` bound changed. The `.length > 0 ? findMany : Promise.resolve([])` guards are preserved (avoids pointless `where:{id:{in:[]}}` round-trips).
  - **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/events/run-sheet.test.ts` (**6/6 green**) — the FIRST test for this route — pinning (1) Tier-0 concurrency via a controlled-pending `battleBoard` (eventTimeline/eventStaff/eventDish all fire while it is pending — impossible in the old serial layout), (2) Tier-1 concurrency via a controlled-pending `dish` (staffMember fires while dish is pending), (3) the full happy path incl. **latest-per-recipe** (two versions supplied → v2 used) + **scaled shopping-list** aggregation (servings/yield scale applied in the list, raw qty on `dish.recipe.ingredients`) + staff + timeline enrichment, (4) battle-board vs event-menu `source`, (5) 401 before any read, (6) 404 before any Tier-0 read. Events test dir **279/279 green** (was 273 + 6 new; zero regression). Gates: `apps/api` `tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO new** (none in `run-sheet/route.ts` or the test — the `Promise.resolve([])` ternary type-inference and `distinct` are clean); code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#19 REMAINS OPEN** — inventory low-stock + run-sheet shipped this initiative; the AI-summary dependency chain (only last 2 parallelizable), `kitchen/nutrition-labels/list` per-recipe N+1 (2N+1), `logistics/vehicles/list` `driver.count`→`groupBy`, and `events/export/csv` over-fetch (`take:5000` no `select`) are still pending. Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is structural (10→6 rounds + a bounded recipeVersion read) regardless of measured magnitude.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-12, nutrition-labels N+1 SHIPPED):** Collapsed the `GET /api/kitchen/nutrition-labels/list` (`apps/api/app/api/kitchen/nutrition-labels/list/route.ts`) per-recipe N+1. **Before:** `recipe.findMany` + a `Promise.all` over recipes doing `recipeVersion.findFirst` (latest version) + `recipeIngredient.count` per recipe = **2N+1 round-trips** (2 queries PER recipe — a list of 100 recipes fired 201 DB queries). **After (3 round-trips total, independent of N):** (1) `recipe.findMany` (unchanged — tenant + optional recipeId filter, `select id/name/createdAt`, `orderBy name asc`); (2) `recipeVersion.findMany` with `distinct: ["recipeId"]` + `orderBy: { versionNumber: "desc" }` → **one row per recipe (the latest version)** in a single query (same `distinct`-for-latest-per-group pattern the run-sheet fix established); (3) `recipeIngredient.groupBy({ by: ["recipeVersionId"], _count: { recipeVersionId: true } })` → ingredient counts for ALL latest versions in one query. A `Map<recipeId, version>` and `Map<versionId, count>` rehydrate per-recipe; recipes with no version default to `ingredientCount: 0`; versions with zero ingredients are absent from the `groupBy` result and default to `0`. The `groupBy` is **guarded** (`if versionIds.length > 0`) so the empty-version case skips the third round-trip entirely (no pointless `in: []`). Response shape is byte-identical (`yield` = `Number(yieldQuantity)` or `null`; `hasNutritionData: true`; `createdAt` serialized to ISO by `NextResponse.json`). **Why it matters:** this route backs the nutrition-labels list screen — the per-recipe fan-out scaled linearly with the tenant's recipe catalog, so a busy kitchen with hundreds of recipes hit hundreds of round-trips on every page load. **Verification:** `apps/api/__tests__/kitchen/nutrition-labels-list.test.ts` **3/3 green** — the FIRST test for this route — a regression guard that (a) asserts the batched methods (`recipe.findMany`, `recipeVersion.findMany`, `recipeIngredient.groupBy`) are each called **once** while the per-row N+1 methods (`recipeVersion.findFirst`, `recipeIngredient.count`) are **never** called (fails loudly if reverted to the `Promise.all` map), (b) pins the full response shape incl. `yield` Number-conversion, null yield, missing-version→0, zero-ingredient-version→0, (c) pins the no-version edge (`groupBy` skipped when no versionIds), and (d) 401 before any DB read. Gates: `apps/api` `tsc --noEmit` — **touched file clean, ZERO new errors** (full run shows 19 errors, ALL pre-existing in untouched `manifest/runtime/src/bottleneck-detector/ai-suggestions.ts` TS2589/7006 — the separate "CI RED on typecheck since ~Jul 9" baseline; none in the nutrition-labels route or test); code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#19 REMAINS OPEN** — inventory low-stock + run-sheet + nutrition-labels shipped this initiative; still pending: AI-summary dependency chain (only last 2 parallelizable), `logistics/vehicles/list` `driver.count`→`groupBy`, `events/export/csv` over-fetch (`take:5000` no `select`), `events/budgets` `include:{lineItems}` over-fetch on list, `ai/bulk-tasks/confirm` serial for-of, `ai/suggestions` `eventStaff.findMany` no-filter + 2nd event query. (`staff/shifts/bulk-assignment` + command-board palette are separate / schema-gated.) Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is structural (2N+1→3 round-trips) regardless of measured magnitude.

- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, logistics/vehicles per-vehicle N+1 SHIPPED):** Collapsed the `GET /api/logistics/vehicles/list` (`apps/api/app/api/logistics/vehicles/list/route.ts`) per-vehicle count N+1 — a #19 MED-cluster sub-item. **Before:** `vehicle.findMany` (page) then a `Promise.all` over the page calling `database.driver.count({ where: { tenantId, vehicleId: vehicle.id, deletedAt: null, status: { not: "inactive" } } })` PER vehicle = **N count queries scaling with page size** (a page of 50 vehicles fired 50 `driver.count` round-trips). **After (1 round-trip regardless of page size):** one `database.driver.groupBy({ by: ["vehicleId"], where: { tenantId, deletedAt: null, status: { not: "inactive" }, vehicleId: { in: pageVehicleIds } }, _count: { vehicleId: true } })` + a `Map<vehicleId, count>` lookup; `assigned_drivers` reads `driverCountByVehicle.get(vehicle.id) ?? 0` (vehicles with 0 active drivers are absent from the groupBy result → Map miss → `0`, byte-identical to the prior `count ?? 0`). **`Driver.vehicleId` is nullable** (`String?`, `manifest.prisma:1649`), so the Map build guards `if (row.vehicleId !== null)` — the `in: pageVehicleIds` filter already excludes unassigned (null-vehicleId) drivers exactly as the prior per-vehicle `count` did (the old equality predicate `vehicleId: vehicle.id` could never match null either), so the result set is identical. **Empty-page guard** (`if (vehicleRecords.length > 0)`) skips the groupBy entirely → no pointless `in: []` round-trip on an empty/last page (matches the run-sheet + nutrition-labels precedent). Response shape byte-identical (`{ vehicles: [{…, assigned_drivers: number}], limit, offset }`). **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/logistics/vehicles-list.test.ts` (**3/3 green**) — the FIRST test pinning the groupBy path — a regression guard asserting `driver.count` is **NEVER** called and `driver.groupBy` is called **once** with the exact scoped args (`vehicleId: { in: [page ids] }`), plus the `assigned_drivers` mapping (vehicle-with-drivers → count, vehicle-without → 0 via Map miss), the empty-page no-op (groupBy skipped), and the 401 auth guard before any DB read. **Fixed the existing `apps/api/__tests__/logistics/logistics.test.ts` vehicles suite** (it mocked the now-removed per-vehicle `driver.count` and had no `driver.groupBy` mock → the non-empty-vehicles test threw → 500): added `groupBy: vi.fn()` to the `driver` mock and pointed the one non-empty-vehicles test at `driver.groupBy` (returns `[{ vehicleId: "v-002", _count: { vehicleId: 2 } }]`; v-001 absent → 0, mirroring the original 0-then-2 sequential count). Full logistics dir **87/87 green** (5 files, zero regression). Gates: `apps/api` `tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO new** (none in `vehicles/list/route.ts` or either test — the 16 are the known email-reminders/kitchen-equipment/staff-shifts/auto-assignment/manifest-runtime-ai-suggestions clusters); code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#19 REMAINS OPEN** — inventory low-stock + run-sheet + nutrition-labels + logistics/vehicles shipped this initiative; still pending: AI-summary dependency chain (only last 2 parallelizable), `events/export/csv` over-fetch (`take:5000` no `select`), `events/budgets` `include:{lineItems}` over-fetch on list, `ai/bulk-tasks/confirm` serial for-of, `ai/suggestions` `eventStaff.findMany` no-event-filter + redundant 2nd event query. The deleted `staffEvents`/`staffEventIdsFiltered`/`filteredStaffAssignments` machinery is gone; the return maps `staffAssignments` directly (the set is now exactly the in-window staff — byte-identical output shape). - **Implementation log (2026-07-13, ai/summaries waterfall SHIPPED):** Collapsed `getEventDataForSummary` (`apps/api/app/api/ai/summaries/[eventId]/route.ts`) — the GET that builds the event-briefing context for the AI summary — from **5 serial round-trips** into **2 dependency-respecting rounds** (the [[parallelization-mock-order-pattern]] technique; same shape as the ai/suggestions increment). **Before:** `event.findFirst` (existence guard) → `$queryRaw` event_dishes → `dish.findMany` (←dishIds) → `eventStaff.findMany` → `allergenWarning.findMany`, all serial. **After:** **Tier 0** `Promise.all([event, eventDishes, staffAssignments, allergenWarnings])` — all four keyed ONLY on `(tenantId, eventId)`; `eventDishes` is data-independent of the `event` row, so the plan's note ("the `$queryRaw` event_dishes step is ALSO data-independent of the `event.findFirst` guard result and could join a parallel batch — only `dish.findMany` truly waits on it") endorses batching it with the guard. **Tier 1** `dish.findMany` (← the event_dishes `dishIds` — genuine data dependency, stays after the batch). The `if (!event) throw` guard moved to AFTER the batch (the result is available once `Promise.all` resolves); on a rare 404 the three sibling reads fire wastefully, but the happy path (every successful summary) drops 5 serial rounds → 2. Query shapes (`where`/`include`/`select`/`orderBy`/the `$queryRaw` template) byte-identical; the `dishIds.length > 0` empty-guard is preserved (no pointless `in: []`); the response-building block is unchanged. **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/ai/summaries.test.ts` (**8/8 green** — the FIRST test for this route) pinning (1) genuine Tier-0 CONCURRENCY (hold `event.findFirst` pending via a controlled resolver → `$queryRaw` + `eventStaff.findMany` + `allergenWarning.findMany` all fire before it resolves, AND `dish.findMany` does NOT — proving it is Tier-1), (2) the Tier-1 dependency (`dish.findMany` called with `id: { in: [dishIds] }` ONLY when event_dishes rows exist), (3) the empty-event_dishes guard (dish read skipped), (4) the full happy path incl. summary/highlights/criticalInfo + `eventTitle`/`model`, (5) the AI-failure → rule-based fallback path, (6) 401 before any DB read, (7) 400 missing eventId, (8) 404 event-not-found. Sibling `__tests__/ai/` dir **29/29 green** (21 suggestions + 8 new; zero regression). Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `summaries/[eventId]/route.ts` or the test** (the concurrency test needed the `as never` cast on its controlled pending-promise, matching the `suggestions.test.ts` precedent — without it the Prisma delegate return-type leaks 2 errors); code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#19 REMAINS OPEN** — inventory low-stock + run-sheet + nutrition-labels + logistics/vehicles + ai/suggestions + events/export/csv + ai/summaries shipped this initiative; the AI-summary dependency chain flagged in prior logs is now RESOLVED (this increment). Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is structural (5→2 rounds on the AI-summary context load) regardless of measured magnitude.

- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, ai/bulk-tasks/confirm serial for-of → parallel SHIPPED):** Collapsed `POST /api/ai/bulk-tasks/confirm` (`apps/api/app/api/ai/bulk-tasks/confirm/route.ts`) — the last #19 sub-item flagged in the prior logs — from a serial `for-of` over `nonDuplicateTasks` into one `Promise.all` over the tasks (the [[parallelization-mock-order-pattern]] technique). Each task issues two governed `runManifestCommandCore` writes (PrepTask.create → PrepTask.updateDetails); within a task updateDetails stays serial behind create (it needs the created id), but the tasks are mutually independent — each is keyed only on its own inputs plus the shared `event.locationId` (loaded once before the loop) — so across tasks the governed round-trips race: **N×2 serial writes collapse to ~2 waves** regardless of task count. The per-task async fn returns `{ createdId?: string }`; `createdIds` is rebuilt by `.map(...).filter(...)` in array order, so **task order is preserved** (Promise.all yields results in input order) — byte-identical `createdCount`/`taskIds`/`skippedCount`. Failure semantics preserved exactly: a create returning `{ ok: false }` → `captureException` + that task contributes no id (filtered out); an updateDetails `{ ok: false }` → `captureException` but the created id is still counted (matches the old `createdIds.push(createdId)`-before-updateDetails order). The `event.locationId!` non-null assertion stays (the `if (!event.locationId) return 400` guard precedes the loop). **Governed-write safety:** each task's create + updateDetails is an independent `RuntimeEngine.runCommand()` (no shared tx, no cross-task ordering dependency); parallel dispatch is safe — events/audit/constraints run per command independently. **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/ai/bulk-tasks-confirm.test.ts` (**5/5 green** — the FIRST test for this route) pinning (1) genuine CONCURRENCY via a discriminating controlled-pending mock (`create` calls held pending → all 3 are in-flight simultaneously, `maxConcurrentCreates === 3` — impossible in the old serial layout where at most 1 was ever pending; fails if reverted to `for-of`), (2) the within-task create→updateDetails serial dependency (each updateDetails body carries the created id + the shared `locationId`; 2 tasks × 2 calls = 4 governed calls), (3) partial-failure isolation (one task's create fails → skipped + `captureException` once, the other two still created in order), (4) the all-duplicates short-circuit (`createdCount:0`, zero governed calls), (5) the 401 auth guard before any DB/governed call. Sibling `__tests__/ai/` dir **34/34 green** (21 suggestions + 8 summaries + 5 new; zero regression). Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `bulk-tasks/confirm/route.ts` or the test**; code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#19 REMAINS OPEN** — inventory low-stock + run-sheet + nutrition-labels + logistics/vehicles + ai/suggestions + events/export/csv + ai/summaries + **ai/bulk-tasks/confirm** shipped this initiative. **#19 clean autonomous sub-items EXHAUSTED** (verified 2026-07-13). The last flagged one — `events/budgets` `include:{lineItems}` over-fetch — is a DEAD-END: the bare `GET /api/events/budgets` route has ZERO frontend/production callers (only its own test suites hit it; consumers use the manifest-GENERATED `/api/events/budgets/list` route via `listEventBudgets` + `/{id}` for detail — cf the "Three #19/#20 DEAD-ENDS" note). Dropping the include from the bare route improves dead code → no real perf win (commit `b4ebb64fd` attempted it + falsely claimed #19 resolved; REVERTED in `d47935d48`). The REAL events/budgets list over-fetch is the generated `/list` route, #6-blocked (upstream generator). The Proposal + KB-content #20 sub-items are likewise documented dead-ends (Proposal has no `@db.Text` cols; KB `content` is consumed by the client). - **Implementation log (2026-07-14, inventory-forecasting alerts N+1 batch collapse SHIPPED):** Collapsed `batchCalculateForecasts` (`apps/api/app/lib/inventory-forecasting.ts`) — backing `GET /api/inventory/forecasts/alerts` (loads all tenant items, forecasts each) — from `1 + 4N` sequential reads into 3 constant reads. **Before:** a serial `for (sku of skus) calculateDepletionForecast(...)`, each issuing 4 reads — `inventoryItem.findFirst` (no select) + tenant-wide `event.findMany` (the `_sku` param was UNUSED, identical for every SKU, re-fetched N×) + `inventoryTransaction.findMany` (historical usage) + the SAME `inventoryTransaction.findMany` again via `calculateConfidenceLevel` (identical args). **After (3 round-trips regardless of SKU count):** (1) ONE `inventoryItem.findMany({ item_number:{in}, select:{id,item_number,quantityOnHand} })` → Map (first-wins mirrors findFirst); (2) ONE hoisted tenant-wide events read (was re-fetched identically per SKU); (3) ONE `inventoryTransaction.findMany({ itemId:{in} })` grouped into a per-item Map; per-SKU math runs pure over the Maps. Also deduped the single-SKU `calculateDepletionForecast` (historical usage fetched 2×→1× via a pure `computeConfidence` helper; 4→3 reads/SKU, which also halves the per-SKU cost in the still-serial `generateReorderSuggestions`). Byte-identical math via extracted pure helpers (`computeHistoricalUsage`/`buildProjectedUsage`/`buildForecastPoints`/`computeConfidence`); the no-item events-only branch is subsumed (`buildProjectedUsage` w/ `dailyAverage=0` == events-only); removed 3 now-dead helpers (`getProjectedUsage`, `getProjectedUsageFromEventsOnly`, `calculateConfidenceLevel`); used a `DecimalLike` structural interface instead of `Prisma.Decimal` annotations (biome strips a type-only `Prisma` import that can't resolve as a namespace for `Prisma.Decimal`). `result-key` + `forecast.sku` field preserved. Missing SKUs degrade to zero-stock via Map miss (a single batched read can't throw per-item — the batched equivalent of the prior per-SKU findFirst isolation). **Verification:** `forecasting.test.ts` **32/32 green** (31 prior + 1 new N+1-collapse regression guard asserting `inventoryItem.findMany`/`inventoryTransaction.findMany`/`event.findMany` each called **ONCE** regardless of SKU count, `findFirst` **NEVER**); full inventory dir **261/261 green** (zero regression); `apps/api` `tsc --noEmit` = **14 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO new**; code-only → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal. **DEFERRED (teed up):** (a) `generateReorderSuggestions` serial per-low-stock-SKU loop still N+1 (3N after the single-SKU dedup, was 4N) — needs a batched reorder core reusing this batched-forecast infra; (b) `getAccuracySummary` per-SKU `inventoryForecast.count` → one `inventoryForecast.groupBy({ by: ["sku"] })`; (c) shipments list route (`apps/api/app/api/shipments/route.ts:113`) select-narrowing — `Shipment.findMany` has no `select` and pulls an unused base64 `signatureData` blob (uses `signatureText`); clean win to add a focused select dropping `signatureData`/`reference`. - **Implementation log (2026-07-13, prep-lists PDF 4×N→4 + nutrition-labels generate `select` SHIPPED — the plan's named "highest remaining structural win"):** Shipped the two sites the prior #20 log flagged as the highest remaining structural win. **`GET /api/kitchen/prep-lists/[id]/pdf` event branch (`preparePdfData`):** collapsed a **4×N waterfall inside the eventDish loop** — per dish it fired `dish.findFirst` + `recipeVersion.findFirst` (pulling the heavy `instructions` `@db.Text` blob, `manifest.prisma:4998`, while consuming only `id`+`yieldQuantity`) + `recipeIngredient.findMany` + `ingredient.findMany`; a 20-dish event paid ~80 round-trips per PDF — into **4 batched reads** following the dependency graph: (1) `dish.findMany({ where:{ id:{ in: dishIds }, tenantId }, select:{ id, recipeId } })`; (2) `recipeVersion.findMany({ where:{ recipeId:{ in: recipeIds }, tenantId }, distinct:["recipeId"], orderBy:{ versionNumber:"desc" }, select:{ id, recipeId, yieldQuantity } })` → latest version per recipe (the `distinct`-for-latest-per-group pattern the run-sheet + nutrition-labels-list #19 increments established — one row per recipeId, the highest versionNumber); (3) `recipeIngredient.findMany({ where:{ recipeVersionId:{ in: versionIds }, tenantId }, select:{ ingredientId, quantity, recipeVersionId } })` grouped into a `Map<versionId, rows>`; (4) `ingredient.findMany({ where:{ id:{ in: ingredientIds }, tenantId }, select:{ id, name, category } })`. The per-eventDish iteration then runs over in-memory Maps, preserving the exact prior behavior: per-eventDish order, per-version ingredient order (no ORDER BY → same physical row order), the `!dish?.recipeId` / `!latestVersion` skip guards, duplicate-dishId processing (each eventDish occurrence is processed), and the `guestCount / yieldQuantity` scaling. Every read carries a focused `select`, so the `instructions` `@db.Text` blob is no longer materialized per dish (the #20 over-fetch fix). Empty-set guards (`dishIds.length > 0` etc.) skip pointless `in: []` round-trips (the run-sheet/nutrition-labels precedent). ### 21. `[RESOLVED 2026-07-12 — RE-VERIFIED SPECULATIVE; no indexes added]` `infra.prisma` P1 indexes (hand-owned, additive migration)
- **What:** Add the high-value composite indexes on infra tables; replace (not duplicate) the now-redundant single-column `OutboxEvent [tenantId]` index; remove the redundant `settings @@index`.
- **Why / evidence:** `admin_audit_trail [tenant_id, created_at]` + `[tenant_id, entity_type, entity_id]` (high-volume audit, seq-scan today); `admin_users [auth_user_id]` (login/auth path, cross-tenant); `OutboxEvent [tenantId, createdAt]` (polling sweep, unbounded growth); `report_schedules [tenant_id, next_run_at]` (cron "due now" = full scan each tick). Verified: the other **4** infra P1 indexes (`admin_audit_trail` ×2, `admin_users [auth_user_id]`, `report_schedules [tenant_id, next_run_at]`) confirmed **ABSENT**; `settings` redundant `@@index` (`:1515`) duplicating `@@unique` (`:1514`) confirmed.
  - ~~`[INVESTIGATE]` OutboxEvent schema ownership: verification reports the generated `manifest.prisma` `OutboxEvent` already carries `@@index([status,createdAt])` + `@@index([tenantId])`. Confirm whether the `[tenantId, createdAt]` gap belongs in `infra.prisma` (this item) or `manifest.prisma` (item #22) before creating the migration — do not double-add.~~
  > **(2nd-revision resolution, 2026-07-12):** **RESOLVED.** `OutboxEvent` lives in **`infra.prisma:1216` (NOT `manifest.prisma`)**, and already has `@@index([status,createdAt])` + `@@index([tenantId])` + `@@index([aggregateType,aggregateId])`. So the `[tenantId, createdAt]` gap belongs **here** (infra), and should **REPLACE the single-column `@@index([tenantId])`**, not be double-added. Prior `[INVESTIGATE]` → `[RESOLVED]`.
- **Fix:** Add the 4 absent indexes + the composite `[tenantId, createdAt]` (replacing the single `[tenantId]`) in `infra.prisma`; generate via `pnpm db:dev --create-only`; review SQL; remove the redundant `settings @@index`. Justify each with the measurement from item #1 (seq-scan on the hot path).
- **Scope:** `prisma-migration`
- **Acceptance check:** `EXPLAIN` shows index scans on the 5 hot paths; the single-column `OutboxEvent [tenantId]` index is replaced (not duplicated); `db:check` clean; `manifest:ci` green; migration committed (not applied to prod without the deploy gate).
- **Implementation log (2026-07-12, RE-VERIFIED SPECULATIVE — NO INDEXES ADDED):** The prior `[RESOLVED]` tag was **STALE** — there was no implementation log (every genuinely-resolved item has one), and a direct re-read of all 5 target models against current `infra.prisma` this turn confirmed all 5 targets were still OPEN (`admin_audit_trail` :391 only `@@id`; `admin_users` :440 only `@@id`; `OutboxEvent` :1216 has `[status,createdAt]`+`[tenantId]`+`[aggregateType,aggregateId]` but no `[tenantId,createdAt]`; `report_schedules` :1425 has `[tenant_id,report_id]` but no `[tenant_id,next_run_at]`; `settings` :1505 has both `@@unique([tenant_id,setting_key])` :1514 AND a redundant `@@index([tenant_id,setting_key])` :1515). A read-hot-path verification then **disproved 4 of the 5 claims** (the spec gate is "Any index added is justified by a measured hot path"): ~~`admin_audit_trail [tenant_id,created_at]` + `[tenant_id,entity_type,entity_id]` (high-volume audit, seq-scan today)~~ + ~~`admin_users [auth_user_id]` (login/auth path, cross-tenant)~~ + ~~`report_schedules [tenant_id,next_run_at]` (cron "due now" full scan each tick)~~ → **ZERO read sites in app code** (bare `rg "admin_audit_trail|admin_users|report_schedules|next_run_at"` over `apps/` excluding tests/generated/migrations returns nothing for the first two; `next_run_at` appears ONLY in generated type files `apps/app/app/lib/manifest-client/logistics.generated.ts` + `manifest-types.generated.ts`, never queried). Audit READS use the **separate `audit_log` model** (`infra.prisma:528`, not `admin_audit_trail`); app auth resolves via the **`User`/`employees` model** in `apps/api/app/lib/tenant.ts` (`where:{tenantId,authUserId:clerkId}` — composite, on a DIFFERENT model), NOT `admin_users`. ~~`OutboxEvent [tenantId,createdAt]` (polling sweep, unbounded growth)~~ → the actual hot poller (`apps/api/app/outbox/publish/route.ts:97-117`) filters `status='pending' ORDER BY created_at` — **already covered by the existing `@@index([status,createdAt])`** (`:1229`); the only `tenantId`+`createdAt` query is the occasional `command-board/[boardId]/replay` route (`:134-176`, multi-predicate, not a hot path). Per the spec gate + YAGNI, **NONE of these speculative indexes were added** — adding an index with no read hot path is exactly the activity-without-proof anti-pattern the spec exists to prevent. The ONE verified-warranted change is the **redundant `settings @@index([tenant_id,setting_key])` removal** (the `@@unique` already indexes those columns → the explicit `@@index` is pure write-overhead with zero read benefit) — **DEFERRED** to bundle with #22's next measured index migration (a solo one-DROP migration is not worth the migration/push overhead). Net: #21 needs NO migration this turn; the speculative indexes were correctly NOT added. **Lesson (applies to #22):** the plan's hot-path claims require read-site verification before any additive index — #22's manifest-index claims need the same `rg`-backed read-site scrutiny before landing, or they risk the same speculative-index failure mode.
