### 24. `[RESOLVED 2026-07-13]` Unclamped `limit` → `clampLimit()` sweep
- **What:** Replace bare `parseInt(searchParams.get("limit"))` with the existing `clampLimit()` helper everywhere.
- **Why / evidence:** Unclamped `limit` → `?limit=999999` unbounded read. A `clampLimit()` helper already exists at `apps/api/lib/pagination.ts` (`DEFAULT_LIMIT=50`, `MAX_LIMIT=200`).
  - ~~…in ~7 staff/timecard routes + goodshuffle…~~
  > **(2nd-revision correction, 2026-07-12):** Correct count: **63 routes unclamped** (not "~7 staff/timecard + goodshuffle"). `clampLimit` is used in **only 22 of ~95 paginated routes**. `training/modules/route.ts` clamps **MANUALLY** (not via `clampLimit` — minor correction); `training/assignments` DOES use it.
  - `[NEW, 2nd Revision]` **2 routes default `limit:1000` with no clamp:** `kitchen/iot/readings:28`, `command-board/[boardId]/replay:69`. **11 `validation.ts` files are a hidden unclamp vector** (4th rev, 2026-07-12: 11, not 6 — validation schemas that accept arbitrary `limit`).
- **Fix:** Use `clampLimit()` at every unvalidated `limit`→`take` site; clamp the 2 default-1000 routes; close the `validation.ts` vector.
- **Scope:** `route`
- **Acceptance check:** No `parseInt(limit)` reaches `take` without clamping; the 2 default-1000 routes clamp; grep confirms zero remaining unclamped sites.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, RESOLVED):** Closed the unbounded-`limit` DoS vector across the apps/api list surface. **Helper extended (backwards-compatible):** `apps/api/lib/pagination.ts` `clampLimit(raw, max=MAX_LIMIT, fallback=DEFAULT_LIMIT)` — the helper's own JSDoc promised "per-route overrides remain possible" but provided no mechanism; the two optional params deliver it so each route preserves its existing default page size while gaining the upper bound. **17 MECHANICAL routes** swapped bare `parseInt(searchParams.get("limit"))` → `clampLimit(...)`, preserving per-route defaults via `fallback` (call-planner/drafts=20, kitchen/waste/entries=100, events/[eventId]/guests=100; the other 14 default to DEFAULT_LIMIT=50): call-planner/drafts, kitchen/waste/entries, events/[eventId]/guests, crm/clients/[id]/{interactions,events}, staff/{certifications,shifts}, logistics/routes/list, integrations/goodshuffle/{inventory,events,invoices}, timecards, staff/time-off/requests, staff/availability, staff/schedules, events/automated-followups/list. **Companion `clampOffset`** on the 7 routes with a direct `offset` param (waste/entries, guests, crm/clients/[id]/{interactions,events}, goodshuffle×3, automated-followups); page-derived offsets left as-is (page-clamping is a separate `skip`/OFFSET concern, out of #24 scope and noted as a follow-up). **5 raw-SQL routes** (timecards, time-off, availability, schedules, automated-followups) clamp `limit` before it enters the `LIMIT ${limit}` tagged template — the clamped number binds as a parameter (safe). **3 SPECIAL cases:** `kitchen/iot/readings` → `clampLimit(raw, 1000, 1000)` (was FULLY unbounded — default 1000, no ceiling); `events/export/csv` → `clampLimit(raw, 5000, 1000)` (was `Math.min(parseInt,5000)` with no NaN/negative guard → `take:NaN` silently returned 0 rows, `take:-5` returned the LAST 5); `command-board/[boardId]/replay` → kept its explicit `>5000 → 400` reject contract, added `!Number.isFinite(limit)` (NaN previously leaked past `NaN < 1 || NaN > 5000` → `take:NaN`). **allergens/warnings** null-sentinel preserved: `take: limit ? clampLimit(limit) : undefined` (the route deliberately returns unbounded when no param is passed — only the present-value path is clamped). **validation.ts vector:** capped `inventory/stock-levels/validation.ts` `f.limit` at `MAX_LIMIT` in both `validateFilters` + `validateTransactionFilters` (defense-in-depth — the route's actual `take` is separately bounded by `parsePaginationParams` at 100; this closes the plan's "validation.ts hidden vector" so a filter `limit` can never exceed the policy ceiling). **Left as-is (NOT a vector):** ~30 routes bound `limit` via a local `Math.min(Math.max(...,1),100)` `PaginationParams` helper (verified this turn: events/route, warehouse/pick-pack, payroll/runs, etc. all wrap the inner `Math.max(...,1)` in `Math.min(...,100)`) — bounded at 100; the 100-vs-200 + local-vs-`clampLimit` inconsistency is cosmetic, documented for a later normalization pass. `sentry-fixer/process` parses `limit` as a job-loop bound (already clamped to `MAX_JOB_BATCH=200`), not a DB read — untouched. **Gotcha (reconfirmed):** biome's `noUnusedImports` autofix DROPS a freshly-added import when the import edit lands before the usage edit (hit on validation.ts) — mitigated by usage-edit-first ordering; cf [[biome-autofix-drops-new-import-mid-batch]]. **Verification:** `apps/api/__tests__/lib/pagination.test.ts` **16/16 green** (was 11; +5 tests for the new `max`/`fallback` overrides + backwards-compat); `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO new** (the 2 `staff/shifts/route.ts:91,109` errors are the documented nullable-`locationId` cluster — the limit edit is at line 37, unrelated); **12 touched-route test files 274/274 green** (export-csv, stock-levels-transactions, client-events, client-interactions, logistics, allergens-warnings, guests, shifts-validation, timecards, availability-validation, schedule-end-to-end, goodshuffle). No schema/manifest touched → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is correctness/availability (a hostile `?limit=999999` no longer materializes a whole-table read, and the `take:NaN`/`take:-5` footguns are gone) regardless of measured magnitude.

### 25. `[PARTIAL 2026-07-13: supplier-catalog {DoS cap + per-product read-N+1 preload} + simulations/apply modifications-loop batching + integrations/webhooks/{retry read-preload, trigger concurrent send+write wave} SHIPPED; governed-write batching remains serial (blocked on #18 runtime rework)]` Serial per-row UPDATE/upsert loops → batch inside transactions
- **What:** Batch the per-row write loops across completion/simulation/webhook routes.
- **Why / evidence:**
  - ~~`inventory/purchase-orders/[id]/complete/route.ts:120-160,212-231` (per-item `purchaseOrderItem.update` + `inventoryItem.update` — **serial**)~~
  > **(2nd-revision correction, 2026-07-12):** PO-complete uses **`Promise.all`** (concurrent within `$transaction`, **not serial as framed**). Still holds a tx connection for N items, but the per-item cost is concurrency, not serialization. Fix target: batch to reduce connection-hold time.
  - ~~`command-board/simulations/{[id]/apply, merge}/route.ts` (per-projection update inside `$transaction`)~~
  > **(2nd-revision correction, 2026-07-12):** `simulations/[id]/apply` route **does NOT exist** — only `merge/route.ts` has the per-projection loop.
  > **(4th rev, 2026-07-12 re-correction):** **FALSE** — `simulations/[id]/apply/route.ts` **DOES exist** (516 lines); the prior "does NOT exist" correction was wrong. Bulk ops in `apply` handle adds/removes via `createMany`/`updateMany`; only the modifications loop (`:438-471`) is serial. Fix target: batch the modifications loop.
  - `webhooks/supplier-catalog/route.ts:209-306` (per-product governed upsert).
  - `[NEW, 2nd Revision]` **`payload.products` is Zod `.min(1)` with NO `.max()`** → **unbounded**. Cap it.
  - `integrations/webhooks/{retry, trigger}/route.ts` (per-row create/update).
- **Fix:** Batch via `updateMany` / `createMany` / a `VALUES` CTE where the governed-write constitution allows; keep governance via `RuntimeEngine.runCommand()` for domain mutations (do not bypass to raw SQL); add a `.max()` to `payload.products`.
- **Scope:** `route`
- **Acceptance check:** Per-row write loops collapse to chunked batches; transaction semantics preserved; before/after on the PO-complete path.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, supplier-catalog products-payload DoS cap SHIPPED):** Closed the unbounded-payload DoS vector on `POST /api/webhooks/supplier-catalog` (`apps/api/app/api/webhooks/supplier-catalog/route.ts`) — the explicit "add a `.max()` to `payload.products`" sub-item the plan names (the `[NEW, 2nd Revision]` finding). **Before:** `WebhookPayloadSchema.products` was `z.array(WebhookProductSchema).min(1)` with **NO `.max()`** → a hostile or buggy supplier could POST an arbitrarily large `products` array, each entry fanning out into a `vendorCatalog.findFirst` read + a governed `runManifestCommand` create/update (`:209-306`), so one request could drive unbounded DB + governed-write work + memory. **After:** `products: z.array(WebhookProductSchema).min(1).max(MAX_PRODUCTS_PER_WEBHOOK)` where `MAX_PRODUCTS_PER_WEBHOOK = Number(process.env.SUPPLIER_CATALOG_MAX_PRODUCTS) || 1000` — a generous default (covers typical catalog pushes) that bounds the vector, env-overridable for large-catalog suppliers (the value genuinely varies by supplier deployment, so env-config is justified, not speculative — mirrors the established `MANIFEST_BATCH_MAX_SIZE` env-cap pattern shipped in #29). The cap fires at **zod validation** (before the connector lookup, signature check, supplier lookup, or any governed write), so an oversized payload is rejected with a `400 "Validation failed"` at the cheapest possible point. **Verification:** `apps/api/__tests__/webhooks/supplier-catalog.test.ts` **21/21 green** (20 existing + 1 new) — added a regression guard that sends 1001 products (one over the default-1000 cap), asserts `400 "Validation failed"`, AND asserts NO DB/governed work fired (`mockSupplierFindFirst` + `runManifestCommand` never called — pinning the DoS is rejected at validation, the whole point of bounding it). Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `supplier-catalog/route.ts` or the test**; code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **DEFERRED sub-items of #25 (separate scoped follow-ups, NOT stubs):** (a) the per-product **read**-N+1 (`vendorCatalog.findFirst` inside the loop at `:236`) — structurally the same Map-preload shape as the shipped #14 inventory-import / #8c webhook-retry read-preloads, BUT the route's own comment (`:235`) documents `(tenantId, supplierId, itemNumber)` is **no longer a unique key**, so a naive pre-loop snapshot would make a within-payload duplicate SKU silently create a 2nd row (data divergence); closing it correctly requires either feeding created ids back into the Map (parse the create `Response` for the id) or deduping the payload by last-SKU-wins — the latter changes the `productsProcessed` response count, a product-behavior decision → defer (not autonomous-safe); (b) the per-product **governed write** batching (the `runManifestCommand` create/update loop) — constitution-bound (`RuntimeEngine.runCommand()` per domain mutation; `createMany`/`updateMany` would bypass RBAC/constraints/audit/events/reactions, cf. #14's governance correction), needs `runManifestBatch` work; (c) the other #25 sites — `command-board/simulations/[id]/apply` serial modifications loop (`:438-471`, confirmed EXISTS per the 4th-rev re-correction), `integrations/webhooks/{retry,trigger}` per-row create/update, PO-complete (already `Promise.all` concurrent per the 2nd-rev correction — connection-hold, not serialization). Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is availability/correctness (a hostile supplier push can no longer drive unbounded work) regardless of measured magnitude.

- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, command-board/simulations/[id]/apply modifications-loop batching SHIPPED — #25c):** Collapsed the serial modifications loop in `POST /api/command-board/simulations/[id]/apply` (`apps/api/app/api/command-board/simulations/[id]/apply/route.ts`) — the explicit #25 sub-item the 4th-rev re-correction named ("only the modifications loop (~:438-471) is serial. Fix target: batch the modifications loop"). **Before:** step 7 of the apply `$transaction` was a `for...of` over `delta.modified_projections` issuing one `await tx.boardProjection.update(...)` PER mod — N serial round-trips holding the interactive-tx connection for the whole loop on every simulation apply. **After (one concurrent batch):** `await Promise.all(delta.modified_projections.map(async (mod) => { ... await tx.boardProjection.update(...) }))` — each mod targets a DISTINCT composite-PK row (`tenantId_id`), reads ONLY pre-loaded in-memory arrays (`simulatedProjections`/`originalProjections`), and writes a payload-driven field/value, so the iterations are fully data-independent → safe to issue concurrently inside the same transaction. The per-mod body is byte-identical except `continue` → `return` (inside the map callback). `updateMany` was NOT viable (each mod may update a DIFFERENT column — `positionX`/`positionY`/`zIndex`/`colorOverride`/`groupId`), so `Promise.all` of per-row updates is the correct shape. **Concurrent-in-transaction precedent (the deciding safety fact, verified this turn):** the shipped `inventory/purchase-orders/[id]/complete/route.ts` ALREADY does `Promise.all` of `tx.purchaseOrderItem.update` (`:120`) / `tx.inventoryTransaction.create` (`:163`) / `tx.inventoryItem.update` (`:212`) inside its `$transaction` (with inline "fix N+1" comments) — proving Prisma 7.8 in this repo supports concurrent queries on the same interactive-tx client; this change reuses that established pattern. **Scope note:** this is RAW Prisma `tx.*`, NOT governed `runtime.runCommand` — `BoardProjection` is a manifest-adjacent infra table written directly via Prisma (no `RuntimeEngine.runCommand` anywhere in this route), so the composite-recipe #18 governed-runtime-concurrency question does NOT apply here. **Verification:** extended `apps/api/__tests__/command-board/simulations.test.ts` — hoisted a stable `txBoardProjectionUpdate` mock reference into the `$transaction` mock (it was a fresh, unreachable `vi.fn()` per call) and added a concurrency test (the FIRST to exercise the modifications loop — the existing happy-path test used empty `boardProjections`, so the loop never ran). The new test crafts 2 projections sharing an `entity_id` between source + simulation boards but differing in one DB-backed field each (`position_x`/`position_y`; the route's API mapping hardcodes `z_index`/`color_override`/`collapsed`/`group_id`/`pinned` equal, so only `position_x`/`position_y`/`width`/`height` can produce mods) → exactly 2 modifications, and asserts (1) genuine CONCURRENCY via a max-in-flight probe (each update yields on `setTimeout(0)`; `maxInFlight === 2` — a reverted serial `for-of` would cap at 1), (2) each update carries the correct mapped field + simulated value on the correct source row in `computeBoardDelta` emission order, (3) the 200 response + `delta.modifications === 2`. Suite **18/18 green** (17 existing + 1 new; the 3 pre-existing apply tests unchanged — only the await structure changed, semantics preserved). Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `apply/route.ts` or the test**; code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#25 REMAINS PARTIAL** — supplier-catalog DoS cap + simulations/apply modifications-loop batching shipped; still open: the supplier-catalog per-product **read**-N+1 + governed-write batching (needs a within-payload dup-SKU product decision per the route's "no longer a unique key" comment), `integrations/webhooks/{retry,trigger}` per-row create/update, PO-complete (already `Promise.all` concurrent per the 2nd-rev correction — connection-hold, not serialization). Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is structural (N serial → 1 concurrent wave of updates per simulation apply, holding the tx connection for ~1 round-trip instead of N) regardless of measured magnitude.

- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, integrations/webhooks/retry per-delivery read-N+1 preload SHIPPED — #25d):** Collapsed the per-delivery `outboundWebhook.findFirst` in `POST /api/integrations/webhooks/retry` (`apps/api/app/api/integrations/webhooks/retry/route.ts`) — the `integrations/webhooks/{retry,trigger}` per-row read the #25 list names. **Before:** the retry loop fired one `outboundWebhook.findFirst({ where: { tenantId, id: delivery.webhookId, deletedAt: null } })` PER delivery (up to `maxRetries=50`/run), and a burst of failures for ONE endpoint re-fetched the same webhook row repeatedly. **After (1 round-trip/run, deduped):** preload the distinct webhooks in ONE `outboundWebhook.findMany({ where: { tenantId, id: { in: distinctWebhookIds }, deletedAt: null } })` into a `Map<webhookId, webhook>`; the per-delivery lookup is an in-memory `Map.get` (the #8c cron/webhook-retry read-preload shape; all deliveries share the resolved `tenantId` so the preload is directly tenant-scoped — no cross-tenant concern). **Feed-back subtlety (the decisive correctness detail — same class as the #14 inventory-import duplicate-`item_number` feed-back):** the preloaded `webhook` is ALSO WRITTEN in the loop (`outboundWebhook.update` bumps `consecutiveFailures` and may set `status:"disabled"` via `shouldAutoDisable`). The prior per-delivery `findFirst` RE-READ the just-updated row, so a burst of FAILING deliveries to the SAME webhook accumulated `consecutiveFailures` across deliveries (2→3→4) AND a tripped auto-disable propagated to later same-webhook deliveries (skipped by the `status !== "active"` guard). A naive Map snapshot would FREEZE both at the stale preloaded value — a SILENT behavior change (under-counting failures / failing to skip a just-disabled webhook mid-batch). Preserved exactly by feeding the two cross-delivery-relevant fields back into the Map after each update: `webhooksById.set(webhook.id, { ...webhook, consecutiveFailures: updates.consecutiveFailures, ...(updates.status ? { status: updates.status } : {}) })`. Only `consecutiveFailures` + `status` need feed-back — `url`/`secret`/`retryCount`/etc. are immutable webhook config. The two early-`continue` paths (deleted → "Webhook configuration was deleted"; inactive → "Webhook is ${status}") do NOT write `outboundWebhook`, so need no feed-back. **Scope discipline:** ships ONLY the read preload — the per-delivery OUTCOME-driven WRITES (`webhookDeliveryLog.update`/`outboundWebhook.update`/`webhookDeadLetterQueue.create`) depend on each delivery's `sendWebhook` HTTP result so cannot be pre-batched; they are INFRA writes (not governed domain mutations), so a future concurrency pass could parallelize the loop, but that is a separate increment. **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/integrations/webhooks-retry.test.ts` (**5/5 green** — the FIRST test for this route) pinning (1) N+1 collapse + dedupe (`findMany` ONCE with `where.id.in:[distinct ids]`, `findFirst` NEVER, for 3 deliveries across 2 webhooks), (2) **consecutiveFailures accumulation** — 2 failing deliveries to wh-A (cf starts 2) → `outboundWebhook.update` data.consecutiveFailures = [3,4] (a snapshot would freeze both at 3 → fails), (3) **auto-disable propagation** — `shouldAutoDisable=true` → delivery 1 disables, delivery 2 to the SAME webhook skipped by the inactive guard (`sendWebhook` called ONCE; a deliveryLog update carries "Webhook is disabled"), (4) deleted-webhook Map miss → "Webhook configuration was deleted" + no send, (5) 401 before any DB read. Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `retry/route.ts` or the test**; code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **Sibling gap flagged for verification:** the cron sibling `cron/webhook-retry` (#8c) shipped ONLY a read preload into a Map AND its loop ALSO does `outboundWebhook.update` with `consecutiveFailures` — ~~it MAY carry the same latent feed-back gap (a future loop should confirm whether #8c feeds back, or whether the cron's per-tick dedupe makes same-webhook-multi-delivery rare enough to be moot).~~ **(RESOLVED 2026-07-13 — confirmed #8c did NOT feed back; the frozen-snapshot bug was REAL (froze `consecutiveFailures` at `preloaded+1` → auto-disable never tripped mid-burst; kept sending to a just-disabled endpoint) and is now fixed with the 2-field Map feed-back mirroring this retry route; see the #8 log entry "cron/webhook-retry Map feed-back correctness fix". 8/8 tests incl. 2 discriminating cf-accumulation + auto-disable-propagation guards.)** **#25 REMAINS PARTIAL** — supplier-catalog DoS cap + simulations/apply + this retry read-preload shipped; still open: the supplier-catalog per-product read-N+1 + governed-write batching (within-payload dup-SKU product decision), `integrations/webhooks/trigger` per-row create/update (read side is already ONE `outboundWebhook.findMany`; the per-webhook write loop is the remaining half — same infra-write shape), PO-complete (already concurrent per the 2nd-rev). Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is structural (up to 50 findFirst → 1 findMany per retry run, deduped) regardless of measured magnitude.

- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, integrations/webhooks/trigger concurrent send+write wave SHIPPED — #25e):** Collapsed the per-webhook serial send+write loop in `POST /api/integrations/webhooks/trigger` (`apps/api/app/api/integrations/webhooks/trigger/route.ts`) — the `integrations/webhooks/trigger` per-row work the #25 list names (the remaining half of the `{retry,trigger}` pair after #25d shipped retry's read-preload). **Before:** the route filtered the tenant's active webhooks, then a `for...of` over the triggered set issued, PER webhook and SERIALLY: `webhookDeliveryLog.create` → `sendWebhook` (outbound HTTP) → `webhookDeliveryLog.update` → `outboundWebhook.update`. N matching webhooks = N serial outbound HTTP round-trips on every entity event (each up to `webhook.timeoutMs`), plus N×3 serial DB writes — a 5-webhook tenant paid ~5×(HTTP+writes) in sequence on every created/updated/deleted entity. **After (one concurrent wave):** `await Promise.all(triggeredWebhooks.map(async (webhook) => { …same per-webhook body… }))`. **Safety premise (verified this turn):** each iteration is fully data-independent — its OWN `deliveryLog` (own id), its OWN HTTP endpoint (own `url`), and its OWN stats update keyed by its OWN `webhook.id`. `triggeredWebhooks` is a `.filter()` over distinct `outboundWebhook.findMany` rows, so each `webhook.id` appears exactly once → no two concurrent iterations contend on the same `outboundWebhook` row. This is SIMPLER than the retry route (#25d): retry had to FEED BACK `consecutiveFailures`/`status` into a shared Map because multiple deliveries target the SAME webhook; here each webhook fires once, so there is no cross-iteration shared state and no feed-back. The shared `payload` (built once before the loop) is read-only → safe to read concurrently. `Promise.all` preserves index order → the `results[]` array (and thus the `{ triggered, results }` response) is byte-identical to the serial version. NOT governed `runtime.runCommand` writes (infra delivery-log/webhook-stats writes), so the manifest-runtime concurrency limit does NOT apply (same raw-Prisma concurrent-write precedent as PO-complete, simulations/apply #25c, retry #25d). **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/integrations/webhooks-trigger.test.ts` (**5/5 green** — the FIRST test for this route) pinning (1) genuine CONCURRENCY via a max-in-flight probe (each `sendWebhook` yields on `setTimeout(0)`; `maxInFlight === 3` for 3 webhooks — a reverted serial `for-of` would cap at 1), (2) per-webhook independence + order (each `deliveryLog.create` carries its OWN `webhookId` and each `outboundWebhook.update` keys its OWN `webhook.id`; `results[]` in `triggeredWebhooks` order with per-webhook `deliveryLogId`), (3) `consecutiveFailures` reset-on-success + bump-on-failure with auto-disable hitting ONLY the failing webhook, (4) the empty-match early-return `{ triggered: 0, results: [] }` with zero create/send/update, (5) 401 before any DB read. Sibling integrations dir **76/76 green** (3 files, zero regression). Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `trigger/route.ts` or the test**; code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#25 REMAINS PARTIAL** — supplier-catalog DoS cap + simulations/apply + retry read-preload + this trigger concurrent wave shipped; still open: the supplier-catalog per-product **read**-N+1 + governed-write batching (within-payload dup-SKU product decision per the route's "no longer a unique key" comment), PO-complete (already `Promise.all` concurrent per the 2nd-rev). Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is structural (N serial outbound HTTP sends → 1 concurrent wave per entity event — the outbound HTTP latency, the slowest part of the path, collapses from Σ(N) to max(N)) regardless of measured magnitude.

- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, supplier-catalog per-product read-N+1 preload SHIPPED — #25a):** Collapsed the per-product `vendorCatalog.findFirst` in `POST /api/webhooks/supplier-catalog` (`apps/api/app/api/webhooks/supplier-catalog/route.ts`) — the read half of #25 that the prior DoS-cap + #25c/d/e logs deferred as "needs a within-payload dup-SKU product decision (not autonomous-safe)." **Before:** the upsert loop fired one `vendorCatalog.findFirst({ where: { tenantId, supplierId, itemNumber } })` PER product (up to `MAX_PRODUCTS_PER_WEBHOOK=1000`), and the prior per-product read RE-READ the just-created row on each iteration (so a within-payload duplicate SKU updated the 1st occurrence's row, last-value-wins). **After (1 round-trip/push):** preload every existing row for the push's SKUs in ONE `vendorCatalog.findMany({ where: { tenantId, supplierId, itemNumber: { in: skus } }, select: { id, itemNumber } })` into a `Map<sku, id>` (first-row-per-SKU wins — `(tenantId, supplierId, itemNumber)` is NOT unique, matching the prior findFirst's "one id"); the per-product lookup is an in-memory `Map.get`. **Within-payload dup-SKU feed-back (the deferred concern, now resolved — identical class to the #14 inventory-import duplicate-`item_number` feed-back, commit `97fdc4059`):** a naive pre-loop snapshot would make a within-payload duplicate SKU create a 2nd row (the prior per-product findFirst re-read the just-created row). Preserved exactly by feeding each successful create's id back into the Map — the created id lives at `(await result.json()).result.id` (this route's `runManifestCommand` returns a `Response` whose success body is `manifestSuccessResponse({ result })` → `{ success, result: { id, … }, events }`); on a create, read it and `existingBySku.set(sku, createdId)` so the 2nd occurrence of a dup SKU finds the just-created row → UPDATE (last-value-wins), byte-identical to the old findFirst behavior and `productsProcessed` unchanged. Read defensively (`typeof createdId === "string"` + `.catch(() => null)` on a malformed success body → best-effort skip of the feed-back, never throws). **Scope discipline:** ships ONLY the read preload — the per-product GOVERNED writes (`runManifestCommand` create/update) stay serial (the manifest runtime is NOT concurrent-safe — see #18's governed-runtime-concurrency resolution; `createMany`/`updateMany` would bypass RBAC/constraints/audit/events/reactions per constitution §12). **Verification:** `apps/api/__tests__/webhooks/supplier-catalog.test.ts` **23/23 green** (21 existing + 2 NEW DISCRIMINATING tests): (a) **N+1 collapse** — 3 distinct SKUs → `findMany` called ONCE with `where.itemNumber.in:[all 3]` + the `select`, `findFirst` NEVER called, commands `["create","update","create"]` (the one existing row updates, the other two create); (b) **dup-SKU feed-back** — 2 products same SKU, no existing → 1st create feeds `vc-new-1` back, 2nd is an UPDATE with `body.id===vc-new-1` + last-value `itemName` (a naive snapshot would make the 2nd a CREATE → fails); `productsProcessed===2`. Existing tests updated for the `findMany` mock (the `setupSupplierAndUser` default + the "update for existing" test). Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in `supplier-catalog/route.ts` or the test** (the 5 transient `noUncheckedIndexedAccess` errors on `mock.calls[N]` were fixed with the repo's `.at(N)?.[0]?` accessor idiom); code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#25 status:** the read-side scope is now COMPLETE — supplier-catalog {DoS cap + read-N+1 preload} + simulations/apply + integrations/webhooks/{retry,trigger} all shipped; the ONLY residual is the per-product **governed-write** batching (constitution-bound serial — blocked on the manifest runtime concurrency rework tracked in #18's NEEDS-RYAN, NOT an autonomous increment). PO-complete is already concurrent per the 2nd-rev. No tag (precondition false: 16 pre-existing tsc; repo `v0.12.X` tags are manifest-release versioning — cf prior tag-decision entries; do NOT tag perf commits). Live before/after latency deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1); the win is structural (N findFirst → 1 findMany per supplier-catalog push, deduped) regardless of measured magnitude. Search: #25a supplier-catalog read preload, vendorCatalog findFirst N+1, within-payload dup-SKU feed-back, manifestSuccessResponse result.id.

### 26. `[RESOLVED 2026-07-13: raw-SQL parameterization + list-route select SHIPPED; detail routes documented low-value]` LOW cluster: detail-route `select` + raw-SQL parameterization
- **What:** Long-tail safety/over-fetch cleanup on detail routes and the raw-SQL interpolation points.
- **Why / evidence:** Detail `findFirst` without `select` pulling large text/JSON: `crm/clients/[id]`, `crm/venues/[id]`, `crm/proposals/[id]`, `staff/employees/route.ts:23`, `staff/performance/list`. Plus raw-SQL interpolation.
  - ~~`analytics/menu-engineering/route.ts:59-91` — `$queryRawUnsafe` string-interpolates `locationFilter` … Verified this revision: this is the **only** raw-SQL interpolation point — all other `$queryRawUnsafe`/`$executeRawUnsafe` are safely parameterized.~~
  > **(2nd-revision correction, 2026-07-12):** The claim "menu-engineering is the ONLY string-interpolated `$queryRawUnsafe`" is **FALSE**. `staffing/coverage/route.ts:104,122,146,162,181` has the **identical `${locParam}` SQL-fragment interpolation pattern**. **Both** bind the value safely but **interpolate the SQL fragment**. Convert both to tagged-template `$queryRaw` with bound parameters. All other `$queryRawUnsafe`/`$executeRawUnsafe` are safely `$1`/`$2`-parameterized (incl. `battle-board/actions/tasks.ts` `$executeRawUnsafe` writes with hardcoded columns).
- **Fix:** Add focused `select` projections; convert both raw queries (`menu-engineering` + `staffing/coverage`) to tagged-template `$queryRaw` with bind parameters.
- **Scope:** `route`
- **Acceptance check:** Payload sizes on cited detail routes shrink; both raw queries use bound params (no string interpolation); `manifest:ci` green.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, menu-engineering + staffing/coverage raw-SQL parameterization SHIPPED — #26 raw-SQL half):** Converted both raw-SQL routes the 2nd-rev correction flagged for `${locParam}` SQL-fragment interpolation to tagged-template `$queryRaw` where every value is a self-binding parameter (commit `4a9d499d9`). **`analytics/menu-engineering` `fetchMenuItemAnalysis`:** was `$queryRawUnsafe` with a hand-built `locationFilter` fragment (`"AND e.location_id = $3::uuid"` or `""`) string-interpolated into the query + manually-numbered `$1`/`$2`/`$3` placeholders; now `$queryRaw\`… WHERE d.tenant_id = ${tenantId} … AND e.event_date >= ${startDate} AND (${locationId}::uuid IS NULL OR e.location_id = ${locationId}::uuid) …\`` — the optional filter is a static `IS NULL OR` clause, so no SQL fragment is ever interpolated into the query text. **`staffing/coverage`:** the SAME pattern across **all five** queries (`dailyRows`, `locationRows`, `todayRows`, `todayLocations`, `weeklyRows`) plus the `locIdx`/`locParam` index-bookkeeping (`:101-102`); each is now a tagged-template `$queryRaw` with `${tenantId}`/`${start|end|todayStart|todayEnd|weeklyStart}`/`${locationId}` self-bound and the same static `(${locationId}::uuid IS NULL OR ss.location_id = ${locationId}::uuid)` clause; the `locIdx`/`locParam` machinery is deleted entirely. Result-set semantics are byte-identical: `NULL::uuid IS NULL` → TRUE (no filter) when no `locationId`; the equality applies when one is given — exactly the prior conditional-fragment behavior. (Drive-by: the weekly query's inline `new Date(Date.now() - 56*24*60*60*1000)` extracted to a named `weeklyStart` const.) **Verification:** added `apps/api/__tests__/analytics/menu-engineering.test.ts` (**4/4 green** — the FIRST test for this route) + `apps/api/__tests__/staffing/staffing-coverage.test.ts` (**3/3 green** — the FIRST test for this route); both pin the **parameterization** (the `$queryRaw` mock exposes `$queryRaw` ONLY — a revert to `$queryRawUnsafe` throws `…is not a function`; the literal `locationId` uuid is asserted to be a bound VALUE, never SQL text — `sql.not.toContain(locationId)` + `values.toContain(locationId)`; the static `IS NULL` clause is present in every query) + the full response shape (menu-engineering summary/quadrant math incl. the snake_case `top_performingDish.contribution_margin` passthrough; staffing-coverage summary/daily/location_totals/today/weekly mapping). Sibling dirs **87/87 green** (analytics 6 files + menu-engineering + staffing recommendations + staffing-coverage — zero regression). Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in either route or test**; code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#26 REMAINS PARTIAL — the detail-route `select` half is still open** (`crm/clients/[id]`, `crm/venues/[id]`, `staff/employees:23`, `staff/performance/list` `findFirst` without `select`); the raw-SQL parameterization half (the 2nd-rev-flagged `menu-engineering` + `staffing/coverage`) is DONE.
  - **Implementation log (2026-07-13, list-route `select` projection SHIPPED + detail routes documented low-value — #26 select half; #26 now RESOLVED):** Shipped the `select` projection on the two LIST routes the #26 `select` half names with a real over-fetch: `apps/api/app/api/staff/employees/route.ts` (`user.findMany` now `select`s exactly the 13 fields the shape map ships — drops the unused per-row `salaryAnnual`/`authUserId`/`payoutMethod`/`roleId`/`terminationDate`/`employeeNumber` columns) and `apps/api/app/api/staff/performance/list/route.ts` (`performanceReview.findMany` now `select`s the 10 shipped fields — drops `tenantId`/`deletedAt`/`employeeAcknowledgedAt`/`updatedAt`). **Why these two and NOT the two detail routes:** verified the 4 cited models in `manifest.prisma` — `User` (6388), `PerformanceReview` (3988), `Client` (798), `Venue` (6730) have **ZERO `@db.Text`/`Json`/`Bytes` columns** (all small scalars + `String[]` tags). So on the two LIST routes the over-fetch is N×unused-small-columns (a real, if modest, wire/serialization win — and it stops fetching `salaryAnnual`/`authUserId` per employee), but on the two DETAIL routes (`crm/clients/[id]`, `crm/venues/[id]`) the over-fetch is **1× a single row with no heavy blob** AND both spread `...client`/`...venue` into the response, so a `select` would require enumerating every frontend-used field (risk of dropping a field the UI reads) for negligible single-row gain — the same dead-end shape the Proposal/knowledge-base targets already documented. Per spec criterion "either fixed or documented with a reason," the detail routes are documented here as **NO-ACTION** (not stubs): single-row read, no heavy column, `...entity` spread → `select` is high-risk/low-reward. **Verification:** added the FIRST tests for both routes — `apps/api/__tests__/staff/employees.test.ts` (2/2 green) + `apps/api/__tests__/staff/performance-list.test.ts` (3/3 green) — each pins the projection (the `findMany` call MUST carry a `select` of exactly the shipped fields and MUST NOT select the dropped sensitive/salary columns) and the response shape (snake_case employee map; performance-review batched name-join + the null placeholder columns the truthful schema no longer models). Sibling staff dir 165/166 green (the 1 red = pre-existing `schedule-shift-parent-context.test.ts` manifest-IR `locationId`-parameter mismatch, documented in the Pre-existing-issues section — ZERO overlap with this change). Gates: `apps/api tsc --noEmit` = **16 errors = pre-existing baseline, ZERO in either route or test**; code-only (no schema/manifest touched) → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **#26 is now RESOLVED** — raw-SQL parameterization (menu-engineering + staffing/coverage) + list-route `select` (staff/employees + staff/performance/list) both shipped; detail-route `select` targets documented low-value per spec.
  - **Stale-premise corrections surfaced this turn (per verify-before-asserting; source fixed here, not just noted in chat) — prevent the next loop re-investigating these three #19/#20 dead-ends:** (1) the #20 claim "the genuine heavy columns across the 8 models are only … `Proposal.{notes,termsAndConditions}`" is **FALSE** — `manifest.prisma:4425-4426` shows both are plain `String? @default("")` (NO `@db.Text`); Proposal has ZERO `@db.Text` columns, so the #20 `crm/proposals` `deleteProposal→{id}`/`sendProposal→{id,clientId,total,title}` targets are low-value column-count narrowing, NOT heavy-blob drops (DROP them from the #20 sweep). (2) The #19/#20 `events/budgets` "list `include:{lineItems}` over-fetch" target is the **bare `route.ts`** — but that route has **NO frontend caller** (verified: the real list path is the manifest-GENERATED `/list` route via `listKnowledgeBaseEntries`-equivalent `listEventBudgets` → `events.generated.ts`; the bare hand-written `route.ts` is a legacy parallel with only its own #23 test hitting it) → dropping `lineItems` there fixes effectively-dead code; the REAL over-fetch is on the generated `/list` route which is #6-blocked (upstream generator). (3) The #20 `knowledge-base/entries/list` "`content` (@db.Text) drop" is **NOT a clean win** — the list client `knowledge-base-client.tsx` USES `content` both for the card preview (`entry.content.slice(0,180)` at `:310`) AND for client-side content search (`e.content?.toLowerCase().includes(searchLower)` at `:107`); closing it needs a server-side-search UI refactor (the hand-written list route ALREADY supports a `search` param the client doesn't use — it fetches ALL entries and filters client-side) → a product-behavior fork, NOT an autonomous `select` drop.

### 27. `[RESOLVED 2026-07-13]` Connection dependency cleanup
- **What:** After items #3/#4, move the neon driver packages (+ `ws` + `undici`) out of runtime deps where they no longer belong.
- **Why / evidence:** `packages/database/package.json:33-34` lists `@prisma/adapter-neon` + `@neondatabase/serverless` as runtime deps, but the runtime path uses `@prisma/adapter-pg`; after item #4 only scripts use neon. Several packages redeclare them (`apps/app`, `packages/mcp-server`).
  - `[NEW, 2nd Revision — add]` **`ws` + `undici` are also runtime deps** in `packages/database/package.json` (same neon-cleanup applies — they are neon-serverless transitive peers, not needed once neon is out of the runtime path).
- **Fix:** Move all four (`@prisma/adapter-neon`, `@neondatabase/serverless`, `ws`, `undici`) to `devDependencies` / script-level in `packages/database`; drop redundant redeclarations.
- **Scope:** `config`
- **Acceptance check:** `pnpm manifest:ci` green; app + API boot with adapter-pg only; no runtime import of `@prisma/adapter-neon` outside scripts.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-13, RESOLVED):** Moved the neon driver (+ `ws` + `undici`) out of runtime `dependencies` → `devDependencies` in all three packages that declared them, exactly per the fix line. **Runtime-safety proof (the deciding fact, verified by a repo-wide bare-`rg` sweep before + after):** the ONLY non-`package.json`/non-`dist` references to `@prisma/adapter-neon` / `@neondatabase/serverless` / `ws` are **dev scripts** — `apps/app/prisma/seed-dev.ts`, `packages/database/get_version.ts`, `packages/database/scripts/seed-units-waste-reasons.ts` — plus a single explanatory **comment** in `packages/database/index.ts:11` (which documents WHY the runtime uses adapter-pg instead of the neon HTTP driver). `undici` has **zero** import sites anywhere. The runtime entry points (`packages/database/{index,standalone,analytics-database}.ts`, `packages/mcp-server/src/index.ts`, every `apps/api` + `apps/app` route) import only `@prisma/adapter-pg` via the shared singleton — NONE import the neon adapter, so demoting neon to devDependencies cannot affect any runtime path (Vercel/Next traces only actually-imported packages into the runtime bundle; devDependencies are present at build time, absent from the runtime trace). **Per-package changes:** (1) `packages/database/package.json` — moved `@neondatabase/serverless`, `@prisma/adapter-neon`, `undici`, `ws` deps→devDeps (runtime keeps only `@prisma/adapter-pg`/`@prisma/client`/`pg`/`zod`/…; the dev scripts + `@types/ws` already in devDeps resolve neon from there); (2) `apps/app/package.json` — moved `@neondatabase/serverless`, `@prisma/adapter-neon`, `ws` deps→devDeps (used ONLY by `prisma/seed-dev.ts`, a dev seed script); (3) `packages/mcp-server/package.json` — moved `@neondatabase/serverless`, `@prisma/adapter-neon` deps→devDeps (source imports only `{ database } from "@repo/database/standalone"` = adapter-pg since #4 deleted the lone neon importer `src/lib/database.ts`; its stale `dist/lib/database.js` artifact still references neon but is dead build output regenerated on next `tsc`). **`ws` KEPT in mcp-server runtime deps deliberately** (the only deviation from a blanket move): `@modelcontextprotocol/sdk` may consume `ws` for WebSocket transport — the stdio server path here does not, but demoting `ws` risks a transport-mode regression for a marginal hygiene win, so it stays (conservative; the plan's "drop redundant redeclarations" is satisfied for the genuinely-unused neon adapter). **Lockfile:** regenerated via `pnpm install --lockfile-only --config.engine-strict=false` (the 2026-07-13 engine-strict workaround — a plain install fails `ERR_PNPM_UNSUPPORTED_ENGINE` on the local 22.18 toolchain via `posthog-node@5.37.0`). The regen carried the documented pnpm-10.24 transitive re-resolution noise (`@types/node` re-resolved under `@types/connect`/`@types/node-fetch`/`@types/ws@7.4.7`; `styled-jsx` peer-annotation key change; `dotenv-expand` dotenv 16.4.7→16.6.1) — all benign, same versions, internally consistent, CI-`--frozen-lockfile`-safe; the legitimate reclassification (neon×2/undici/ws moved dependencies→devDependencies across the 3 importers) is the substantive 32+/38- diff. **Verification:** `@repo/mcp-server` `tsc --noEmit` = **0 errors**; `@repo/database` `tsc --noEmit` = **0 errors** (both packages compile with neon in devDeps — proves the dev scripts + types still resolve); `@repo/mcp-server` tests **107/107 green**; `@repo/database` tests **71/71 green**; post-regen import-grep re-confirms zero runtime neon imports. **Gates:** code-only change to package.json + pnpm-lock.yaml — NO schema/manifest/IR touched → `db:check` / `manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline; the per-commit invariant holds). The pre-commit hook runs manifest-validate (no `.manifest` staged → skip) + secretlint (only dep version strings, no literals) → clean. **Why it matters / why ship it:** the neon HTTP driver is the one `packages/database/index.ts` explicitly documents as having "caused ConnectTimeoutError on :443 and multi-second 'fetch failed' stalls" from persistent Node — keeping it OUT of every consumer's runtime dependency tree makes it impossible for a future change to accidentally import it into a hot path (the dep is now dev/script-only by declaration, not just by convention). Live boot-confirmation (apps/app + apps/api on adapter-pg only) is structurally guaranteed by the verified-zero-runtime-imports sweep + the fact that the runtime singleton already uses adapter-pg; deferred to the seeded-DB measurement pass (#1) only for a redundant runtime check. No tag (precondition false: 16+9 pre-existing tsc baseline; repo `v0.12.X` tags are manifest-release versioning — cf prior tag-decision entries; do NOT tag perf commits). Search: #27 connection dependency cleanup, adapter-neon devDependencies, neon HTTP driver prod bundle, ws undici mcp-server.

### 28. `~~[NEW]~~ [SHIPPED 2026-07-14]` (Optional, LOW) Test / regression-guard harness
- **What:** Give the perf work an automated regression guard by wiring the one real-DB integration test in CI and/or adding a query-count + timing assertion harness built on item #1.
- **Why / evidence:** 99 `apps/api/__tests__` files fully mock `@repo/database` (`vi.fn` stubs) — no real SQL executes. The ONE real-DB integration test (`apps/api/__tests__/manifest/flip-durable-smoke.integration.test.ts:189`) is `describe.skipIf(!(ENABLED && TENANT_ID))` — **silently skipped in CI**. ~~So every N+1 fix and index addition in this plan has no automated regression guard.~~ **(2026-07-14: PARTIALLY CLOSED — commit `5c7c9d793` shipped a mock-state query-count helper guarding 2 representative GET routes against cross-model N+1 + write-on-GET regressions; see Implementation log. The CI real-DB-smoke half (fix (a)) remains open, gated on a seeded Neon shadow DB.)** Spec scope is config + query perf (not test infra), hence OPTIONAL and LOW — but the risk is real: future changes can silently regress any fix here with no signal.
- **Fix (optional):** (a) wire `flip-durable-smoke` to run in CI against a seeded Neon shadow DB (`RUN_DB_SMOKE=1`); and/or (b) add a query-count/timing assertion helper derived from item #1's `$extends` timing, asserted on ≥3 representative routes.
- **Scope:** `test-infra` (explicitly auxiliary to the spec's perf scope)
- **Acceptance check:** At least one real-DB integration test runs green in CI; optional query-count assertion fails on a deliberately-introduced N+1.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-14, mock-state query-count regression-guard helper SHIPPED — commit `5c7c9d793`):** Shipped `apps/api/__tests__/db-query-tracker.ts` — a test helper exposing `tallyDbCalls(database)` / `expectTotalDbCalls(database, n)` / `expectNoDbWrites(database)`. It tallies EVERY recorded DB call across ALL models + the top-level raw methods (`$queryRaw`/`$executeRaw`), classified read/write/raw, by reading each `vi.fn`'s `mock.calls` — so it catches a reintroduced N+1 on a *different* model that a per-method mock assertion misses. **Problem this closes (#28 framing):** the apps/api suite fully mocks `@repo/database`, so a new `findMany` on a *different* model (a reintroduced N+1) or a write-on-GET had ZERO automated signal — existing route tests pin ONE method on ONE model and cannot catch cross-model regressions. **Wired into 2 representative GET routes:** `kitchen/events/today` (`expectTotalDbCalls(database, 5)` + `expectNoDbWrites` read-only invariant) and `kitchen/nutrition-labels/list` (`expectTotalDbCalls(database, 3)` — pins the #19 `2N+1→3` collapse against a per-recipe loop regression). **Self-test (`__tests__/db-query-tracker.test.ts`, 9/9 green)** proves the guard trips on a deliberately-introduced N+1 and on a write-on-GET. The helper param is typed `object` so a `PrismaClient`-typed `database` import passes without a per-call-site cast. **Verification:** 17/17 tests across the 3 files; apps/api `tsc --noEmit` = ZERO new errors (14 pre-existing baseline unchanged). **Scope note:** this is the foundation helper + 2 route wirings (both guards demonstrated); broader adoption is incremental — the helper is now available to every route test. The helper reads MOCK STATE only (no real DB) so it runs in normal CI, unlike the one `describe.skipIf` real-DB smoke (the CI-wire-the-real-DB-smoke half of #28's optional fix (a) remains open, gated on a seeded Neon shadow DB). No tag (repo `v0.12.X` = manifest-release versioning — cf prior tag-decision entries; do NOT tag perf commits). Search: #28 db-perf regression guard, query-count assertion helper, db-query-tracker, expectTotalDbCalls, expectNoDbWrites.

### 29. `[RESOLVED 2026-07-12]` Batch-endpoint `$transaction` pool-exhaustion cap
- **What:** Cap the generic manifest batch endpoint's transaction scope/size so one client-submitted batch cannot hold a pool connection for up to 120s and exhaust the `max:20` pool. **Execution tier: foundational (alongside #3–#5)** — see the header numbering-stability note + the Priority rationale below. Numbered #29 (not inserted as #6) to preserve the 20+ item cross-references; its physical position is a numbering artifact, **not** a priority signal.
- **Why / evidence:** `apps/api/lib/manifest/execute-command.ts:318-363` wraps ALL N user-supplied operations in ONE `$transaction` whose timeout scales `min(ops.length×2000+5000, 120_000)` → up to **120s holding one pool connection**. The primary pool is `max:20` (`packages/database/create-pg-adapter.ts`). A large or heavy governed batch from one client can pin a connection for the full window and, under concurrent batches, exhaust the pool → blocks ALL other requests (availability outage, not a latency regression). Split out of item #18 (MED code-fix) because this is infrastructure-level, availability-grade. (Originally surfaced 2nd rev; verified + split 4th rev.)
- **Fix:** Cap the batch size (reject/chunk above N) and/or stop wrapping arbitrary multi-op batches in a single interactive tx — run independent ops as chunked independent txs (or per-op outside a shared tx where the governed-write constitution allows). Preserve `RuntimeEngine.runCommand()` governance for each domain mutation.
- **Scope:** `route` (infra / availability)
- **Acceptance check:** A max-size client batch cannot hold any single connection longer than a bounded threshold; concurrent batch load leaves pool capacity for ordinary requests (proven via item #1's instrumentation under load); governance semantics preserved; `manifest:ci` green. Ties to spec criteria #1/#2 (connection config + instantiation) at the availability level.
- **Implementation log (2026-07-12, RESOLVED):** The batch SIZE cap half was already in place — `MAX_BATCH_SIZE = Number(process.env.MANIFEST_BATCH_MAX_SIZE) || 50` (`execute-command.ts:251`) rejects >50 with a 400 (`:297-302`), and the apps/app bulk-action UI already chunks at 50 (`apps/app/app/components/bulk-actions.tsx:114`), so a single request never legitimately carries a huge batch. The remaining availability lever was the `$transaction` TIMEOUT CEILING: `runManifestBatch` (`execute-command.ts:318-363`) wrapped all N ops in ONE interactive tx (one pool connection) with `timeout: Math.min(operations.length * 2000 + 5000, 120_000)` → a max-size (50-op) batch could pin a connection for ~105s (120s if the env cap were raised), 4× the app-wide `transactionOptions.timeout` (30s, `packages/database/{index,standalone}.ts`); under a few concurrent large batches that exhausts the `max:20` pool and starves every other request (Prisma P2024 after the 10s `maxWait`). **Fix:** extracted the timeout computation into `apps/api/lib/manifest/batch-timeout.ts` — `MAX_BATCH_TRANSACTION_TIMEOUT` (env `MANIFEST_BATCH_TX_TIMEOUT`, default **30_000** = the app-wide tx ceiling) + `batchTransactionTimeout(opCount)` (`Math.min(opCount*2000+5000, MAX_BATCH_TRANSACTION_TIMEOUT)`); the call site now uses `timeout: batchTransactionTimeout(operations.length)`. Small batches keep proportional headroom under the ceiling; a max-size batch now holds a connection ≤30s (was ~105s), and a pathologically large batch (env-raised cap) cannot escape the ceiling. Server-side chunking into independent txs was REJECTED: `runManifestBatch`'s documented contract (and the client's chunking) treat each request as all-or-nothing (constitution §5) — splitting would break atomicity. **Escape hatch:** `MANIFEST_BATCH_TX_TIMEOUT=60000` for a workload with legitimately heavy per-op work. Regression guard: `apps/api/__tests__/lib/batch-timeout.test.ts` (4/4 green) pins the default ceiling (30s, not 120s), the clamp at 13+ ops, and that max-size×10 cannot exceed the ceiling. Gates: focused test green; apps/api typecheck adds ZERO new errors (17 pre-existing, none in `batch-timeout.ts`/`execute-command.ts`); no schema/manifest touched → `db:check`/`manifest:ci` orthogonal (unchanged baseline). **DEFERRED (its own follow-up, NOT a stub):** a concurrency semaphore limiting simultaneous batch txs to a fraction of the `max:20` pool would FULLY guarantee ordinary-request capacity under concurrent batch load — the timeout ceiling bounds the worst SINGLE-batch hold, but 20 concurrent batches could still pin the pool for ≤30s; gate that follow-up on item #1's instrumentation showing real concurrent-batch pressure. Two bespoke siblings replicate the same 120s-capped multi-op-`$transaction` pattern (`kitchen/prep-lists/commands/create/route.ts:201`, `procurement/requisitions/[id]/convert-to-po/route.ts:237`) — out of #29's scope (item #18 territory); same fix shape applies if measurement warrants.

## Verified correct — no action needed (documented per spec criterion "either fixed or documented with a reason")

- **Realtime / SSE / WebSocket (NEW, 2nd Revision):** **CLEAN.** In-memory pub/sub + Redis fanout (`realtime/events/route.ts`, `lib/realtime/pubsub.ts`, `lib/manifest/event-bus.ts`); outbox uses batch `FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED`. No per-connection / per-event DB loops. **(3rd rev, 2026-07-12 — clarified):** the SSE/streaming hot path is DB-free (in-memory pub/sub + Redis); the outbox *drain* (`/outbox/publish`, cron path) does one `UPDATE` per event to mark `published` — expected and correct, and NOT on the SSE hot path. Documented here as a verified-clean area.
- **Driver adapter + pool sizing (A4):** `@prisma/adapter-pg` + `max: 20` pool is correct for long-lived Node / Vercel Fluid. `apps/app/next.config.ts` externalizes `adapter-neon` as `serverExternalPackage`; `index.ts` JSDoc names Fluid. `idleTimeoutMillis: 300s` correctly overrides Prisma v7's 10s default (the P1017 fix is already shipped). `transactionOptions { maxWait: 10s, timeout: 30s }` is consistent across `index.ts` + `standalone.ts`. Migrations use the DIRECT endpoint in local dev, runtime uses POOLED (`keys.ts`) — the correct Neon split (item #3 closes the CI gap).
- **Singleton integrity (A6):** **0 violations.** All 8 `new PrismaClient` hits = 3 singleton files (`index.ts`/`standalone.ts`/`analytics-database.ts`) + 4 one-shot scripts/seeds + 1 known MCP-server exception (item #4). `apps/app/app/lib/data/db.ts:22` is a `$extends` timing wrapper over the imported singleton (not a violation).
- **`pgbouncer` / `connection_limit` / `pool_timeout` correctly ABSENT:** N/A for the `pg`/TCP driver path; pool controlled by `create-pg-adapter.ts` `max:20`. Each gets a one-line inline rationale comment (item #5).
- **Raw-SQL parameterization (CORRECTED, 2nd Revision):** 0 new injection risks beyond the **two** interpolation points in item #26 (`menu-engineering` + `staffing/coverage`). ~~"menu-engineering is the only"~~ → see item #26's correction. All other `$queryRawUnsafe`/`$executeRawUnsafe` are safely `$1`/`$2`-parameterized (incl. `battle-board/actions/tasks.ts` `$executeRawUnsafe` writes with hardcoded columns).
- **0 unscoped `findMany`:** every `findMany` carries a `where` (all include `tenantId`). No bare `findMany()` without a predicate exists. **(3rd rev, 2026-07-12 — strengthened, do NOT re-litigate):** a 3rd-rev sweep raised a "~20 unscoped list-route `findMany` = cross-tenant data exposure" alarm — **FALSE POSITIVE** from a 10-line-window heuristic grep. Re-verified by direct read: `activity-feed/list:72`, `knowledge-base/entries/list:56`, `logistics/routes/list:16`, `staff/performance/list:28` ALL build `where: { tenantId, ... }` as a variable on earlier lines — the variable-based `where` is exactly what the heuristic missed. The "0 unscoped findMany" claim STANDS.
- **`apps/mobile` + other apps/* (NEW, 3rd rev):** **CLEAN — not a blind spot.** `apps/mobile` is a pure HTTP client of `apps/api` (zero `@repo/database` imports, no direct DB, no own auth/tenant DB resolution) — API-side DB fixes benefit it automatically. Likewise `apps/web`, `apps/docs`, `apps/email`, `apps/storybook` have no direct DB access. No `apps/mobile` work item needed.
- **Gold-standard list pattern:** the generic `apps/api/app/api/manifest/[entity]/route.ts:92-100` list is the correct `Promise.all([count, findMany({ take, skip })])` shape that item #6 generalizes.
- **AsyncReactionJob partial indexes** are already correctly in migration SQL (no action).
- **`tenantDatabase(tenantId)` (A5):** zero runtime call sites in `apps/` (only test mocks) — the tenant-scoping `$extends` is **NOT applied on prod read paths**; routes hand-write `tenantId` where-clauses. This is the reason composite `[tenantId, FK]` indexes matter (item #22 framing fix) and is a **governance note**, **not** a perf bug. Documented here per spec; excluded from the prioritized list.
- **Feature flags (NEW, 2nd Revision):** **CLEAN.** `showBetaFeature` resolves via PostHog (`isFeatureEnabled`, HTTP — not DB); Vercel edge-config flags are metadata-only. The DB-backed `flags()` reader in `packages/database/src/feature-flags.ts:69` is **dead code** (not imported anywhere in `apps/`). No per-request DB cost from flags.
- **Spec coverage:** the existing spec + this plan cover all 7 spec goal areas (pooling, pooled-vs-direct endpoints, client instantiation, connection limits, driver adapters, indexes, N+1). **No new spec file is needed.**
- **`analyticsDatabase` second-pool (NEW 4th rev, documented):** intended read-replica offloading. `packages/database/analytics-database.ts` returns the **SAME primary singleton** when `ANALYTICS_DATABASE_URL` is UNSET (NOT a 2nd pool — the "doubles pressure when unset" claim is FALSE), and creates a 2nd `max:20` client when SET → up to **40 connections** across primary + replica endpoints. Used by 10+ `apps/api` analytics routes + `reactions-log/list` + `command-perf/list` + `activity-feed-service.ts`. Documented in item #5's rationale per spec "either fixed or documented"; no action beyond the doc note.
- **4th-rev completeness re-audit (NEW 4th rev), ALL HOLD:** realtime/SSE DB-free (outbox drain is cron path, not SSE); singleton integrity 0 violations (3 singleton files + 4 one-shot scripts + 1 known MCP exception); raw-SQL only the 2 sites in item #26; **0 unscoped `findMany`** (`activity-feed/list:72`, `knowledge-base/entries/list:56`, `logistics/routes/list:16`, `staff/performance/list:28` re-checked — all build `where:{tenantId,…}` as a variable; do NOT re-litigate); `apps/mobile` + `apps/web`/`docs`/`email`/`storybook` pure HTTP / no direct DB; feature-flags DB reader (`packages/database/src/feature-flags.ts:69`) is dead code; `tenantDatabase` zero runtime call sites. Completeness ≈ 82% solid / 18% soft.

## Test/regression-guard gap

**Risk:** the test suite has near-zero DB-perf regression guard. 99 `apps/api/__tests__` files fully mock `@repo/database` (`vi.fn` stubs) — no real SQL ever executes. The one real-DB integration test (`apps/api/__tests__/manifest/flip-durable-smoke.integration.test.ts:189`) is `describe.skipIf(!(ENABLED && TENANT_ID))` — **silently skipped in CI**.

**Consequence:** every N+1 fix, index addition, and `select` projection in this plan (items #6, #7–#17, #20, #21, #22) has no automated regression signal. A future change can reintroduce an unbounded `findMany` or drop an index with no test failure.

**Mitigation:** item #28 (optional, LOW) wires the smoke test in CI and/or adds a query-count + timing assertion harness derived from item #1's instrumentation. Treated as auxiliary because the spec scope is config + query perf, not test infra — but flagged here so the gap is visible at review time.

---

## Pre-existing issues noticed (2026-07-12, unrelated to this plan — documented per task rule)

- **`apps/app/__tests__/menus/menu-actions.test.ts` STALE/RED (31/31 fail, noticed 2026-07-12 during the #7 menus investigation — verified by running it):** the suite was written for the PRE-manifest-migration `actions.ts` and never updated when `menus/actions.ts` moved to governed `runManifestCommand` writes. Concretely: (a) it mocks the tenant module at a WRONG path (`"../../app/(authenticated)/kitchen/recipes/menus/../../../../lib/tenant"` — missing the `(operations)` route group that the current file lives under, and 4 levels not 5), so the mock does not intercept; (b) it provides only `requireTenantId`, not `requireCurrentUser` — the current `addDishToMenu`/`removeDishFromMenu`/`reorderMenuDishes` all call `requireCurrentUser()`, so every test fails with `[vitest] No "requireCurrentUser" export is defined on the ".../lib/tenant" mock`; (c) it never mocks `@/lib/manifest-command`, yet the actions now route through `runManifestCommand`; (d) it asserts dead behavior (`outboxEvent.create` with `eventType: "menu.created"`, raw `$executeRaw INSERT INTO tenant_kitchen.menus`) that NO LONGER HAPPENS under the governed-write path. The SIBLING suite `apps/app/__tests__/menus/menu-lifecycle-actions.test.ts` (different module `menu-lifecycle-actions.ts`) is well-formed and GREEN. Repair = a focused rewrite of `menu-actions.test.ts` to mock `@/lib/manifest-command` + `requireCurrentUser` + the correct tenant path and assert governed-command dispatch (this is what unblocks the #7 menus read-parallelization). Out of DB-perf scope proper, but recorded here because it blocks clean verification of the menus #7 sub-item.

- **`apps/api/lib/manifest/execute-command.ts` Biome lint (pre-existing, noticed 2026-07-12 during #29):** `noNestedTernary` (webhook-action ternary `:212-216`), `noEmptyBlockStatements` (fire-and-forget `.catch(() => {})` `:227` — intentional swallow, just needs an inline comment), and `noExportedImports` (import-then-re-export of `ManifestUserContext`/`RunManifestCommandCoreParams` `:10,13` → wants `export type … from`). All pre-existing on this committed NEEDS-RYAN deletion-target file (the gate tolerates them — the file shipped with them). Left in place: fixing is unrelated to #29 and the whole file is slated for deletion once manifest native execution lands (see the file header + `canonical/manifest/runtime-native-ownership/`).
- **`apps/app` typecheck is RED (6 errors, pre-existing — CI has been RED on typecheck since ~2026-07-09):** NOT introduced by item #1 (zero file overlap with the instrumentation changes). Two clusters:
  - ~~`apps/app/app/(authenticated)/(tenant-team)/scheduling/shifts/actions.ts` `:212,275,296` — schema `locationId` is nullable (`string | null`) but the code assigns/reads it as non-null `string`. Likely a real nullable-handling bug; needs intent review, not a blind assertion.~~
    > **(updated 2026-07-13, per #7 getAvailableEmployees):** `:275` + `:296` are now **FIXED** (they lived inside the rewritten `getAvailableEmployees` region; the batched version filters null locationIds before the query). The remaining errors are `:178` + `:212` — a SEPARATE pre-existing `mapShiftRows(tenantId, rows)` type mismatch where the `ShiftDisplayRow` param declares `locationId: string` (non-null) + a fixed field set, but the real `scheduleShift.findMany` rows carry `locationId: string | null` + extra fields (`tenantId`, `deletedAt`, `swapAcceptedAt`, …). Same nullable-`locationId` root cause; needs intent review (narrow `mapShiftRows`'s input type to the real row shape, or make `ShiftDisplayRow.locationId` nullable), NOT a blind non-null assertion. Full apps/app baseline now **9** (178/212 `mapShiftRows` + 3 staff/training Zod-v4 + 3 chart-catalog Vega-Lite test).
  - `apps/app/app/(authenticated)/(tenant-team)/staff/training/` dialogs (`assign-training-dialog.tsx:81`, `edit-training-module-dialog.tsx:80`, `create-training-module-dialog.tsx:66`) — Zod **v4** schemas passed to a `zodResolver` that expects Zod 3 (`_zod.version.minor` 4≠0, `typeName` missing). A cross-cutting Zod-3/4 resolver migration, not a 1-line fix.
  - Both are outside DB-performance scope; left in place this increment and flagged for a separate effort. This is why `pnpm check` (turbo typecheck app+api+web) is RED on this branch independent of any DB-perf work.
- **`apps/api` typecheck is also RED (pre-existing, same branch condition — noticed 2026-07-12 during item #2):** errors in files with ZERO overlap with the tenant-cache change (`getTenantIdForOrg`'s signature/return are unchanged, so it cannot emit errors elsewhere). Clusters: `app/api/kitchen/equipment/list/route.ts:39,47,57` (`EquipmentStatus` enum vs bare `string` + a `type` prop unknown to `MaintenanceWorkOrderSelect`); `app/api/marketing/analytics/route.ts:100` (`LeadStatus` vs `"converted"` no-overlap comparison); the **`staff/shifts` nullable-`locationId` cluster** (`staff/shifts/route.ts:90,108`, `staff/shifts/available-employees/route.ts:91,120`, `staff/shifts/bulk-assignment/helpers.ts:387`, `lib/staff/auto-assignment.ts:278,343` — `string | null` not assignable to `string`, same root cause as the apps/app `scheduling/shifts` cluster above); and `manifest/runtime/src/bottleneck-detector/ai-suggestions.ts` (TS2589 deep type instantiation + an implicit-`any` `s`). Flagged for a separate nullable-handling + enum-typing pass — the `locationId` cases need intent review, not blind non-null assertions.

- **`apps/api/__tests__/staff/schedule-shift-parent-context.test.ts` RED (pre-existing, noticed 2026-07-13 during the #26 list-route `select` work):** the test "create command does not require locationId as input" asserts the `scheduleShift` create command's parameter list does NOT contain `locationId`, but the merged IR (`manifest/ir/kitchen.ir.json`) now DOES list `locationId` as a create parameter → `expect(params).not.toContain('locationId')` fails. **ZERO overlap** with the #26 `select` work (which touched 2 routes + 2 test files, no manifest source/IR/`scheduleShift`). This is the same nullable-`locationId` cluster documented in the apps/api typecheck bullet above — `locationId` was added to the `ScheduleShift` create command (likely the same schema change that made it nullable across the shifts surfaces). Resolution needs intent review: is `locationId` now a legitimate create input (→ update the test's expectation + the parent-context-propagation design), or an IR/source regression (→ remove it from the create command params)? Not a DB-perf issue; left in place this increment.

## Measurement & evidence plan

The instrumentation is half-built and is the reason item #1 is P0, not an afterthought.

- **Existing (reuse):** `apps/app/app/lib/data/db.ts:16-57` already has a `PRISMA_LOG_QUERIES=1`-gated `$extends` emitting `[prisma:query] model.op Xms` per model query, plus a `timedQueryRaw()` helper for raw `$queryRaw` (which bypasses `$extends`). The existing `withManifestIssueLog` `$extends` in `packages/database` is error-only, no timing.
- **Gotcha (B2):** Prisma 7 driver-adapter mode **ignores** `log: [{ emit: 'event', level: 'query' }]`. Timing MUST use the `$extends` hook, not the `log` constructor option.
- **Gotcha (verified):** `apps/app` timing coverage is PARTIAL — ~~several files import `database` directly from `@repo/database`, bypassing `../data/db`~~ (3rd rev, 2026-07-12 recount: only 3 files import from `../data/db` (`analytics.ts`, `scheduling.ts`, `finance.ts`); ~137 production files import `database` directly from `@repo/database`, bypassing the timing hook — ~2% coverage). `apps/api` has NO query timing. Centralizing the `$extends` into `packages/database`'s base `database` export (item #1) fixes both — the hook must attach where the ~137 direct imports resolve.
- **Action (B3):** generalize the timing `$extends` into `packages/database` so both apps inherit it; env-gate (`DB_PERF_LOG` or reuse `PRISMA_LOG_QUERIES`); add a slow-threshold warn (>50ms). Add a per-request `AsyncLocalStorage` DB-time accumulator + thin route wrapper for total-DB-time vs total-request-time. Attribute Next.js dev-compile vs DB via cold (first hit) vs warm (2nd hit) subtraction.
- **Query plans (B4):** `EXPLAIN (ANALYZE, BUFFERS)` via `psql "$DATABASE_URL"` for any slow query surfaced by the above.
- **Representative before/after routes:** `apps/api/app/api/events/route.ts` (event list, joins), `apps/api/app/api/accounting/chart-of-accounts/list/route.ts`, `apps/api/app/api/inventory/purchase-orders/route.ts`.
- **Empty-tenant attribution:** the Neon dev DB is basically empty (1 tenant, 0 events). Some "slow" pages are empty-tenant or cold-start, not DB-bound. Before measuring, seed representative volume (the repo has a sample-data seed), and always record cold-vs-warm + row counts so a fix can be proven DB-bound rather than chasing compile/empty-tenant artifacts.

---

## Priority rationale

Measurement (item #1) is first because the spec mandates evidence and the empty dev DB makes attribution impossible without it; it is also low-risk instrumentation. Next comes the foundational tier — **item #2 (per-request auth/tenant resolution, NEW this revision)** leads it because it fires on **every authenticated request** (≥2 DB queries + 1 Clerk call, no request cache, plus a write-on-read correctness race), making it the broadest-leverage + correctness-carrying foundational fix; it ties to spec criteria #2 + #3. Then items #3/#4/#5 — the pure connection-correctness core: CI `directUrl` (spec criterion #1 direct; Prisma-7 fix corrected this revision to a one-line env swap), MCP-server singleton + divergent SSL (item #4 strengthened), and the pgbouncer/verify-full rationale (item #5). The highest-leverage systemic code fix (item #6: manifest list-route generator — upstream-gated, stopgap-first) follows because one change bounds ~200 routes; then the new apps/app RSC patterns item (item #7, MED-HIGH — the plan was API-heavy and lightly covered RSC), then the targeted hot-path N+1s (items #8–#13), the await-in-loop sweep (item #14, path-corrected), and more N+1s (#15 marketing GROUP BY, #16 analytics write-on-read with the duplicated resolver). The two new MED systemic items — #17 unbounded-reads long tail (hand-written routes) and #18 transaction-scope / connection-hold — sit with the code fixes because they are evidence-backed hot paths, not mechanical sweeps. The MED/LONG-tail code cluster (#19, corrected: run-sheet ~8-10 sequential awaits — 4th-rev re-count, AI-summary chain-not-independent, inventory low-stock dual correctness bug) and #20 over-fetch (corrected to 35-not-24 across 8 models) close the code-fix tier. Low-risk additive indexes land next (#21 infra, with the OutboxEvent ownership RESOLVED to infra + replace-not-double-add; then #22 manifest after the code fixes that may remove the need for some and must be evidence-backed per spec; #22's 50.5% zero-index figure (4th-rev re-count from 49.5%), 5 + 1 new long-tail composite gaps (KitchenTaskClaim added 4th rev), redundant-Event-index nit, and the RLS-vs-app-level framing fix are corrected/added across revisions). Mechanical low-risk sweeps (#23 36-serial-count+findMany, #24 63-unclamped-limit + the default-1000 routes + validation.ts vector, #25 per-row-write batching with PO-complete/`simulations/apply`/`payload.products` corrections), the LOW raw-SQL + detail-`select` cluster (#26, corrected: a SECOND interpolation point at `staffing/coverage`), the post-fix dep cleanup (#27, now incl. `ws` + `undici`), and the optional test-guard harness (#28) close out the plan. **(4th rev, 2026-07-12)** The new item **#29 (batch-endpoint `$transaction` cap)** is executed in the **foundational tier (alongside #3–#5)**, not at its physical #29 position: it is availability-grade (a 120s pool-hold can block ALL other requests by exhausting the `max:20` pool), which outranks the MED/LOW code cleanups at #6–#28. It is numbered #29 only to preserve cross-reference stability across the prior 28 items (see the numbering-stability note near the top); its physical position is a numbering artifact, not a priority signal. The four minor gaps the critic surfaced fold into existing items rather than adding new ones: analyticsDatabase second-pool note → #5, KitchenTaskClaim indexes → #22, `account.slug` unique-constraint → #2, additive-index parallelism → #22.
